Diyat for Loss of Senses and Speech: Full Compensation and Proof Methods
Rulings and proofs for diyat on senses, speech, and genitals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyat for loss of each sense and speech, identify the dalil, and explain the accepted methods of proof.

Core Idea
Each sense is an independent benefit; loss of one requires full diya, and objective tests verify the loss.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq with commentary from Ayni and Fath establishes that full diya is due for the loss of any of the five senses, as well as the penis and glans, and for speech when the victim cannot pronounce most letters. The text also provides practical methods to prove such losses and addresses Abu Yusuf's objection that these losses are unverifiable.

Guided Path
1
List the faculties
Identify which organs and faculties the passage rules on: penis (ذكر), glans (حشفة), intellect (عقل), hearing (سمع), sight (بصر), smell (شم), taste (ذوق), and speech articulation (16 letters).
The beard is also mentioned but only if it does not regrow, which is a separate case.
2
State the ruling for each
For each sense and the penis/glans, full diya is obligatory. For speech: full diya if the victim cannot pronounce most letters; otherwise just arbitration (hukumat al-adl).
The text specifies that loss of the penis includes loss of intercourse, procreation, etc., justifying full diya.
3
Locate the proof (dalil)
The author cites a reported judgement: 'he awarded four diyas for a single blow that took intellect, speech, hearing, and sight.' This establishes that multiple diyas are payable for multiple faculties.
The report is zanni al-thubut but accepted as a basis for analogy.
4
Understand the Hanafi reasoning
Each sense is an independent intended benefit (manfa'ah maqsudah). The answer to the objection: death is loss of the whole, and faculties are dependent parts; when alive, each is independent, so separate diyas are due.
This distinguishes from homicide where only one diya applies.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf argued that loss of senses cannot be verified, so the assailant's denial is accepted unless he confesses or refuses an oath. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad) accept objective tests.
The mufta bihi is the majority view, supported by practical tests.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذكر والحشفة والعقل والسمع والبصر والشم والذوق واللحية إن لم تنبت، ستة عشر حرفا. وهي: التاء والثاء والجيم والدال والذال والراء والزاء والسين والشين والصاد والضاد والطاء والظاء واللام والنون والياء فما أصاب الفائت يلزمه، ولا مدخل للحروف الحلقية فيه، وهي الهمزة والهاء والعين والحاء والغين والخاء ولا الشفوية وهي: الباء والفاء والميم والواو، وقيل: إن قدر على أكثرها تحب حكومة عدل الحصول الإفهام مع الاختلال، وإن عجز عن الأداء الأكثر تحب كل الدية. (عيني، فتح) والذكر إلخ لفوات منفعة جمة من الوطء والإيلاد واستمساك البول ورميه ودفق الماء والإيلاج الذي هو طريق الإعلاق عادة وكذا في الحشفة الدية الكاملة؛ لأن الحشفة أصل في منفعة الإيلاج والدفق والقصبة كالتابع له عيني رد المحتار والعقل والسمع إلخ : أي ضرب رجلا، فذهب بالضرب عقله أو سمعه أو بصره أو شمه أو ذوقه، ففي كل واحد منها الدية الكاملة؛ لأن لكل واحد منها منفعة مقصودة، وقد روي قضى بأربع ديات في ضربة ذهب بها العقل والكلام والسمع والبصر، وقال أبو يوسف: لا يعرف الذهاب، والقول قول الجاني؛ لأنه منكر، ولا يلزمه شيء إلا إذا صدقه، أو نكل عن اليمين. وقيل: ذهاب البصر يعرفه الأطباء، فيكون قول رجلين عدلين حجة فيه، وقيل: يستقبل به الشمس مفتوح العين، فإن دمعت عينه علم أنها باقية، وإلا فلا، وقيل: يلقي بين يديه حية، فإن هرب منها علم أنها لم تذهب، وإلا فهي ذاهبة، ويعرف ذهاب الشم بالروائح الكريهة، والذوقِ باستغفاله بإطعامه نحو حنظل بعد حلو، والكلام بأن يغرز على لسان إبرة، فإن خرج منه دم أسود، فصادق، وإن أحمر، فلا أو تطلب غفلته ليسمع كلامه إذا لم يكن أحد، والسمع بأن يغافل ثم ينادى، فإن أجاب علم أنه لم يذهب وإلا فهو ذاهب. فإن قيل: كيف أوجبتم أربع ديات فيما إذا ضربه ضربة واحدة فذهب بها العقل والكلام والسمع والبصر مع أنها إذا أفضت إلى موته لم تجب إلا دية واحدة والموت أعظم في ذلك؟ قيل: الموت فوات الجملة، وهذه الأشياء تبع للجملة فيدخل التبع في المتبوع، فأما إذا لم يمت فكل واحد من هذه المعاني غير تابع للآخر فلم يدخل في أرشه. (ملتقطا من العيني والفتح)
The penis, glans, intellect, hearing, sight, smell, taste, and beard if it does not grow. Sixteen letters. They are: ت, ث, ج, د, ذ, ر, ز, س, ش, ص, ض, ط, ظ, ل, ن, ي. Whatever of the lost [letters] is affected is required, and there is no entry for throat letters: ء, ه, ع, ح, غ, خ, nor lip letters: ب, ف, م, و. And it is said: if he is able to [speak] most of them, a just arbitration is required for obtaining understanding with disorder, and if he is unable to perform most, the full diya is required. (Ayni, Fath) 'The penis etc.' due to loss of immense benefit from intercourse, procreation, retention of urine and its emission, ejection of fluid, and insertion which is the usual way of impregnation. Likewise in the glans, full diya, because the glans is the origin in the benefit of insertion and ejection, and the shaft is like its follower. (Ayni, Radd al-Muhtar) 'The intellect and hearing etc.': i.e., he struck a man and by the strike his intellect or hearing or sight or smell or taste went, so for each one of them is full diya, because for each there is a intended benefit. And it has been reported that he (Umar?) judged four diyas in a strike which took intellect, speech, hearing, and sight. Abu Yusuf said: the going [of these] is not known, and the statement is the statement of the assailant because he is a denier, and nothing is required from him unless he confirms or refuses the oath. And it is said: the loss of sight is known by doctors, so the statement of two just men is evidence therein. And it is said: he is faced towards the sun with open eye, and if his eye tears, it is known it remains, otherwise no. And it is said: a snake is thrown before him, and if he flees from it, it is known it did not go, otherwise it has gone. And loss of smell is known by foul odors, and taste by his being distracted by feeding him something like colocynth after sweet, and speech by pricking his tongue with a needle: if black blood comes out, it is true; if red, no. Or his inattention is sought so that he hears his speech when no one is around. And hearing by being distracted then called out, and if he responds, it is known it did not go, otherwise it has gone. If it is said: How did you make obligatory four diyas when he struck him one blow and thereby intellect, speech, hearing, and sight went, while if it led to his death only one diya is obligatory, and death is greater in that? It is said: death is loss of the whole, and these things are dependent on the whole, so the dependent enters into the depended. But when he does not die, each of these meanings is not dependent on the other, so it does not enter into its compensation. (Compiled from Ayni and Fath)
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding diyat (blood money) for loss of senses and the male genitalia. The initial listing includes the penis, glans (hashafa), intellect (aql), hearing, sight, smell, taste, and beard if it does not regrow. The text then discusses diyat for loss of speech articulation: sixteen Arabic letters (excluding throat and lip letters) are identified; if the victim can pronounce most letters but with difficulty, a just arbitration (hukumat al-adl) is imposed, but if unable to pronounce most, full diya is due. The author provides the reasoning: loss of the penis involves loss of multiple benefits (intercourse, procreation, urination, etc.), and the glans is considered the primary organ for insertion and ejaculation, so full diya is required. For each sense (intellect, hearing, sight, smell, taste) full diya is mandated because each is a distinct intended benefit. A report is cited where Umar (or the Prophet) awarded four diyas for a single blow resulting in loss of intellect, speech, hearing, and sight. An intra-Hanafi dispute with Abu Yusuf is noted: he argues that the loss of these faculties cannot be verified, so the assailant's denial is accepted unless he admits or refuses an oath. The text then details methods to prove loss: for sight, it may be determined by doctors (two just witnesses) or by sun exposure or a snake test; for smell, by foul odors; for taste, by feeding bitter after sweet; for speech, by tongue pricking (black blood indicates truth); for hearing, by calling out unexpectedly. A question-answer objection is raised: if a single blow causing death requires only one diya, why are multiple diyas awarded for loss of faculties? The answer: death is loss of the whole, and these faculties are dependent parts that enter into the whole; but when alive, each faculty is independent and thus its loss is compensated separately.

Key Terms
دية (diya): Blood money, compensation paid for bodily harm or homicide; here, full diya is 100 camels or equivalent.
حكومة عدل (hukumat al-adl): A just arbitration value determined by a judge based on the extent of injury, used when no fixed diya is prescribed.
عقل (aql): Intellect or mental faculty; its loss requires full diya as it is a distinct benefit.
حشفة (hashafa): Glans of the penis; its loss requires full diya as the primary organ for intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a person loses both smell and taste due to a single blow, how many diyas are due?
A) One full diya
B) Two full diyas
C) Two hukumat al-adl
D) One diya for the blow and nothing extra

Key Takeaway
Full diya is due for the loss of each independent sense and for the penis/glans; multiple diyas can be awarded for a single blow, and the loss can be proven through objective tests accepted by Hanafi jurisprudence.

Diyat for Permanent Loss of Beard and Head Hair
Ruling on diyat for permanent loss of beard/head hair with Shafi'i/Maliki opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires full diya for permanent loss of beard/head hair and evaluate the Shafi'i/Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
Beard and head hair are complete beauty; their permanent loss demands full diya, like a limb.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute: does shaving the beard or head hair with permanent loss warrant full diya (blood money) or only a discretionary compensation (hukumat al-adl)? The Hanafi school rules that these features constitute complete beauty, so their total removal triggers full diya. The Shafi'i and Maliki schools analogize them to other body hair and require less. The passage also details the nuances of sparse beards and the critical condition of root damage.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: full diya for permanent loss of beard or head hair, conditioned on damage to the hair root and a year's wait without regrowth.
The ruling applies only if the hair does not regrow after a year; if it regrows, no diya but the assailant is disciplined.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Shafi'i and Maliki schools hold that only hukumat al-adl (assessed compensation) is due, not full diya.
They argue that hair is an increase that naturally regrows, and shaving is common in some cultures.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Their dalil: analogy to leg/chest hair (no diya), the fact that shaving is customary, and the slave case where only deficiency in value is due.
They also note that hair regrows after shaving, so permanent loss is not assumed.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes beard/head hair as integral to beauty, unlike other hair. Permanent loss removes complete beauty, analogous to protruding ears (fixed diya).
For the slave, purpose is service not beauty, so only value reduction.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi school awards full diya (e.g., 100 camels); Shafi'i/Maliki award a lesser, arbitrated amount.
This difference affects victims' compensation in personal injury cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عنده واللحية إن لم تنبت إلخ يعني إذا حلق اللحية أو شعر الرأس، فإن لم ينبت ففي كل واحد منهما دية كاملة؛ لأنه أزال جمالا على الكمال، وقال الشافعي ومالك: لا تجب فيهما الدية، وتجب فيهما حكومة عدل؛ لأن ذلك زيادة في الآدمي، ولهذا ينمو بعد كمال الحلقة، ولهذا يحلق الرأس كله واللحية بعضها في بعض البلاد، فلا تتعلق به الدية كشعر الساق والصدر، ولهذا يجب في شعر العبد نقصان القيمة ولنا أن اللحية في وقتها جمال، وفي حلقها تفويته على الكمال، فتجب الدية كما في الأذنين الشاخصتين، وكذا شعر الرأس جمال، ألا ترى أن من عدمه خلقة يتكلف في ستره، بخلاف شعر الصدر والساق؛ لأنه لا يتعلق به جمال، وأما لحية العبد، فعن أبي حنيفة له: أنه يجب فيه كمال القيمة، فلا يلزمنا وأما على ظاهر الرواية، فالجواب أن المقصود من العبد الاستخدام دون الجمال وهو لا يفوت بالحلق، بخلاف الحر، واختلفوا في لحية الكوسج، والأصح أنه إن كان على ذقنه شعرات معدودة فليس في حلقها شيء؛ لأن وجودها يشينه ولا يزينه وإن كان أكثر من ذلك بأن كان على الخد والذقن جميعا لكنه غير متصل، ففيه حكومة عدل؛ لأن فيه بعض الجمال، وإن كان متصلا، ففيه كمال الدية؛ لأنه ليس بكوسج، وفي لحيته كمال جمال، وهذا كله إذا أفسد المنبت، فيؤجل سنة، فإن لم ينبت فيها وجبت الدية، وإن نبت حتى استوى كما كان لا يجب شيء؛ لأنه لم يبق لفعل الجاني في البدن، ولكنه يؤدب على ذلك لارتكابه المحرم. واعلم أن قوله: "إن لم تنبت" قيد للحية وشعر الرأس جميعا، فلو أخر المصنف قوله: "لم تنبت" عن قوله: "شعر الرأس" لكان أولى. (تكملة، فتح، عيني)
With him, 'and the beard if it does not grow etc.' means if he shaves the beard or head hair, then if it does not grow, in each one of them full diya is required, because he removed complete beauty. Al-Shafi'i and Malik said: diya is not required in them, and hukumat al-adl is required in them, because that is an increase in the human, and therefore it grows after the completion of the creation, and therefore the entire head is shaved and the beard partially in some regions, so diya is not attached to it like the hair of the leg and chest, and therefore deficiency in value is required for the slave's hair. Our proof: the beard at its time is beauty, and in shaving it, it is lost completely, so diya is required just like the protruding ears. Similarly, head hair is beauty; do you not see that he who lacks it by creation goes to trouble to cover it, unlike chest and leg hair because no beauty is attached to it. As for the slave's beard, from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) that full value is required in it, so we are not bound. As for the apparent transmission, the answer is that the purpose of the slave is service, not beauty, and it is not lost by shaving, unlike the free person. They differed regarding the beard of the kawsaj (sparse beard), and the most correct is that if on his chin there are a few countable hairs, then nothing is in shaving them, because their existence disfigures him and does not adorn him. And if it is more than that, such that it is on both cheek and chin but disconnected, then hukumat al-adl is required, for there is some beauty. And if it is connected, then full diya is required, because he is not a kawsaj, and in his beard is complete beauty. All this is if he damaged the growth site, so a year is granted. If it does not grow within that time, diya becomes obligatory; if it grows until it becomes as it was, nothing is required because no effect of the assailant's act remains on the body, but he is disciplined for committing a prohibited act. And know that his statement 'if it does not grow' is a condition for both beard and head hair. If the author had placed 'does not grow' after 'head hair', it would have been better. (Takmila, Fath, Ayni)
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute on diyat for shaving the beard and head hair. The Hanafi ruling: if the hair does not regrow within a year, full diya is required because beard and head hair are considered complete beauty. The opponent's view (Shafi'i and Maliki): only hukumat al-adl (just arbitration) is required, as hair is a growth that naturally regrows and is not essential, analogous to leg and chest hair. They also argue that shaving is common in some regions and that for a slave, only a reduction in value is due. The Hanafi response: beard and head hair are beautifying features, unlike other body hair; their permanent loss removes a complete beauty, hence full diya, analogous to protruding ears. The passage then details the case of a kawsaj (man with sparse beard): if only a few hairs, nothing is due as they are disfiguring; if more but disconnected, hukumat al-adl; if connected and full, full diya. The condition for liability is that the hair root (manbit) is damaged; a one-year wait is allowed for regrowth. If it regrows, no diya but the assailant is disciplined for the prohibited act of shaving. A textual note indicates that the condition 'if it does not grow' applies to both beard and head hair, and the author's wording could have been clearer.

Key Terms
كوسج (kawsaj): A man with sparse or non-connected facial hair; his beard is not considered complete beauty.
منبت (manbit): The root or growth site of hair; damaging it is a condition for diya.
حكومة عدل (hukumat al-adl): A justly assessed compensation when no fixed arsh exists; here, for partial or non-beauty hair loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The length of the beard
B) Whether the beard is considered beautiful (connected and full)
C) The age of the man
D) Whether the shaving was intentional

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school awards full diya for permanent loss of beard or head hair because they are considered complete beauty, but only if the root is damaged and a year passes without regrowth; sparse or disconnected beards receive only hukumat al-adl.

Diyat for Paired Organs and Classification of Body Parts
Rulings on diyat for paired organs and classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fixed diyat amounts for paired organs and classify body parts into individuals, pairs, quarters, tenths, and teeth according to Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
For paired organs, loss of both demands full diya; loss of one demands half; exceptions like male breasts require hukumat al-adl.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq systematizes the fixed diyat (arsh) for various body parts. It covers specific rulings for eyes, hands, lips, eyebrows, testicles, and female breasts, including sequential cutting and hermaphrodite status. It then provides a comprehensive classification framework that simplifies diyat calculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the paired organs and their default diya
List the paired organs mentioned: eyes, hands, lips, eyebrows, testicles, female breasts, nipples. Note that for each pair, loss of both requires full diya, loss of one requires half diya, unless otherwise specified (e.g., male breasts have hukumat al-adl).
The text explicitly states: 'And the two eyes... full diya for both, half for one.'
2
Analyze special cases: sequential cutting and hermaphrodite
Read the rulings for cutting testicles and penis in different orders, and note the difference between Abu Hanifa and the two companions regarding hermaphrodite breast diya.
If testicles cut after penis, two diyas; if testicles cut first, hukumat al-adl for penis.
3
Memorize the five-category classification system
Organize body parts into five groups: individuals (afrad), pairs (azwaj), quarters (arba'), tenths (ashar), and teeth (asnan). Note the diya fraction for each: full, half, quarter, tenth, half-tenth respectively.
4
Connect classifications to specific examples
Apply the classification: nose (individual) → full diya; one eye (pair) → half diya; one eyelash (quarter) → quarter diya; one finger (tenth) → tenth diya; one tooth → half-tenth diya.
The text also includes 'meanings' as individuals: intellect, soul, smell, taste.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on hermaphrodite
Abu Hanifa considers hermaphrodite like a woman (full diya for both breasts, half for one); Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require half of what is in a man's breasts and half of what is in a woman's breasts.
The mufta bihi is the majority view as presented.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(فتح) وثديي المرأة: ففي قطعهما الدية كاملة، وفي قطع أحدهما نصف الدية بخلاف ثديي الرجل؛ لأنه ليس فيه تفويت منفعة الإرضاع، فيجب حكومة عدل، وفي حلمتي المرأة كمال الدية؛ لفوات منفعة الإرضاع وإمساك اللبن، وفي إحداهما نصف الدية، والخنثى كالمرأة عند الإمام وعندهما يجب نصف ما في ثديي الرجل، ونصف ما في ثديي المرأة. (فتح) الدية واعلم أن ما لا ثاني له في بدن الإنسان من الأعضاء، أو المعاني المقصودة ففيه كمال الدية، والأعضاء أربعة أنواع أفراد وهي ثلاثة الأنف واللسان والذكر، والمعاني التي هي أفراد في البدن: العقل والنفس والشم والذوق، وأما الأعضاء التي هي أزواج، فالعينان والأذنان الشاخصتان والحاجبان والشفتان واليدان وثديا المرأة والأنثيان والرجلان، ففيهما الدية وفي أحدهما نصفها والتي هي أرباع أشفار العين، وفي كل شفر ربع الدية، والتي أعشار: أصابع اليدين والرجلين ففي العشرة الدية وفي الواحدة عشرها، والتي تزيد على ذلك: الأسنان، وفي كل منها نصف عشر الدية، ويأتي بيان ذلك رد المحتار) وفي كل واحد إلخ: أراد به ما هو مزدوج من هذه الأعضاء المذكورة كما في العين الواحدة واليد الواحدة. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٤١/٢]
And the two eyes [intentional or accidental]; what is meant by his statement 'the two eyes' is loss of their globes, and in his statement 'the sight' is loss of light while the eye remains, and this is if accidental; as for intentional, there is qisas in it as indicated by his statement earlier: 'the eye if it goes while it is protruding' so remember that. (Ayni, Fath) And the two hands: if cut from the joint, accidentally or from elsewhere, intentionally or accidentally. And the two lips: if cut from the root accidentally, or cutting part of them intentionally or accidentally. And the two eyebrows: whether shaving them is intentional or accidental. And the two testicles [i.e., the two testicles if accidental]. Likewise the two breasts of a woman; and is there qisas in them when intentional? There is no mention of it in the apparent books. And if the testicles are cut before the penis, or the penis first then the testicles, then there are two diyas, because the benefit of the testicles after cutting the penis remains, which is retention of semen and urine. If the testicles are cut first then the penis, then for the testicles diya, and for the penis hukumat al-adl, because by cutting the testicles he becomes a eunuch, and for the penis of a eunuch hukumat al-adl. (Fath) And the two breasts of a woman: cutting both requires full diya, and cutting one requires half diya, unlike the breasts of a man because there is no loss of the benefit of breastfeeding, so hukumat al-adl is required. And in the nipples of a woman full diya, for loss of the benefit of breastfeeding and retention of milk; and in one of them half diya. The hermaphrodite is like a woman according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and according to the two companions, half of what is in the man's breasts and half of what is in the woman's breasts are required. (Fath) The diya: And know that whatever has no second in the human body of organs or intended meanings, full diya is in it. The organs are four types: individuals, which are three: nose, tongue, penis; the meanings that are individuals in the body: intellect, soul, smell, taste. As for organs that are pairs, they are: the two eyes, protruding ears, eyebrows, lips, hands, woman's breasts, testicles, feet; full diya for both and half for one. And those that are quarters: the eyelashes; in each lash a quarter diya. And those that are tenths: fingers of hands and feet; in ten full diya, in one a tenth. And those that exceed that: teeth; in each half a tenth diya; and its explanation will come (Radd al-Muhtar). And 'in each one etc.' means by it what is paired from these mentioned organs, as in one eye and one hand.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement summarizing the fixed diyat for paired organs and classifying body parts. It begins with the eyes: loss of the eyeball (even if light remains) is considered loss of the eye, and intentional loss invites qisas, but accidental loss requires diya. It then lists various paired organs: hands (cut from joint or elsewhere), lips, eyebrows, testicles, female breasts. Special cases are noted: if both testicles and penis are cut sequentially, the order matters—if testicles cut after penis, two diyas because testicles still serve a purpose; if testicles cut first, only hukumat al-adl for the penis because it becomes that of a eunuch. Female breasts require full diya for both, half for one; male breasts require only hukumat al-adl. Nipples of a woman have full diya. Hermaphrodite's ruling differs between Abu Hanifa and the two companions. The passage concludes with a systematic classification: individual organs (no pair) like nose, tongue, penis, and individual meanings (intellect, soul, smell, taste) command full diya. Paired organs command full diya for both and half for one. Quarter diya applies to each eyelash (shufr). Tenth diya to each finger/toe. Half-tenth diya for each tooth. The text also notes that the phrase 'each one' refers to paired organs like one eye or one hand.

Key Terms
أفراد (afrad): Organs that exist singly in the body (no pair); loss requires full diya.
أزواج (azwaj): Paired organs; loss of both requires full diya, one side half diya.
شفر (shufr): Eyelash; each eyelash is a quarter of diya (total four lashes per eye?).

A) Full diya
B) Half diya

D) Two diyas

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of body parts for diyat provides fixed fractional amounts for individuals (full), pairs (half per side), quarters (eyelashes), tenths (fingers/toes), and half-tenths (teeth).

Diyat — Blood Money

Diyat for Beard and Head Hair: Regrowth Condition
Ruling on diyat for beard/head hair with conditions on beauty and regrowth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules of diyat for beard and head hair, distinguishing between full diya, equitable compensation, or no compensation based on beauty and regrowth.

Core Idea
Beard and head hair diyya depends on beauty: full diyya for full beauty, equitable for partial, nothing if removal improves appearance.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq details the rules for blood money when someone forcibly removes another's beard or head hair. The ruling hinges on whether the removal disfigures or enhances, and crucially, whether the hair root (manbit) is damaged, requiring a one-year observation period. Understanding this distinction is vital for accurate diyya assessment in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of hair removal
The passage describes three cases: (1) hair that disfigures (e.g., sparse beard) – removal improves appearance; (2) hair that partially beautifies (non-connected patches); (3) hair that fully beautifies (connected, full beard).
This is based on whether the hair adds beauty or not.
2
Determine compensation for each category
For disfiguring hair: no compensation. For partial beauty: equitable compensation (hukumat al-adl). For full beauty: full diyya.
The compensation is not fixed but judged by the qadi for hukumat al-adl.
3
Understand the condition of manbit damage
All the above rulings apply only when the hair growth root (manbit) is damaged. If the manbit is intact, the hair will regrow and no compensation is due.
Manbit damage is essential for liability.
4
Apply the one-year waiting period
If the manbit is damaged, the offender is given a one-year reprieve. If the hair regrows within the year, no diyya; if it does not, full diyya becomes due.
The waiting period is a critical condition before liability is finalized.
5
Note the ta'zir for prohibited act
Even if the hair regrows and no diyya is due, the offender may still be disciplined (ta'zir) for committing a prohibited act (forcibly shaving someone's hair).
Criminal liability exists separately from civil compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فليس في حلقها شيء؛ لأن وجودها يشينه ولا يزينه وإن كان أكثر من ذلك بأن كان على الخد والذقن جميعا لكنه غير متصل، ففيه حكومة عدل؛ لأن فيه بعض الجمال، وإن كان متصلا، ففيه كمال الدية؛ لأنه ليس بكوسج، وفي لحيته كمال جمال، وهذا كله إذا أفسد المنبت، فيؤجل سنة، فإن لم تنبت فيها وجبت الدية، وإن نبت حتى استوى كما كان لا يجب شيء؛ لأنه لم يبق لفعل الجاني في البدن، ولكنه يؤدب على ذلك لارتكابه المحرم. واعلم أن قوله: "إن لم تنبت" قيد للحية وشعر الرأس جميعا
There is nothing in shaving it because its existence disfigures him and does not adorn him. If it is more than that, e.g., on both cheek and chin but not connected, then equitable compensation is due because there is some beauty. If it is connected, then full blood money is due because he is not hairless. In his beard there is complete beauty. All this is when the growth root is damaged, so he is deferred for one year. If it does not grow within it, blood money becomes obligatory. If it grows until it becomes equal as before, nothing is obligatory because no trace of the offender's act remains on the body, but he is disciplined for committing the prohibited. Know that his statement "if it does not grow" is a condition for both beard and head hair.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq discusses the blood money (diya) for removing beard and head hair. The ruling differentiates based on whether the hair removal adds beauty or disfigurement. If the removed hair (e.g., a sparse beard) actually disfigures, no diya is due. If some beauty remains (e.g., non-connected patches), equitable compensation (hukumat al-adl) is given. If the hair is full and connected (like a proper beard), full diya is due because it constitutes complete beauty. The key condition is that the hair growth root (manbit) must be damaged. Then the victim is observed for one year; if hair grows back normally, no diya—only discipline for the offender. If it does not regrow, full diya is owed. This applies to both beard and head hair.

Key Terms
المنبت (al-manbit): The hair growth root (follicle) in the skin whose damage prevents regrowth
حكومة عدل (hukumat al-adl): Equitable compensation assessed by a judge when a fixed diya is not prescribed
الدية (al-diyah): Full blood money (100 camels or equivalent) for a life or complete organ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One month
B) One year
C) Until the victim dies
D) No waiting period

Key Takeaway
The one-year waiting period and the condition of manbit damage are crucial for establishing liability for hair loss in Hanafi diyat law.

Diyat for Eyelashes, Fingers, and Joints
Fixed diya amounts for eyelashes, fingers, and joints.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyat amounts for eyelashes, each finger, and each joint of the fingers according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Diyat is fixed proportional: one-quarter for one eyelash, one-tenth per finger, and one-third or half per joint depending on joint count.

This lesson covers the specific diyat amounts for small but important body parts: eyelashes, fingers, and their joints. These rulings are precise, reflecting the principle that diyat compensates for both function and beauty. Understanding these will help you calculate compensation for injuries to extremities and facial features.

Guided Path
1
Count the eyelashes
Identify that 'ashfar' refers to the four edges of the eyelids (two upper, two lower). The diya for all four is full diya. For one edge (shifr), it's one-quarter.
Hanafi: each edge is considered a separate unit.
2
Identify finger diya
Each finger of either hand or foot gets one-tenth of full diya. This includes thumbs, index, middle, ring, and little fingers.
No distinction between hand and foot fingers.
3
Calculate joint diya
A finger with three joints: each joint is one-third of that finger's diya. For the thumb (two joints): each joint is one-half.
Joints are valued proportionally to the finger total.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي أشفار العينين دية، وفي أحدها ربعها، وفي كل إصبع من أصابع اليدين والرجلين عشرها، وما فيها مفاصل، ففي أحدها ثلث دية إصبع، ونصفها لو فيها مفصلان، وفي كل سن خمس من الإبل، أو خمس مائة درهم وكل عضو ذهب نفعه، ففيه دية كاملة كيد شلت وعين ذهب ضوؤها.
And for the eyelashes of both eyes is a full blood money, and for one of them is a quarter of it. And for every finger of the fingers of the hands and feet is a tenth of it. And in what has joints among them, for one joint is a third of the blood money of a finger, and half if it has two joints. And for every tooth is five camels or five hundred dirhams. And every organ whose function is lost, in it is full blood money, like a hand that is paralyzed or an eye whose light is lost.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq provides specific fixed amounts (diya) for various body parts: Eyelashes: full diya for both, quarter for one. Fingers: each finger (of hands or feet) is one-tenth of full diya. For fingers with joints, each joint is one-third of the finger's diya if three joints, half if two joints (like thumb). Teeth: each tooth is five camels or five hundred dirhams. Finally, a general rule: any organ that loses its function incurs full diya, regardless of whether its form remains. Examples: a paralyzed hand or an eye blinded. This is because diya is based on loss of benefit (manfa'ah), not just form. If an organ has no function but has beauty (e.g., a prominent ear), its loss may require full diya if beauty is lost.

Key Terms
الأشفار (al-ashfar): The edges of the eyelids where eyelashes grow; plural of shifr
المفصل (al-mafsal): A joint of a finger; each finger has 1-3 joints

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Two

Key Takeaway
Diyat for eyelashes, fingers, and joints is fixed as fractions of full diya, with joint values depending on the finger's total joints.

Diyat for Teeth and Loss of Function
Fixed diya for teeth and general rule for loss of function.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diya amount for a single tooth and apply the general rule that loss of function alone incurs full diya for an organ.

Core Idea
Diya for a tooth is five camels (or 500 dirhams); any organ that loses its function entirely requires full diya, even if its form remains.

This lesson covers two important rulings: the fixed diya for teeth (every tooth, regardless of type, carries the same amount) and the general principle that loss of function (like a paralyzed hand or blind eye) triggers full diya. This principle shows that diya compensates for utility, not just physical loss.

Guided Path
1
Identify tooth diya
Every tooth, whether incisor or molar, primary or permanent, gets five camels or five hundred dirhams.
Hanafi: no distinction between front and back teeth.
2
Understand the general rule
If an organ remains physically present but loses its function, the diya is the same as if it were completely severed. Examples: a paralyzed hand, an eye blinded.
The function (naf') is the basis of value.

Diyat for Eyelids (Al-Ashfar)
Ruling on diyat for eyelids with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyat amounts for eyelids and explain the reasoning based on aesthetic and protective functions.

Core Idea
Full diyat for both eyelids; one-quarter for one, because beauty and protection are lost.

This lesson focuses on the first part of the passage, which establishes the diyat for the eyelids (ashfar). The ruling is presented with a concise statement followed by commentary explaining the rationale. Understanding this ruling requires appreciation of how Hanafi fiqh values both aesthetic and functional aspects of body parts in determining compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action triggers diyat for eyelids: cutting or removing the eyelids (ashfar) such that they do not grow back. The ruling: full diyat for both, one-quarter for one eyelid.
The text specifies 'قلعها ولم تنبت' (pulled out and did not grow back).
2
Locate the proof and reasoning
The commentary provides the rationale: eyelids contribute to beauty and protect the eye from harm and dirt. This is a form of ta'lil (legal reasoning) based on the purpose (hikmah) of the limb.
No explicit hadith is cited for eyelids; the ruling is derived from general principles of compensation.
3
Understand the scope
Note that the ruling applies whether the act is intentional or accidental, and that the eyelashes are considered part of the eyelid. If the entire eyelid with lashes is cut, one diyat is due.
The commentary clarifies that the lashes and eyelids are treated as one unit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الديات
ديات الأطراف
وفي أشفار العينين دية، وفي أحدها ربعها، وفي كل إصبع من أصابع اليدين والرجلين عشرها، وما فيها مفاصل، ففي أحدها ثلث دية إصبع، ونصفها لو فيها مفصلان، وفي كل سن خمس من الإبل، أو خمس مائة درهم وكل عضو ذهب نفعه، ففيه دية كاملة كيد شلت وعين ذهب ضوؤها.

و في أشفار العينين إلخ [عمدا كان أو خطأ] [جمع شفرة بضم الشين وهو حرف الجفن حيث ينبت الهدب. (عيني)] وفي أشفار العينين الدية إذا قلعها ولم تنبت وفي أحدها أي أحد الأشفار ربعها أي ربع الدية؛ لأنه يتعلق بها الجمال على الكمال، ويتعلق بها دفع الأذى والقذى من العين، ولو قطع الجفون بأشفارها تحب دية واحدة؛ لأن الأشفار مع الجفون كشيء واحد [رمز الحقائق: ٤٤١/٢] وفي كل إصبع إلخ : أي في كل إصبع من أصابع اليدين أو الرجلين عشرها أي عشر الدية؛ لأن في قطع جميع الأصابع الدية، وفي قطع واحدة عشرها؛ لقوله عليه: " في كل إصبع عشر من الإبل، والأصابع كلها سواء، ولا يعتبر الزيادة فيها. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٤١/٢] وما فيها مفاصل إلخ: أي الأصابع التي فيها مفاصل، ففي أحدها ثلث دية إصبع؛ لأنه ثلثها، فدية الإصبع الألف، فيجب في أحد المفاصل ثلث الألف، ونصفها أي نصف دية إصبع لو كان فيها أي في الإصبع مفصلان كالإبهام ففي أحدها نصف دية أصبع كما هو ظاهر. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٤١/٢]
وفي كل سن إلخ : إذا كان قلعه خطأ وإن كان عمدا ففيه القصاص كما مر] لقوله : "وفي كل سن خمس من الإبل". وكل عضو إلخ أي إذا ضرب عضوا، فذهب نفعه بضربه، ففيه دية كاملة كما إذا ضرب يده فشلت به، أو عينه فذهب ضوءها؛ لأن وجوب الدية يتعلق بتفويت جنس المنفعة، فإذا زالت منفعة كلها وجب عليه أرش موجبه كله ولا عبرة للصورة بدون المنفعة؛ لكونها تابعة، فلا يكون لها حصة من الأرش إلا إذا تجردت عند الإتلاف بأن أتلف عضوا ذهب منفعته فحينئذ يجب فيه حكومة عدل إن لم يكن فيه جمال كاليد الشلاء، أو أرشه كاملا إن كان فيه جمال كالأذن الشاخصة، فلا يلزم من اعتبار الصورة والجمال عند انفراده عن اعتبارهما معا. تكملة البحر الرائق: ۱۳۷/۹] وكذا إذا ضربه في صلبه، فانقطع ماؤه تجب الدية، وكذا لو أحدبه، ولو زالت الحدوبة، فلا شيء عليه لزوالها رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٢/٢]
Book of Diyat. Diyat of Limbs. And for the two eyelids of both eyes is the full diyat, and for one of them is one-quarter of it. And for every finger from the fingers of the hands and feet is one-tenth of it. And whatever has joints, then for one of them is one-third of the diyat of a finger, and half of it if it has two joints. And for every tooth is five camels, or five hundred dirhams. And every limb whose function is lost, then in it is the full diyat, like a hand that becomes paralyzed and an eye whose sight is lost. Commentary: 'And for the two eyelids etc.' whether intentional or accidental. 'Asfar' plural of 'shifr' with damma on shin, which is the edge of the eyelid where the eyelashes grow. And for the two eyelids of both eyes is the full diyat when they are pulled out and do not grow back. And for one of them, i.e., one of the eyelids, is one-quarter of it, i.e., one-quarter of the full diyat; because beauty depends on them completely, and they serve to repel harm and dirt from the eye. And if one cuts the eyelids with their lashes, one full diyat is due, because the lashes and eyelids are like one thing. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/441] 'And for every finger etc.': i.e., for every finger of the fingers of the hands or feet is one-tenth of it, i.e., one-tenth of the full diyat; because cutting all the fingers incurs the full diyat, and cutting one incurs one-tenth; due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'For every finger is ten camels, and all fingers are equal, and the increase (in number) is not considered.' [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/441] 'And whatever has joints etc.': i.e., fingers that have joints, then for one joint is one-third of the diyat of a finger; because it is one-third of it. So the diyat of a finger is one thousand, so for one joint one-third of a thousand is obligatory. And half of it, i.e., half of the diyat of a finger, if the finger has two joints, like the thumb, then for one joint is half of the diyat of a finger, as is apparent. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/441] 'And for every tooth etc.': if it is extracted unintentionally, but if intentional then retaliation is due as mentioned earlier, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'And for every tooth is five camels.' 'And every limb etc.': i.e., if one strikes a limb and its function is lost by the strike, then full diyat is due, as when one strikes his hand and it becomes paralyzed, or his eye and its light is lost; because the obligation of diyat is connected to the loss of the type of function. So when all of its function is removed, full compensation for the entire cause is obligatory upon him, and consideration is not given to the form without the function, because the form is subsidiary. So it has no share of compensation unless it is considered separately at the time of destruction, i.e., if one destroys a limb whose function is already lost, then in that case a just discretionary compensation (hukumat al-adl) is obligatory if there is no beauty in it, like a paralyzed hand; or full compensation if there is beauty in it, like a protruding ear. So it does not follow that considering form and beauty together when they are separate is the same as considering them together. [Takmilat al-Bahr al-Raiq: 9/137] Similarly, if he strikes his back (spine) and his (seminal) fluid is cut off, the full diyat is obligatory; and similarly if he makes him hunchbacked; and if the hump goes away, nothing is due upon him due to its removal. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/442]
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq is a ruling statement with proof, presented as a commentary (sharh) on the original matn. It covers the diyat amounts for specific body parts: eyelids, fingers, teeth, and the general principle for loss of function. The text begins by stating that cutting both eyelids (asfar) incurs the full diyat, and cutting one eyelid incurs one-quarter of the full diyat. The commentator clarifies that this applies whether done intentionally or accidentally, and that the eyelashes are considered part of the eyelid. The reason given is that eyelids serve both aesthetic and protective functions. Then the passage addresses fingers: each finger of the hands or feet incurs one-tenth of the full diyat, based on the hadith 'For every finger is ten camels.' All fingers are treated equally regardless of size. For fingers with joints (i.e., fingers except the thumb which has two joints), cutting one joint incurs one-third of the finger's diyat, because the finger has three joints. For the thumb, which has two joints, cutting one joint incurs half the finger's diyat. For teeth, each tooth incurs five camels (or five hundred dirhams) if the extraction was accidental; intentional extraction leads to retaliation. The passage then expands to the general rule: if a limb's function is destroyed, the full diyat is due, even if the limb remains intact. The example given is a paralyzed hand or an eye that loses sight. However, if a limb that already lacks function is destroyed, then only a discretionary compensation (hukumat al-adl) is due if the limb has no aesthetic value (like a paralyzed hand), or full compensation if it has aesthetic value (like a protruding ear). Finally, the text mentions that striking the spine causing loss of seminal fluid or causing a hump incurs full diyat, but if the hump goes away, nothing is due. The entire exposition is rooted in Hanafi fiqh, with proofs from hadith and rational reasoning (ta'lil).

Key Terms
أشفار (ashfar): Eyelids, specifically the edges where eyelashes grow.
دية (diyah): Fixed compensation paid for causing injury or death, varying by body part.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the diyat for removing one eyelid permanently?
A) Full diyat
B) Half diyat
C) One-quarter diyat
D) One-third diyat

Key Takeaway
The diyat for eyelids is fixed: full diyat for both, one-quarter for one, based on their combined role in beauty and protection.

Diyat for Fingers and Joints
Ruling on diyat for fingers and joints with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the diyat for fingers and their joints, applying the rule of proportional division.

Core Idea
Each finger: one-tenth diyat; each joint: one-third of a finger's diyat for three-joint fingers, half for two-joint fingers.

This lesson covers the second part of the passage, detailing diyat for fingers and their joints. The rulings are based on a hadith and logical division. Understanding the proportional system is essential for accurate compensation in cases of finger injuries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling for fingers
The passage states that for each finger of the hands or feet, one-tenth of the full diyat is due. This is based on the hadith: 'For every finger, ten camels.'
All fingers are equal; no difference between fingers of hand or foot, or between fingers of different sizes.
2
Apply the joint rule
For fingers with three joints (most fingers), cutting one joint incurs one-third of the diyat of that finger. For the thumb, which has two joints, cutting one joint incurs half of the finger's diyat.
The diyat of a finger is set at one thousand (dirhams or camels equivalent) for calculation purposes; a joint's diyat is a fraction of that.
3
Compute the amounts
If full diyat is 10,000 dirhams (or 100 camels), one finger diyat is 1,000 dirhams (10 camels). For a three-joint finger, one joint diyat is 333.33 dirhams (3.33 camels). For the thumb, one joint diyat is 500 dirhams (5 camels).
The text uses 'alf' (one thousand) as a convenient figure for the finger's diyat.

Diyat for Teeth and Loss of Function Principle
Ruling on diyat for teeth and general principle for loss of function

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyat for teeth and apply the general principle that loss of a limb's function incurs full diyat regardless of form.

Core Idea
Each tooth: five camels; loss of function of any limb: full diyat, even if the limb remains intact.

This lesson covers the last part of the passage: diyat for teeth and the general rule for loss of limb function. The hadith for teeth is cited, and the commentator elaborates a key principle: diyat is based on the loss of function (manfa'ah), not just the physical form. This has wide implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for teeth
Each tooth that is extracted accidentally incurs a diyat of five camels (or five hundred dirhams). If done intentionally, retaliation (qisas) applies instead of diyat.
The text mentions 'or five hundred dirhams' as an alternative payment.
2
Understand the loss of function principle
If any limb loses its function entirely, full diyat is due. Examples: a paralyzed hand or an eye that loses sight. The form of the limb is irrelevant; the function is what matters.
This is a general principle that overrides the specific amounts for individual parts when only function is lost.
3
Apply the exceptions
If a limb already lacks function (e.g., a paralyzed hand) is destroyed, then only hukumat al-adl (discretionary compensation) is due if there is no beauty, or full compensation if there is beauty (e.g., a protruding ear).
The commentator gives examples: a paralyzed hand (no beauty) gets hukumat al-adl; a protruding ear (has beauty) gets full compensation.

وفي كل سن إلخ : إذا كان قلعه خطأ وإن كان عمدا ففيه القصاص كما مر] لقوله : "وفي كل سن خمس من الإبل". وكل عضو إلخ أي إذا ضرب عضوا، فذهب نفعه بضربه، ففيه دية كاملة كما إذا ضرب يده فشلت به، أو عينه فذهب ضوءها؛ لأن وجوب الدية يتعلق بتفويت جنس المنفعة، فإذا زالت منفعة كلها وجب عليه أرش موجبه كله ولا عبرة للصورة بدون المنفعة؛ لكونها تابعة، فلا يكون لها حصة من الأرش إلا إذا تجردت عند الإتلاف بأن أتلف عضوا ذهب منفعته فحينئذ يجب فيه حكومة عدل إن لم يكن فيه جمال كاليد الشلاء، أو أرشه كاملا إن كان فيه جمال كالأذن الشاخصة، فلا يلزم من اعتبار الصورة والجمال عند انفراده عن اعتبارهما معا. تكملة البحر الرائق: ۱۳۷/۹] وكذا إذا ضربه في صلبه، فانقطع ماؤه تجب الدية، وكذا لو أحدبه، ولو زالت الحدوبة، فلا شيء عليه لزوالها رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٢/٢]
Book of Diyat. Diyat of Limbs. And for the two eyelids of both eyes is the full diyat, and for one of them is one-quarter of it. And for every finger from the fingers of the hands and feet is one-tenth of it. And whatever has joints, then for one of them is one-third of the diyat of a finger, and half of it if it has two joints. And for every tooth is five camels, or five hundred dirhams. And every limb whose function is lost, then in it is the full diyat, like a hand that becomes paralyzed and an eye whose sight is lost. Commentary: 'And for the two eyelids etc.' whether intentional or accidental. 'Asfar' plural of 'shifr' with damma on shin, which is the edge of the eyelid where the eyelashes grow. And for the two eyelids of both eyes is the full diyat when they are pulled out and do not grow back. And for one of them, i.e., one of the eyelids, is one-quarter of it, i.e., one-quarter of the full diyat; because beauty depends on them completely, and they serve to repel harm and dirt from the eye. And if one cuts the eyelids with their lashes, one full diyat is due, because the lashes and eyelids are like one thing. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/441] 'And for every finger etc.': i.e., for every finger of the fingers of the hands or feet is one-tenth of it, i.e., one-tenth of the full diyat; because cutting all the fingers incurs the full diyat, and cutting one incurs one-tenth; due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'For every finger is ten camels, and all fingers are equal, and the increase (in number) is not considered.' [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/441] 'And whatever has joints etc.': i.e., fingers that have joints, then for one joint is one-third of the diyat of a finger; because it is one-third of it. So the diyat of a finger is one thousand, so for one joint one-third of a thousand is obligatory. And half of it, i.e., half of the diyat of a finger, if the finger has two joints, like the thumb, then for one joint is half of the diyat of a finger, as is apparent. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/441] 'And for every tooth etc.': if it is extracted unintentionally, but if intentional then retaliation is due as mentioned earlier, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'And for every tooth is five camels.' 'And every limb etc.': i.e., if one strikes a limb and its function is lost by the strike, then full diyat is due, as when one strikes his hand and it becomes paralyzed, or his eye and its light is lost; because the obligation of diyat is connected to the loss of the type of function. So when all of its function is removed, full compensation for the entire cause is obligatory upon him, and consideration is not given to the form without the function, because the form is subsidiary. So it has no share of compensation unless it is considered separately at the time of destruction, i.e., if one destroys a limb whose function is already lost, then in that case a just discretionary compensation (hukumat al-adl) is obligatory if there is no beauty in it, like a paralyzed hand; or full compensation if there is beauty in it, like a protruding ear. So it does not follow that considering form and beauty together when they are separate is the same as considering them together. [Takmilat al-Bahr al-Raiq: 9/137] Similarly, if he strikes his back (spine) and his (seminal) fluid is cut off, the full diyat is obligatory; and similarly if he makes him hunchbacked; and if the hump goes away, nothing is due upon him due to its removal. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/442]
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq is a ruling statement with proof, presented as a commentary (sharh) on the original matn. It covers the diyat amounts for specific body parts: eyelids, fingers, teeth, and the general principle for loss of function. The text begins by stating that cutting both eyelids (asfar) incurs the full diyat, and cutting one eyelid incurs one-quarter of the full diyat. The commentator clarifies that this applies whether done intentionally or accidentally, and that the eyelashes are considered part of the eyelid. The reason given is that eyelids serve both aesthetic and protective functions. Then the passage addresses fingers: each finger of the hands or feet incurs one-tenth of the full diyat, based on the hadith 'For every finger is ten camels.' All fingers are treated equally regardless of size. For fingers with joints (i.e., fingers except the thumb which has two joints), cutting one joint incurs one-third of the finger's diyat, because the finger has three joints. For the thumb, which has two joints, cutting one joint incurs half the finger's diyat. For teeth, each tooth incurs five camels (or five hundred dirhams) if the extraction was accidental; intentional extraction leads to retaliation. The passage then expands to the general rule: if a limb's function is destroyed, the full diyat is due, even if the limb remains intact. The example given is a paralyzed hand or an eye that loses sight. However, if a limb that already lacks function is destroyed, then only a discretionary compensation (hukumat al-adl) is due if the limb has no aesthetic value (like a paralyzed hand), or full compensation if it has aesthetic value (like a protruding ear). Finally, the text mentions that striking the spine causing loss of seminal fluid or causing a hump incurs full diyat, but if the hump goes away, nothing is due. The entire exposition is rooted in Hanafi fiqh, with proofs from hadith and rational reasoning (ta'lil).

Key Terms
سن (sinn): Tooth.
منفعة (manfa'ah): Function or benefit of a limb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the diyat for a tooth?
A) One-tenth of full diyat
B) Five camels
C) One hundred dirhams
D) Full diyat

Key Takeaway
Teeth: fixed diyat per tooth; loss of function of any limb: full diyat, with exceptions for already non-functional limbs.

Definition and Classification of Shijaj
Definition and classification of head wounds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the ten types of head and facial wounds (shijaj) according to the Hanafi school and distinguish them from other wounds (jarahat).

Core Idea
A shajjah is only on the head or face; elsewhere it is a jarahah with no fixed diyat.

This passage begins a new chapter on shijaj, defining their linguistic scope and enumerating ten specific types. Understanding this classification is essential because fixed diyat applies only to these head/facial wounds, not to other body parts. The commentary emphasizes that the ruling is built on the precise linguistic meaning, so a wound on the leg, even if it resembles a mudihah, does not qualify.

Guided Path
1
Define shajjah linguistically and legally
Identify that shajjah is a wound on the face or head only; other wounds are jarahah. This definition determines which wounds have fixed diyat.
The ruling is based on the 'reality' (haqiqah) of the term, i.e., its linguistic usage.
2
Recognize the unique status of ja'ifah
Note that ja'ifah (penetrating wound into a cavity) can occur on the head or abdomen, so it is included in the diyat discussion but not counted among the ten shijaj.
Ja'ifah is mentioned alongside ammah because of equal diyat, but it is not a shajjah in the strict sense.
3
Trace the progression of wound depth
Start from the most superficial (harisah: skin cut without blood) and move deeper through damiyah, badi'ah, up to ammah (reaching the brain membrane). Understand the anatomical landmarks.
Memorizing the order helps in diagnosis and legal categorization.
4
Enumerate all ten types in order
List: 1) harisah, 2) damiyah (or dami'ah), 3) dami'ah (or damiyah), 4) badi'ah, 5) mutalahimah, 6) simhaq, 7) mudihah, 8) hashimah, 9) munaqqilah, 10) ammah. Note that the source says hashimah was omitted in one list but is the tenth.
The commentary from al-Fath clarifies that hashimah is the tenth type.
5
Apply the classification rule to a scenario
Given a description of a wound, determine whether it is a shajjah or jarahah, and if shajjah, identify its type (e.g., a wound that exposes bone without displacement = mudihah).
This is the practical skill for qadis and muftis.

أحكام الشجاج
فصل في الشجاج
في الموضحة نصف عشر الدية، وفي الهاشمة عشرها، وفي المنقلة عشر ونصف عشر،
وفي الآمة أو الجائفة ثلثها
التي تصل إلى الجوف

فصل: عقد للشجاج فصلا على حدة لكثرة مسائلها، وإن كانت نوعا من أنواع ما دون النفس. (فتح) في الشجاج: الشجاج - بالكسر - جمع شجة بالفتح، وهي في اللغة الجرح يكون في الوجه أو الرأس، وما يكون بغيرها يسمى جراحة، فالحكم مرتب على الحقيقة أي حكم الشجاج يثبت في الوجه والرأس على ما هو حقيقة اللغة؛ لأن الشجة لغة ما كان فيهما لا غير، وفي غيرهما لا يجب المقدر فيهما، بل يجب حكومة عدل، فلو تحققت الموضحة مثلا في نحو الساق واليد لا يجب الأرش المقدر لها؛ لأنها جراحة لا موضحة، بل يجب حكومة عدل؛ لأن التقدير بالتوقيف، وهذا إنما ورد في ما يختص بالوجه والرأس، ولا شيء من الجراح لها أرش معلوم إلا الجائفة كما في "الظهيرية".
واعلم أن الشجاج عشرة؛ لأن الشجة إما أن تقطع الجلد فقط، أو تزيد عليه، والأولى إما أن يظهر فيها دم أو لا، الأولى الحارصة، والثانية إما أن تسيل أو لا، الثاني: الدامعة والأول: الدامية، وما يزيد إما أن يقطع اللحم الذي بينه وبين العظم أو لا، الثاني: الباضعة والأول: إما أن يظهر القطع الجلدة الرقيقة الحائلة بين الجلد والعظم أو لا، الثاني: المتلاحمة والأولى السمحاق. ثم إن أظهرت العظم ولم تنقله، فهي الموضحة وإن نقلت فهي المنقلة إن لم تصل إلى الجلدة التي بين العظم والدماغ، وإن وصلت فهي الآمة، هكذا نقل في "الفتح" عن "الحموي"، وقد ترك فيه ذكر العاشرة، وهي الهاشمة، فاحفظه، فهذه عشر شجاج، وقد ذكر المصنف أحكامها مفصلا، فقال: في الموضحة إلخ. في الموضحة إلخ إن كانت خطأ، وإن كانت عمدا ففيها القصاص أي في الموضحة، وهي التي توضح العظم أي تبينه وتكشفه، نصف عشر الدية؛ لما روي في كتاب عمرو بن حزم الله أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: " في الموضحة خمس من الإبل، وفي الهاشمة عشر، وفي المنقلة خمس عشرة، وفي الآمة - ويروى - المأمومة ثلث الدية رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٢/٢] وفي الهاشمة إلخ وهي التي تهشم العظم أي تكسره عشرها أي عشر الدية، لما روينا. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٢/٢] وفي المنقلة إلخ : وهي التي تنقل العظم بعد الكسر فيها عشر ونصف عشر الدية لما روينا رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٢/٢]
وفي الآمة بتشديد الميم وهي التي تصل إلى أم الدماغ، وأم الدماغ هي الجلدة الرقيقة التي تجمع الدماغ. أو الجائفة ثلثها: أي ثلث الدية الجائفة: وهي التي تكون في الرأس والبطن، بخلاف سائر الشجاج حيث لا تكون إلا في الرأس والوجه، وقيل: لا تتحقق الجائفة فيما فوق الحلق، فلذلك لم تدخل الجائفة في العشرة؛ لأنها لا يطلق عليها الشجة، وإنما ذكرت مع الآمة؛ لاستوائهما في الحكم، قال علي: "في الجائفة ثلث الدية"، وكذلك في الآمة ثلث الدية لما روينا الآن. رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٢/٢]
Book of Diyat. Page 431. Rulings of Shijaj. Chapter on Shijaj. For the mudihah, half a tenth of the diyat; for the hashimah, one-tenth; for the munaqqilah, one-tenth and half a tenth; and for the ammah or ja'ifah, one-third of it, the one that reaches the cavity. Chapter: He made a separate chapter for shijaj due to the many issues, even though they are a type of the less-than-life category. (Fath) Regarding shijaj: shijaj (with kasr) is the plural of shajjah (with fatha), which linguistically is a wound on the face or head. What is elsewhere is called jarahah (wound). So the ruling is based on the reality, i.e., the ruling of shijaj applies to the face and head according to the linguistic reality; because shajjah linguistically is only what is in them. In other places, the fixed amounts for them are not obligatory, rather a discretionary compensation (hukumat al-adl) is obligatory. So if a mudihah occurs on the shin or hand, the fixed compensation is not obligatory for it, because it is a jarahah not a mudihah; rather a discretionary compensation is obligatory, because the fixed amounts are based on (prophetic) specification, and this has only been reported for what is specific to the face and head. And no wound has a known compensation except the ja'ifah, as in al-Zahiriyyah. Know that shijaj are ten: because the shajjah either cuts the skin only or goes beyond it. The first: either blood appears or not; the first (no blood) is al-harisah; the second (blood appears) is either it flows or not; the second (does not flow) is al-dami'ah, and the first (flows) is al-damiyah. What goes beyond: either it cuts the flesh between skin and bone or not; the second (does not cut) is al-badi'ah; the first (cuts) either reveals the thin membrane between skin and bone or not; the second (does not reveal) is al-mutalahimah, and the first is al-simhaq. Then if it exposes the bone but does not move it, it is the mudihah; if it moves it, it is the munaqqilah, provided it does not reach the membrane between bone and brain; if it reaches, it is the ammah. This is transmitted in al-Fath from al-Hamawi. He omitted the tenth, which is the hashimah, so preserve it. So these are ten shijaj. The author has mentioned their rulings in detail, saying: 'For the mudihah, etc.' 'For the mudihah, etc.' if it was accidental; if intentional, then retaliation is due for it. The mudihah is the one that exposes the bone, i.e., makes it appear and uncover it. Half a tenth of the diyat; because it is narrated in the book of 'Amr ibn Hazm that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'In the mudihah, five camels; in the hashimah, ten; in the munaqqilah, fifteen; and in the ammah – and it is also narrated as ma'mumah – one-third of the diyat.' [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/442] 'And in the hashimah etc.': it is the one that crushes the bone, i.e., breaks it; one-tenth, i.e., one-tenth of the diyat, as we have narrated. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/442] 'And in the munaqqilah etc.': it is the one that moves the bone after the fracture; in it is one-tenth and half a tenth of the diyat, as we have narrated. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/442] 'And in the ammah' with tashdid on the mim – it is the one that reaches the umm al-dimagh (mother of the brain), which is the thin membrane that holds the brain. 'Or the ja'ifah': one-third of it, i.e., one-third of the diyat. The ja'ifah is the one that occurs in the head and abdomen, unlike other shijaj which occur only in the head and face. And it is said: the ja'ifah does not occur above the throat, therefore it was not included among the ten, because it is not called shajjah. Rather, it is mentioned alongside the ammah because they are equal in ruling. 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'In the ja'ifah, one-third of the diyat,' and similarly in the ammah, one-third of the diyat, as we have narrated. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/442]
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, forming the beginning of a new chapter (fasl) on shijaj (head and facial wounds) from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq. It first states the fixed diyat amounts for four types of wounds: mudihah (exposing bone) gets half a tenth (i.e., 5 camels out of 100? Actually 'half a tenth' is 0.05 of full diyat? The hadith says 5 camels, which is half a tenth of 100 camels); hashimah (crushing bone) gets one-tenth (10 camels); munaqqilah (displacing bone) gets one-tenth and half a tenth (i.e., 15 camels); and ammah (reaching the brain membrane) or ja'ifah (penetrating the cavity) gets one-third (33.33 camels). The commentary then explains the linguistic definition: shajjah is only for head/face wounds; elsewhere they are called jarahah and have no fixed amounts except ja'ifah. The text then details the ten types of shijaj: starting from the superficial harisah (skin scratch without blood), dami'ah (blood without flow), damiyah (flowing blood), badi'ah (cutting flesh), mutalahimah (cutting deeper flesh), simhaq (reaching the membrane over bone), mudihah (exposing bone), hashimah (crushing bone), munaqqilah (displacing bone), and ammah (reaching brain membrane). The ja'ifah is not counted among the ten as it can occur in the abdomen and is more general. The proofs cited include the famous letter of 'Amr ibn Hazm and the saying of 'Ali (RA). The overall structure is typical of Hanafi fiqh: defining terms, stating rulings, and providing evidence.

Key Terms
شجة (shajjah): A wound specific to the face or head; all other wounds are called jarahah.
موضحة (mudihah): A wound that exposes the bone but does not move it.
آمة (ammah): A wound that reaches the membrane covering the brain (umm al-dimagh).
جائفة (ja'ifah): A wound that penetrates into the cavity of the head or abdomen.

Key Takeaway
A shajjah is strictly a head/facial wound; precise classification determines both the fixed diyat amounts and whether qisas applies.

Fixed Diyat for Major Head Wounds
Fixed diyat rulings for major head wounds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fixed diyat amounts for mudihah, hashimah, munaqqilah, ammah, and ja'ifah, and explain the Hadith evidence and the ruling of Ali (RA).

Core Idea
Five camels for mudihah, ten for hashimah, fifteen for munaqqilah, one-third of full diyat for ammah and ja'ifah.

This section provides the core ruling on diyat for the most significant head wounds. After defining the ten types, the author specifies the fixed compensation for four major categories: mudihah, hashimah, munaqqilah, and ammah/ja'ifah. The amounts are derived from the famous letter of Amr ibn Hazm and the verdict of Ali (RA). Understanding these fixed amounts is essential for judges and muftis when adjudicating accidental wounding cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four/five wound types with fixed diyat
Mudihah (exposes bone), hashimah (crushes bone), munaqqilah (displaces bone), ammah (reaches brain membrane), and ja'ifah (penetrates cavity). The first four are from the ten shijaj; ja'ifah is included though not a shajjah.
Note that the diyat for ammah and ja'ifah is the same (one-third), so they are often mentioned together.
2
Recall the diyat amounts
Mudihah: half a tenth (5 camels). Hashimah: one-tenth (10 camels). Munaqqilah: one-tenth + half a tenth (15 camels). Ammah/Ja'ifah: one-third (33 1/3 camels). These are fractions of the full diyat (100 camels).
The full diyat is 100 camels; fractions are given in the text as 'half a tenth', etc.
3
Understand the evidence
The Prophet (s) said in the letter of Amr ibn Hazm: 'In the mudihah, five camels; in the hashimah, ten; in the munaqqilah, fifteen; in the ammah, one-third of the diyat.' Ali (RA) also said the same for ja'ifah. These are ahad hadith but accepted by the Hanafi school.
The evidence is considered zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalalah in meaning.
4
Distinguish between accidental and intentional
The text says 'if it was accidental' (خطأ) these amounts apply. If intentional, retaliation (qisas) is possible for wounds that have specific measurements (like mudihah) as per the principle of equality in qisas.
The passage briefly mentions 'إذا كانت خطأ' implying the fixed diyat is for accidents.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given an accidental wound described as 'the bone is crushed and pieces are displaced' (munaqqilah), the diyat is 15 camels. Confirm the wound type, check if it is intentional, and derive the ruling.
Always verify that the wound is on the head/face, as per the definition in the previous lesson.

وفي الآمة أو الجائفة ثلثها

فصل: عقد للشجاج فصلا على حدة لكثرة مسائلها، وإن كانت نوعا من أنواع ما دون النفس. (فتح) في الشجاج: الشجاج - بالكسر - جمع شجة بالفتح، وهي في اللغة الجرح يكون في الوجه أو الرأس، وما يكون بغيرها يسمى جراحة، فالحكم مرتب على الحقيقة أي حكم الشجاج يثبت في الوجه والرأس على ما هو حقيقة اللغة؛ لأن الشجة لغة ما كان فيهما لا غير، وفي غيرهما لا يجب المقدر فيهما، بل يجب حكومة عدل، فلو تحققت الموضحة مثلا في نحو الساق واليد لا يجب الأرش المقدر لها؛ لأنها جراحة لا موضحة، بل يجب حكومة عدل؛ لأن التقدير بالتوقيف، وهذا إنما ورد في ما يختص بالوجه والرأس، ولا شيء من الجراح لها أرش معلوم إلا الجائفة كما في "الظهيرية".
واعلم أن الشجاج عشرة؛ لأن الشجة إما أن تقطع الجلد فقط، أو تزيد عليه، والأولى إما أن يظهر فيها دم أو لا، الأولى الحارصة، والثانية إما أن تسيل أو لا، الثاني: الدامعة والأول: الدامية، وما يزيد إما أن يقطع اللحم الذي بينه وبين العظم أو لا، الثاني: الباضعة والأول: إما أن يظهر القطع الجلدة الرقيقة الحائلة بين الجلد والعظم أو لا، الثاني: المتلاحمة والأولى السمحاق. ثم إن أظهرت العظم ولم تنقله، فهي الموضحة وإن نقلت فهي المنقلة إن لم تصل إلى الجلدة التي بين العظم والدماغ، وإن وصلت فهي الآمة، هكذا نقل في "الفتح" عن "الحموي"، وقد ترك فيه ذكر العاشرة، وهي الهاشمة، فاحفظه، فهذه عشر شجاج، وقد ذكر المصنف أحكامها مفصلا، فقال: في الموضحة إلخ. في الموضحة إلخ إن كانت خطأ، وإن كانت عمدا ففيها القصاص أي في الموضحة، وهي التي توضح العظم أي تبينه وتكشفه، نصف عشر الدية؛ لما روي في كتاب عمرو بن حزم الله أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: " في الموضحة خمس من الإبل، وفي الهاشمة عشر، وفي المنقلة خمس عشرة، وفي الآمة - ويروى - المأمومة ثلث الدية رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٢/٢] وفي الهاشمة إلخ وهي التي تهشم العظم أي تكسره عشرها أي عشر الدية، لما روينا. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٢/٢] وفي المنقلة إلخ : وهي التي تنقل العظم بعد الكسر فيها عشر ونصف عشر الدية لما روينا رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٢/٢]
وفي الآمة بتشديد الميم وهي التي تصل إلى أم الدماغ، وأم الدماغ هي الجلدة الرقيقة التي تجمع الدماغ. أو الجائفة ثلثها: أي ثلث الدية الجائفة: وهي التي تكون في الرأس والبطن، بخلاف سائر الشجاج حيث لا تكون إلا في الرأس والوجه، وقيل: لا تتحقق الجائفة فيما فوق الحلق، فلذلك لم تدخل الجائفة في العشرة؛ لأنها لا يطلق عليها الشجة، وإنما ذكرت مع الآمة؛ لاستوائهما في الحكم، قال علي: "في الجائفة ثلث الدية"، وكذلك في الآمة ثلث الدية لما روينا الآن. رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٢/٢]
Book of Diyat. Page 431. Rulings of Shijaj. Chapter on Shijaj. For the mudihah, half a tenth of the diyat; for the hashimah, one-tenth; for the munaqqilah, one-tenth and half a tenth; and for the ammah or ja'ifah, one-third of it, the one that reaches the cavity. Chapter: He made a separate chapter for shijaj due to the many issues, even though they are a type of the less-than-life category. (Fath) Regarding shijaj: shijaj (with kasr) is the plural of shajjah (with fatha), which linguistically is a wound on the face or head. What is elsewhere is called jarahah (wound). So the ruling is based on the reality, i.e., the ruling of shijaj applies to the face and head according to the linguistic reality; because shajjah linguistically is only what is in them. In other places, the fixed amounts for them are not obligatory, rather a discretionary compensation (hukumat al-adl) is obligatory. So if a mudihah occurs on the shin or hand, the fixed compensation is not obligatory for it, because it is a jarahah not a mudihah; rather a discretionary compensation is obligatory, because the fixed amounts are based on (prophetic) specification, and this has only been reported for what is specific to the face and head. And no wound has a known compensation except the ja'ifah, as in al-Zahiriyyah. Know that shijaj are ten: because the shajjah either cuts the skin only or goes beyond it. The first: either blood appears or not; the first (no blood) is al-harisah; the second (blood appears) is either it flows or not; the second (does not flow) is al-dami'ah, and the first (flows) is al-damiyah. What goes beyond: either it cuts the flesh between skin and bone or not; the second (does not cut) is al-badi'ah; the first (cuts) either reveals the thin membrane between skin and bone or not; the second (does not reveal) is al-mutalahimah, and the first is al-simhaq. Then if it exposes the bone but does not move it, it is the mudihah; if it moves it, it is the munaqqilah, provided it does not reach the membrane between bone and brain; if it reaches, it is the ammah. This is transmitted in al-Fath from al-Hamawi. He omitted the tenth, which is the hashimah, so preserve it. So these are ten shijaj. The author has mentioned their rulings in detail, saying: 'For the mudihah, etc.' 'For the mudihah, etc.' if it was accidental; if intentional, then retaliation is due for it. The mudihah is the one that exposes the bone, i.e., makes it appear and uncover it. Half a tenth of the diyat; because it is narrated in the book of 'Amr ibn Hazm that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'In the mudihah, five camels; in the hashimah, ten; in the munaqqilah, fifteen; and in the ammah – and it is also narrated as ma'mumah – one-third of the diyat.' [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/442] 'And in the hashimah etc.': it is the one that crushes the bone, i.e., breaks it; one-tenth, i.e., one-tenth of the diyat, as we have narrated. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/442] 'And in the munaqqilah etc.': it is the one that moves the bone after the fracture; in it is one-tenth and half a tenth of the diyat, as we have narrated. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/442] 'And in the ammah' with tashdid on the mim – it is the one that reaches the umm al-dimagh (mother of the brain), which is the thin membrane that holds the brain. 'Or the ja'ifah': one-third of it, i.e., one-third of the diyat. The ja'ifah is the one that occurs in the head and abdomen, unlike other shijaj which occur only in the head and face. And it is said: the ja'ifah does not occur above the throat, therefore it was not included among the ten, because it is not called shajjah. Rather, it is mentioned alongside the ammah because they are equal in ruling. 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'In the ja'ifah, one-third of the diyat,' and similarly in the ammah, one-third of the diyat, as we have narrated. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/442]
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, forming the beginning of a new chapter (fasl) on shijaj (head and facial wounds) from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq. It first states the fixed diyat amounts for four types of wounds: mudihah (exposing bone) gets half a tenth (i.e., 5 camels out of 100? Actually 'half a tenth' is 0.05 of full diyat? The hadith says 5 camels, which is half a tenth of 100 camels); hashimah (crushing bone) gets one-tenth (10 camels); munaqqilah (displacing bone) gets one-tenth and half a tenth (i.e., 15 camels); and ammah (reaching the brain membrane) or ja'ifah (penetrating the cavity) gets one-third (33.33 camels). The commentary then explains the linguistic definition: shajjah is only for head/face wounds; elsewhere they are called jarahah and have no fixed amounts except ja'ifah. The text then details the ten types of shijaj: starting from the superficial harisah (skin scratch without blood), dami'ah (blood without flow), damiyah (flowing blood), badi'ah (cutting flesh), mutalahimah (cutting deeper flesh), simhaq (reaching the membrane over bone), mudihah (exposing bone), hashimah (crushing bone), munaqqilah (displacing bone), and ammah (reaching brain membrane). The ja'ifah is not counted among the ten as it can occur in the abdomen and is more general. The proofs cited include the famous letter of 'Amr ibn Hazm and the saying of 'Ali (RA). The overall structure is typical of Hanafi fiqh: defining terms, stating rulings, and providing evidence.

Key Terms
شجة (shajjah): A wound specific to the face or head; all other wounds are called jarahah.
موضحة (mudihah): A wound that exposes the bone but does not move it.
آمة (ammah): A wound that reaches the membrane covering the brain (umm al-dimagh).
جائفة (ja'ifah): A wound that penetrates into the cavity of the head or abdomen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) One-third of full diyat

Key Takeaway
Five head wound types have fixed diyat: mudihah (5), hashimah (10), munaqqilah (15), ammah/ja'ifah (33.33); these are wajib in accidental cases and supported by ahad hadith and companion saying.

Diyat — Blood Money
beginner
