Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
10 min
Inclusion of Mudihah Compensation in Diyah for Loss of Faculties
Ruling with proof on inclusion of wound compensation in diyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when arsh al-mudihah is included in diyah for loss of faculties and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Arsh al-mudihah enters diyah only for loss of mind or hair; for other faculties, separate diyah is due according to Abu Hanifah.

This passage from Kitab al-Diyat addresses a nuanced scenario: when a head wound (mudihah) causes loss of a faculty like mind, hearing, or sight, does the fixed compensation for the wound (arsh) merge with the full blood money (diyah) for the lost faculty? The answer depends on which faculty is lost and involves a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the reasoning behind inclusion and exclusion.

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling
Read the opening sentence: if a head wound causes loss of mind or hair, arsh al-mudihah is included in the diyah; if it causes loss of hearing, sight, or speech, it is not included. This is the position of Abu Hanifah.
Note that 'arsh' is fixed at 1/20 of full diyah (5 camels), while 'diyah' is 100 camels (or equivalent).
2
Identify the Proofs
The passage mentions two proofs: (1) reasoning: loss of mind nullifies all limb benefits, so the arsh is subsumed; loss of hair stems from the same cause as the wound. (2) A narrated judgment of Caliph Umar (RA) awarding four separate diyas for loss of mind, speech, hearing, and sight from a single blow.
The Umar narration is a dalil naqli (transmitted evidence) supporting non-inclusion for multiple faculties.
3
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifah includes only mind and hair. Abu Yusuf includes hearing and speech but not sight. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) generally exclude all faculties except mind (some reports). Zufar excludes all.
The dispute hinges on whether each faculty is a 'principal benefit' (asl bi nafsihi) or dependent on the mind.
4
Understand the Thamarah (Practical Consequence)
If a wound causes loss of both mind and hearing: under Abu Hanifah, only one diyah (for mind) is due; under the Sahibayn, two diyas (one for mind, one for hearing) are due. This affects the total compensation amount.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is that of Abu Hanifah, as supported by the majority of later Hanafi scholars.
5
Apply the Principle to New Cases
The passage also provides a general rule: if a single injury destroys two things in the same limb, the lesser compensation is included in the greater. If it affects two limbs, each gets its own arsh. Test this with scenarios like a cut finger causing paralysis of the hand.
This principle is used to analogize other similar cases.

Book of Blood Money. Rulings on head wounds: with regard to vision, movement, and speech, a just assessment. If a man is wounded on the head and thereby loses his mind or the hair of his head, the compensation (arsh) for the clear cranial wound is included in the full blood money (diyah). But if he loses his hearing, sight, or speech, it is not included. If he inflicts a clear cranial wound, (the ruling) regarding the eye, the penis, and the tongue: intentionally, and speech i.e., regarding the tongue, such that he does not cry out as in al-Khaniyyah. So full diyah is obligatory for a minor if he cries out; if he does not cry out, then a just assessment (hukumat al-adl) applies. In al-Zayla‘i there is something contrary to this, and the conclusion is that crying out is like speech in requiring full diyah, according to what is in some [versions] of al-Khaniyyah. Al-Zayla‘i distinguished by saying that crying out is not speech but mere sound, and knowledge of its health is through speech. (Fath) 'Hukumat al-adl': it is in the nominative as the subject, and its predicate is advanced, i.e., his statement: 'for the supernumerary finger and what follows is coordinated with it, i.e., for all the four mentioned there is a just assessment. As for the supernumerary finger, because it is a part of a human, compensation is obligatory for it as an honor, even if there is no benefit or adornment in it, like a supernumerary tooth. Retaliation (qisas) is not obligatory for it, even if the cutter has a supernumerary finger, because equality between them is not known except by conjecture. When qisas is prevented due to doubt, its arsh is obligatory. It has no estimated arsh in the Shari‘ah, so a just assessment is obligatory. As for the remaining ones, because the purpose of these limbs is their benefits, so if the existence of benefit is unknown, the full diyah is not obligatory due to doubt, so a just assessment is obligatory. According to the three (other imams), full diyah is obligatory unless it is known that they are not sound. And if the soundness of these limbs is known, its ruling is the ruling of an adult in cases of error and intentionality, if that is established by evidence or by the confession of the offender. If he denies and no evidence is established against him, the statement is the statement of the offender. Similarly, if he says: 'I do not know its soundness, full arsh is not obligatory upon him except with evidence.' And like the mention of a minor is the mention of a eunuch and an impotent man in ruling and in dispute. (Fath 'Ayni, Mulla Miskin) 'Arsh al-mudihah' [i.e., the blood money of what is lost from it, so only the diyah is obligatory (Ta'i)] because with the loss of the mind, the benefit of all limbs becomes invalid. So it becomes as if he wounded him to the bone (awdahahu) and he died. And the arsh of the mudihah is obligatory for the loss of part of the hair, so much so that if it grows back, it is dropped. And the diyah is obligatory for the loss of the hair. And they are connected, i.e., the arsh of the mudihah and the diyah, by a single cause. So the part enters into the whole, like if a man's finger is cut and his hand becomes paralyzed. The conclusion is that when an injury occurs to a single limb and destroys two things, and the arsh of one is greater, the lesser is included in it. There is no difference between intentional and accidental. If it occurs to two limbs, it is not included, and for each one its arsh is obligatory, whether intentional or accidental, according to Abu Hanifah, because qisas is dropped by it according to him. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), qisas is obligatory for the first if it was intentional and possible to execute; otherwise, it is as Abu Hanifah said. Zufar said: the arsh of limbs is not included in one another. (Fath, 'Ayni) 'No': i.e., the arsh of the mudihah is not included in the arsh of any of these things according to the two. According to Abu Yusuf, it is included in the diyah of hearing and speech, but not included in the diyah of sight, because it is apparent and thus not attached to the mind. As for hearing and speech, they are hidden, so they are attached to the mind, thus the arsh of the mudihah enters into them just as it enters into the arsh of the mind. According to the two (Sahibayn), each of these benefits is a principal in itself, so it does not enter. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/444) And in al-Fath, in explaining their madhhab, he said: Because they are like different limbs, unlike the mind because its benefit returns to the whole. And it is narrated that 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) judged in the case of one man (who struck another on the head causing loss of mind, speech, hearing, and sight) awarding four full diyahs.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) and an intra-Hanafi dispute. It begins by stating the general ruling: if a head wound (shajjah) causes loss of mind (aql) or hair, the compensation for the wound (arsh al-mudihah) is included (dakhala) in the full diyah. If it causes loss of hearing, sight, or speech, it is not included. The reason is that the mind and hair are considered part of the whole, whereas the other faculties are separate. The commentary by al-Fath explains that the loss of mind nullifies the benefit of all limbs, so the wound compensation is subsumed. The text then discusses the case of a minor: if he cries out after the wound, full diyah is due; if not, a just assessment (hukumat al-adl). There is a dispute with al-Zayla‘i. Next, the term 'hukumat al-adl' is defined: it applies to cases like a supernumerary finger or tooth, where no fixed arsh exists. The commentary notes that for such parts, a just assessment is made, and that the three other imams (Shafi‘i, Maliki, Hanbali) hold that full diyah is due unless the defect is known. The principle is then established: when an injury affects one limb and destroys two things, the lesser compensation is included in the greater. If it affects two limbs, each gets its own arsh. This is the position of Abu Hanifah; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that if the first injury was intentional, qisas is due for it, otherwise arsh. Zufar holds that they are never included. Finally, a report of 'Umar (RA) is cited as proof: he awarded four diyas for a single injury that caused loss of mind, speech, hearing, and sight, implying non-inclusion for multiple faculties.

Key Terms
شجاج (shijaj): Head wounds that reach the bone; plural of shajjah.
أرش الموضحة (arsh al-mudihah): Compensation for a wound that lays bare the bone (mudihah).
حكومة عدل (hukumat al-adl): A just assessment by a judge to determine compensation for injuries without fixed arsh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifah, if a head wound (mudihah) causes loss of hearing, what is the total compensation?
A) One full diyah (100 camels) only.
B) One full diyah (100 camels) plus arsh of mudihah (5 camels).
C) Two full diyas (200 camels) plus arsh.
D) Only arsh of mudihah (5 camels).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the wound compensation (arsh al-mudihah) is included in the full diyah only when the head wound causes loss of mind or hair; for other faculties, separate compensation is required.

Injury to Multiple Body Parts: Inclusion and Qisas in Hanafi Law
Rulings on compensation when injury to one member affects another, with the principle of inclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between injuries to distinct limbs, non-distinct limbs, and a single limb with multiple effects, and state whether qisas or arsh is due according to Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
For injuries to one limb or two non-distinct limbs, Abu Hanifah bars qisas and requires arsh; the Sahibayn allow qisas for the first injury.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq lays out the Hanafi rules for compensation when an injury affects multiple body parts or causes additional damage. The key legal question is whether the injured parts are considered distinct (mutabayin) or non-distinct, and whether the injury is to one limb causing two effects. The passage also presents an important intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifah and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cases listed
The passage begins with several injury scenarios: loss of both eyes, cut finger paralyzing another, cut top joint paralyzing rest, broken half tooth with discoloration. Note that Abu Hanifah says no qisas in any of these.
These are the instances where the principle of inclusion will be applied.
2
Understand the Sahibayn's exception
For a mudihah (scalp wound) that also causes loss of eyes, and for a cut finger that paralyzes another, the Sahibayn require qisas for the first injury and arsh for the second.
This dispute centers on whether the injuries are considered one unit or separate.
3
Extract the general principle
The text provides an asl (principle): if injury is to two truly distinct parts (like hand and foot), arsh of one does not prevent qisas of the other (consensus). If injury is to one part causing two effects (like wound causing loss of sight), arsh of one effect prevents qisas of the other. If injury is to two non-distinct parts (like finger paralyzing neighbor), Abu Hanifah says it prevents qisas, Sahibayn say it does not.
This principle is decisive for determining the compensation structure.
4
Apply to single-limb cases
For a single limb where the remaining part has no benefit, only one arsh is due. If benefit remains, arsh for lost part plus just assessment (hukumat al-adl) for the remainder.
The benefit of the remaining part determines whether a separate assessment is needed.
5
Note the consensus on half tooth
Breaking half a tooth causing discoloration of the rest necessitates full diyah of the tooth by consensus.
This illustrates the rule for a single limb with two effects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الديات ٤٣٥ أحكام الشجاج فذهب عيناه، أو قطع إصبعه، فشلت أخرى، أو المفصل الأعلى، فشل ما بقي، عمداً أي إصبع أخرى قطع المفصل من الأصابع منها أو كل اليد أو كسر نصف سنه فاسود ما بقي فلا ،قود، وإن قلع سنه، فنبت مثل أو أصفر أو احمر أو اخضر مكانها أخرى سقط الأرش، وإن أقيد، فنبت سن الأول، يجب، وإن شج رجلا، أي من أخرى أي اقتص من القاطع أي الرجل الأول فالتحم ولم يبق له أثر ، أو ضرب فجرح فبرء وذهب أثره، أي اندمل الجرح ونبت الشعر فلو بقي فحكومة عدل فلا قود: أي فلا قصاص في الوجوه المذكورة كلها عند أبي حنيفة مطلقا، وقالا يجب القصاص في الموضحة، والدية في العين فيما إذا شجه ،موضحة فذهبت عيناه، وكذا إذا قطع إصبعا، فشلت أخرى بجنسها يقتص للأولى، ويجب الأرش للأخرى، وعنده : لما لم يجب القصاص في العضوين يجب الأرش كل واحد منهما كاملا، وإن كان عضوا واحدا بأن قطع الاصبع من المفصل الأعلى فشل ما بقي منها يكتفي بأرش واحد إن لم ينتفع بما بقي، وإن كان ينتفع به تجب دية المقطوع، وتجب حكومة عدل في الباقي بالإجماع، وكذا إذا كسر نصف السن، فاسود ما بقي أو اصفر أو احمر، تجب دية السن كله بالإجماع. والأصل: أن الجناية متى وقعت على محلين متباينين حقيقة كاليد والرجل فأرش أحدهما لا يمنع قود الآخر بالاتفاق، ومتى وقعت على محل واحد وأتلفت شيئين كموضحة أزالت عقله أو سمعه أو بصره أو نطقه، فإن عضوا واحدا كما إذا قطع المفصل الأعلى من الإصبع فشل ما بقي أو كسر نصف السن، فاسود ما بقي يمنع أرش أحدهما قود الآخر، وإذا كانا عضوين غير متباينين كإصبع شلّ جاره يمنع عنده لا عندهما، فعنده: لا يجب القصاص بل يجب أرش كل واحد منهما، وعندهما يجب القصاص مع وجوب المال. (عيني، رد المحتار)
Book of Blood Money. Rulings on head wounds. So if his eyesight is lost, or he cuts his finger and another becomes paralyzed, or the top joint (of a finger) so the rest becomes paralyzed, intentionally. (i.e., another finger; cutting the joint from the fingers, whether from them or the whole hand, or breaking half a tooth so that the rest becomes black, then no qisas.) And if he pulls out a tooth and a similar one grows, or yellow, or red, or green in its place, the arsh drops. And if qisas is executed and the tooth of the first grows back, it is obligatory (to return the arsh? Actually the text says 'يجب' meaning something is obligatory). And if a man is wounded (on the head) i.e., from another, i.e., qisas is executed from the cutter, i.e., the first man, and it healed and no trace remained, or if he struck and it caused a wound and it healed and its trace disappeared, i.e., the wound scabbed over and hair grew, so if something remained, then a just assessment. Then no qisas: i.e., no retaliation in all the mentioned cases according to Abu Hanifah absolutely. The two (Sahibayn) said: qisas is obligatory in the mudihah, and diyah for the eye when he wounds him with a mudihah and both eyes are lost. Similarly, if he cuts a finger and another becomes paralyzed of its type, qisas is executed for the first, and arsh is obligatory for the other. According to him (Abu Hanifah): since qisas is not obligatory for two limbs, the arsh for each is complete. If it is one limb, such as cutting the finger from the top joint so the rest becomes paralyzed, one arsh suffices if the remainder is of no benefit; if benefit remains, then the diyah of the cut part is obligatory, and a just assessment for the remainder, by consensus. Similarly, if he breaks half a tooth and the rest becomes black, yellow, or red, the diyah of the entire tooth is obligatory by consensus. The principle: when an injury occurs to two truly distinct places like hand and foot, the arsh of one does not prevent qisas for the other, by agreement. When it occurs to one place and destroys two things, like a mudihah that removes his mind, hearing, sight, or speech, then it is one limb, like if he cuts the top joint of the finger and the rest becomes paralyzed, or breaks half a tooth and the rest becomes black, the arsh of one prevents qisas for the other. If they are two non-distinct limbs, like a finger that paralyzes its neighbor, it prevents (qisas) according to him (Abu Hanifah) but not according to the two (Sahibayn). According to him: qisas is not obligatory but the arsh of each is obligatory; according to them: qisas is obligatory along with monetary compensation. ('Ayni, Radd al-Muhtar)
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage provides rulings on injuries affecting multiple body parts, with detailed intra-Hanafi disputes. It begins by listing cases: loss of both eyes, cutting a finger causing another to become paralyzed, cutting the top joint of a finger causing the rest to become paralyzed, breaking half a tooth causing discoloration of the remainder, and pulling out a tooth with regrowth (the last is elaborated later). For all these, Abu Hanifah says no qisas (retaliation) is due; instead, compensation (arsh) is paid for each injury. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ: they require qisas for the mudihah if intentional and possible, and diyah for the eyes. The commentary then clarifies the principle: when injury is to two truly distinct parts (e.g., hand and foot), the arsh of one does not prevent qisas for the other, by consensus. When injury is to one part causing two effects (e.g., wound causing loss of mind), the compensation for one effect prevents qisas for the other. When the two parts are not truly distinct (e.g., two fingers where one's injury disables the other), Abu Hanifah holds that qisas is not due but each gets arsh, while the Sahibayn hold that qisas is due for the first plus arsh for the second. The text also specifies that for a single limb where the remaining part has no benefit, only one arsh is due; if benefit remains, arsh for the lost part plus just assessment for the remainder. For broken half-tooth with discoloration, full diyah of the tooth is due by consensus.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for bodily injury; e.g., cutting the limb that was cut.
شلت (shallat): To become paralyzed or disabled; loss of function.
حكومة عدل (hukumat al-adl): A just assessment by a judge for compensation when no fixed amount exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifah, if a person intentionally cuts another's finger and, as a result, an adjacent finger becomes paralyzed, what is the ruling?
A) Qisas for the cut finger, arsh for the paralyzed finger.
B) No qisas; arsh for both fingers.
C) Qisas for both injuries.
D) Full diyah for the entire hand.

Key Takeaway
When injury affects two non-distinct limbs or one limb in two ways, Abu Hanifah bars qisas and requires arsh for each injury; the Sahibayn allow qisas for the first injury if possible.

Tooth Extraction with Regrowth: Dropping of Arsh
Ruling on arsh when a pulled tooth regrows perfectly or partially

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on arsh when a perfectly regrown tooth returns, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A perfectly regrown tooth nullifies the injury — no arsh is due, but partial or crooked regrowth still requires compensation.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in the chapter of diyat: what happens when a tooth that was forcibly extracted grows back? Does the original injury still demand compensation? The Hanafi school has an internal difference, and the ruling touches on the deeper principle that an injury that effectively disappears also removes the liability for arsh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is tooth extraction. According to Abu Hanifah, if a perfect tooth grows back, arsh is dropped. The Sahibayn say full arsh remains.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites consensus on minors as the primary proof. If a minor's extracted tooth regrows, no compensation is due by consensus.
Consensus is a strong proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The consensus shows that the injury is nullified when the tooth regrows perfectly. The same principle applies to adults by analogy (qiyas).
The illa is the restoration of the injury.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Sahibayn argue that the extraction was a completed injury that already obligated arsh; regrowth is a separate blessing from Allah, not invalidating the original liability.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the madhhab.
5
Determine the tarjih
The text presents Abu Hanifah's view as the primary position, supported by the consensus for minors. This is the mufta bihi position.
The relied-upon view is that of Abu Hanifah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قلع سنه إلخ : أي إن قلع رجل سن رجل، فنبتت مكان السن المقلوعة سن أخرى، سقط الأرش عن القالع عند أبي حنيفة وقالا عليه الأرش كاملا؛ لأن الجناية وقعت موجبة له والتي نبتت نعمة مبتدأة من تعالى، وله: أن الجناية قد زالت معنى، ولهذا لو قلع من صبي فنبتت مكانها أخرى لا يلزمه شيء بالإجماع، هذا إذا نبتت مثل الأولى، وإن نبتت معوجة فعليه حكومة عدل عند أبي حنيفة ولو نبتت إلى النصف فعليه نصف الأرش. رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٥/٢] الله يجب إلخ: معناه: إذا قلع رجل سن رجل، فاقتص من القالع ثم نبتت من الأول أي المقتص له، يجب عليه أي على المقتص له أرش من المقتص منه، وهو القالع الأول؛ لأنه تبين أنه استوفى بغير حق؛ لأن الموجب فساد المنبت ولم يفسد حيث نبتت مكانها أخرى، فانعدمت الجناية، ولهذا يستنظر حولا، وفي "التتمة : والصحيح أنه يستنظر في سن البالغ حتى يبرأ؛ لأن نباته نادر فلا يفيد تأجيله إلى سنة، فيؤخر إلى البرئ ليعلم عاقبته [ رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٥/٢]
And if he pulls out a tooth etc.: i.e., if a man pulls out a man's tooth, and another tooth grows in the place of the extracted tooth, the arsh is dropped from the extractor according to Abu Hanifah. The two (Sahibayn) said: full arsh is due upon him, because the injury occurred requiring it, and what grew is a new blessing from Allah. According to him (Abu Hanifah): the injury has been nullified in effect, and for this reason, if he pulls from a minor and another grows in its place, nothing is due by consensus. This applies if it grows like the first; if it grows crooked, then a just assessment upon him according to Abu Hanifah. If it grows to half, then half the arsh. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/445) 'Allah must be' etc.: meaning, if a man pulls out a man's tooth, and then qisas is executed from the extractor, then the tooth of the first (i.e., the person on whose behalf qisas was executed) grows back, it is obligatory upon him (i.e., the person on whose behalf qisas was executed) to pay arsh to the extractor, because it becomes clear that he exacted retaliation without right, since the cause (corruption of the root) did not materialize as the tooth grew back, so the injury is nullified. For this reason, a year's wait is observed. In al-Tatimmah: the correct view is that for an adult's tooth, one waits until it heals, because its growth is rare, so deferring for a year is not beneficial; rather, delay until healing to know its outcome. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/445)
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on tooth extraction with regrowth, including an intra-Hanafi dispute and a later discussion on qisas. The core ruling: if a pulled tooth grows back naturally, the arsh (compensation) is dropped according to Abu Hanifah, because the injury is effectively undone. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say full arsh is still due, because the extraction was a completed injury and the regrowth is a separate blessing. Abu Hanifah supports his view with the consensus that for a minor's tooth, no compensation is due if it regrows. If the regrown tooth is crooked, a just assessment is due. If it grows only halfway, half the arsh is due. The passage then discusses a scenario where qisas was executed: if the victim's tooth grows back after he had qisas performed on the perpetrator, then he must pay arsh to the perpetrator because the qisas was based on the assumption of permanent loss, which turned out false. In such a case, a waiting period of one year (or until healing) is observed to determine if the tooth will regrow. The correct view, per al-Tatimmah, is to wait for the adult's tooth until it heals (not a full year), as regrowth is rare.

Key Terms
قلع السن (qal' al-sinn): Extraction of a tooth; a specific type of injury.
نبات (nabaat): Regrowth of a tooth after extraction.
أرش (arsh): Fixed compensation for bodily injuries, akin to diyat.
حكومة عدل (hukumat al-adl): An equitable assessment of compensation determined by a just arbitrator when no fixed amount exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifah, if a person pulls out another's tooth and a perfectly similar tooth grows in its place, what is the ruling on arsh?
A) Full arsh is due.
B) No arsh is due.
C) Half arsh is due.
D) A just assessment is due.

Key Takeaway
Natural perfect restoration of an injury nullifies compensation; imperfect restoration requires proportional compensation.

Qisas for Tooth Extraction: The Effect of Regrowth and the Waiting Period
Ruling on qisas for tooth extraction and the waiting period for regrowth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling when a tooth regrows after qisas was executed, and state the waiting period (istizhar) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
If a tooth regrows after qisas, the victim must compensate the perpetrator because the injury was not permanent; a waiting period of up to a year (or until healing) is observed.

This lesson extends the previous discussion: what if the victim's tooth grows back after he has already had the perpetrator's tooth pulled in retaliation (qisas)? The author explains that the original victim must now pay arsh to the perpetrator, because the basis for qisas (permanent loss) turned out to be false. The passage also clarifies the correct waiting period to determine if a tooth will regrow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A man pulls another's tooth. Then qisas is executed on the perpetrator (his tooth is pulled). Later, the victim's tooth regrows.
2
State the ruling
The original victim must pay arsh to the perpetrator because the qisas was based on a false assumption of permanent loss.
The ruling is clear: wajib (obligatory).
3
Understand the reasoning
The basis for qisas was the corruption of the root (fasad al-munbat). Since the tooth regrew, the root was not permanently corrupted, so the qisas was unjustified.
The injury is considered nullified.
4
Note the waiting period
A waiting period (istizhar) of one year is generally prescribed to determine if the tooth will regrow.
This is to ascertain the outcome before finalizing any compensation.
5
Recognize the refinement from al-Tatimmah
For adults, regrowth is rare, so the correct view is to wait until healing (al-buru'), not necessarily a full year.
This refinement makes the rule more practical.

When Qisas is Not Due: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Head Wounds
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas for mawdihah with eye loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that determines when qisas is replaced by arsh for head wounds and identify the practical difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Qisas is not due when one injury destroys two functions on a single limb.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the liability for head wounds. The key issue is whether qisas (retaliation) is due when a single blow causes both a mawdihah (wound exposing bone) and the loss of an eye. The ruling hinges on the legal principle of mahall (locus): is the injury considered one place or two?

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed scenario
The dispute arises when an aggressor strikes the victim's head, creating a mawdihah that also causes loss of sight in both eyes. Determine what each party argues for qisas and compensation.
This scenario is the classic point of ikhtilaf.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his rationale
Abu Hanifa holds that no qisas is due; instead, full arsh (fixed compensation) must be paid for each lost function (the mawdihah and the eyes). His rationale: both injuries arise from one act on one place (the head), so the arsh for one function prevents qisas for the other.
He considers the head as a single mahall.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their rationale
The Sahibayn hold that qisas is due for the mawdihah (since it is a wound on the head) and diyah (blood money) for the eyes, treating them as separate injuries. They view the mawdihah and the eye damage as occurring on distinct mahalls.
They separate the wound from the sensory loss.
4
Apply the general principle to other cases
The passage generalizes: if injury is on two truly separate limbs (like hand and leg), arsh of one does NOT prevent qisas of the other. If it is on one limb destroying two functions (like a finger cut causing paralysis of the remaining part), then arsh of one prevents qisas.
Intermediate cases, like a finger that paralyzes its neighbor, are disputed.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
Under Abu Hanifa, the aggressor faces no physical retaliation but must pay full compensation for each loss. Under the Sahibayn, the aggressor would suffer qisas for the mawdihah (a wound on the head) and also pay diyah for the eyes.
This shows that the classification of mahall directly affects the penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام الشجاج
فذهب عيناه، أو قطع إصبعه، فشلت أخرى، أو المفصل الأعلى، فشل ما بقي، عمداً أي إصبع أخرى قطع المفصل من الأصابع منها أو كل اليد أو كسر نصف سنه فاسود ما بقي فلا قود، وإن قلع سنه، فنبت مكانها أخرى سقط الأرش، وإن أقيد، فنبت سن الأول، يجب، وإن شج رجلا، أي من أخرى أي اقتص من القاطع أي الرجل الأول فالتحم ولم يبق له أثر، أو ضرب فجرح فبرء وذهب أثره، أي اندمل الجرح ونبت الشعر فلو بقي فحكومة عدل
فلا قود: أي فلا قصاص في الوجوه المذكورة كلها عند أبي حنيفة مطلقا، وقالا يجب القصاص في الموضحة، والدية في العين فيما إذا شجه موضحة فذهبت عيناه، وكذا إذا قطع إصبعا، فشلت أخرى بجنسها يقتص للأولى، ويجب الأرش للأخرى، وعنده: لما لم يجب القصاص في العضوين يجب الأرش كل واحد منهما كاملا، وإن كان عضوا واحدا بأن قطع الاصبع من المفصل الأعلى فشل ما بقي منها يكتفي بأرش واحد إن لم ينتفع بما بقي، وإن كان ينتفع به تجب دية المقطوع، وتجب حكومة عدل في الباقي بالإجماع، وكذا إذا كسر نصف السن، فاسود ما بقي أو اصفر أو احمر، تجب دية السن كله بالإجماع. والأصل: أن الجناية متى وقعت على محلين متباينين حقيقة كاليد والرجل فأرش أحدهما لا يمنع قود الآخر بالاتفاق، ومتى وقعت على محل واحد وأتلفت شيئين كموضحة أزالت عقله أو سمعه أو بصره أو نطقه، فإن عضوا واحدا كما إذا قطع المفصل الأعلى من الإصبع فشل ما بقي أو كسر نصف السن، فاسود ما بقي يمنع أرش أحدهما قود الآخر، وإذا كانا عضوين غير متباينين كإصبع شلّ جاره يمنع عنده لا عندهما، فعنده: لا يجب القصاص بل يجب أرش كل واحد منهما، وعندهما يجب القصاص مع وجوب المال. (عيني، رد المحتار)
Rulings of head wounds: Then his two eyes go, or he cuts his finger, then another becomes paralyzed, or the upper joint, then what remains becomes paralyzed, intentionally or any other finger cuts the joint of the fingers from it or the whole hand or breaks half of his tooth then what remains blackens, then no qisas, and if he pulls out his tooth, and another grows in its place, the arsh falls, and if qisas is applied, then the first's tooth grows, it is required, and if he wounds a man, i.e., from another, i.e., he retaliates against the cutter, i.e., the first man, then it heals and no trace remains, or he strikes and wounds and it heals and its trace goes, i.e., the wound closes and hair grows, so if it remains, then the discretionary assessment (hukumat adl). So no qisas: i.e., no retaliation in all the mentioned faces according to Abu Hanifa absolutely, and the two said it is obligatory in the mawdihah, and the diyah for the eye in the case if he wounds him with a mawdihah and his eyes go, and likewise if he cuts a finger, then another becomes paralyzed by its kind, he retaliates for the first, and the arsh is obligatory for the other, and according to him: since qisas is not obligatory for the two limbs, the full arsh is obligatory for each one, and if it is one limb, such as cutting the finger from the upper joint and what remains of it becomes paralyzed, one arsh suffices if the remainder is not useful, and if it is useful, the diyah of the cut part is obligatory, and a hukumat adl is obligatory for the remainder by consensus, and likewise if he breaks half of the tooth, then what remains blackens or yellows or reddens, the diyah of the whole tooth is obligatory by consensus. And the principle is: whenever the injury occurs on two truly distinct places like the hand and the leg, the arsh of one does not prevent the qisas of the other by agreement, and whenever it occurs on one place and destroys two things like a mawdihah that removes his intellect or hearing or sight or speech, then (it is) one limb, as if he cuts the upper joint of the finger and what remains becomes paralyzed, or breaks half of the tooth and what remains blackens, the arsh of one prevents the qisas of the other; and if they are two limbs that are not distinct like a finger that paralyzes its neighbor, he (Abu Hanifa) holds that it prevents, not the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to him (Abu Hanifa): qisas is not obligatory, rather the arsh of each one is obligatory, and according to them (the Sahibayn): qisas is obligatory along with the payment of wealth. (Ayni, Radd al-Muhtar).
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage discusses the rulings on head wounds and injuries, specifically when qisas (retaliation) is not due. It begins by listing various injuries such as loss of eyes, paralysis of other fingers, etc., and states that in all these cases, no qisas is due according to Abu Hanifa. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that qisas is due in the case of a mawdihah (a wound that exposes bone) and diyah for the eye. The dispute centers on whether the injury affects one or two limbs. The principle is explained: if the injury involves two truly separate limbs, the compensation (arsh) for one does not prevent qisas for the other. If the injury is on one limb but destroys two functions (like both sight and hearing in a single wound), then the arsh for one prevents qisas for the other. The Sahibayn consider a mawdihah that destroys both eyes as two separate injuries? Actually the text says they require qisas for the mawdihah and diyah for the eye. The commentary concludes that according to Abu Hanifa, no qisas is due, and full arsh is required for each. For a single limb, one arsh suffices if the remaining part is useless, otherwise diyah for the cut part and hukumat adl for the remainder. The key principle is the concept of mahall (place) and whether the injuries are on one or two distinct places.

Key Terms
شجاج (shijaj): Head wounds, specifically those that reach the bone.
موضحة (mawdihah): A wound that exposes the bone.
حكومة عدل (hukumat adl): Discretionary assessment of compensation when a fixed arsh is not specified.
محل (mahall): The place or locus of the injury; legally relevant for determining whether qisas is due or only arsh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when a mawdihah destroys both eyes, what is the ruling?
A) Qisas is due for the mawdihah; diyah for the eyes.
B) No qisas; full arsh for both the wound and the eyes.
C) Only hukumat adl is required.
D) The offender is exempt because the blow was unintentional.

Key Takeaway
The key principle: if a single injury on one mahall destroys multiple functions, arsh for one prevents qisas for the others; this is disputed within the Hanafi school when the mahall is considered one but functions are separate.

Tooth Extraction and Regrowth: When Does Arsh Fall?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on arsh for tooth regrowth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on tooth extraction with regrowth, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to determine compensation.

Core Idea
A regrown tooth negates the injury for Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn see the injury as complete.

When a tooth is pulled and a new one grows, the question arises: is the aggressor still liable for compensation? This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding their different reasoning is key to applying Hanafi diyat law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the core issue
The act is qal' sin (tooth extraction). The core issue is whether arsh is owed if a tooth regrows perfectly.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa holds no arsh because the injury has ceased in meaning; consensus on a child's case supports this.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold full arsh because the injury was complete; regrowth is a new blessing from Allah.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa argues that the injury's effect is undone by regrowth; the text emphasizes this with 'zalat ma'nan' (ceased in meaning).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and variations
Perfect regrowth: no arsh (Abu Hanifa) vs full arsh (Sahibayn). Imperfect regrowth: hukumat adl or half arsh under Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قلع سنه إلخ : أي إن قلع رجل سن رجل، فنبتت مكان السن المقلوعة سن أخرى، سقط الأرش عن القالع عند أبي حنيفة وقالا عليه الأرش كاملا؛ لأن الجناية وقعت موجبة له والتي نبتت نعمة مبتدأة من تعالى، وله: أن الجناية قد زالت معنى، ولهذا لو قلع من صبي فنبتت مكانها أخرى لا يلزمه شيء بالإجماع، هذا إذا نبتت مثل الأولى، وإن نبتت معوجة فعليه حكومة عدل عند أبي حنيفة ولو نبتت إلى النصف فعليه نصف الأرش. رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٥/٢
الله يجب إلخ: معناه: إذا قلع رجل سن رجل، فاقتص من القالع ثم نبتت من الأول أي المقتص له، يجب عليه أي على المقتص له أرش من المقتص منه، وهو القالع الأول؛ لأنه تبين أنه استوفى بغير حق؛ لأن الموجب فساد المنبت ولم يفسد حيث نبتت مكانها أخرى، فانعدمت الجناية، ولهذا يستنظر حولا، وفي "التتمة : والصحيح أنه يستنظر في سن البالغ حتى يبرأ؛ لأن نباته نادر فلا يفيد تأجيله إلى سنة، فيؤخر إلى البرئ ليعلم عاقبته [ رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٥/٢]
And if he pulls out his tooth etc.: meaning if a man pulls out the tooth of another, and another tooth grows in place of the pulled one, the arsh falls from the extractor according to Abu Hanifa, and the two say the full arsh is due because the injury occurred causing it, and the growing tooth is a new blessing from Allah. And to him (Abu Hanifa): the injury has ceased in meaning, and so if it grows from a child and another grows, nothing is due by consensus. This is if it grows like the first, but if it grows crooked, then hukumat adl according to Abu Hanifa. And if it grows halfway, then half the arsh. Allah: it is required etc.: meaning if a man pulls out the tooth of another, then he retaliates against the extractor, then the tooth of the first (the one who retaliated) grows, then it is required upon him (the one who retaliated) to give arsh to the one from whom he retaliated, because it becomes clear that he took without right; because the cause was the corruption of the growth place and it was not corrupted since another grew in its place, so the injury is nullified. And for this reason he waits a year. And in al-Tatimma: the correct view is to wait in the case of a tooth of an adult until he heals, because its growth is rare, so postponement to a year does not help; thus he postpones until healing to know its outcome.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage deals with the case of tooth extraction where a new tooth grows. According to Abu Hanifa, if a new tooth grows in place of the pulled one, no compensation (arsh) is required because the injury is effectively undone. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the full arsh is due because the injury was complete at the time, and the regrowth is a separate blessing. The text also discusses variations: if the new tooth is crooked, hukumat adl is due; if it grows only halfway, half the arsh. Additionally, if qisas was carried out by pulling the aggressor's tooth and then the victim's tooth regrows, the victim must pay arsh to the aggressor. The passage also mentions that in the case of a child, consensus holds that no arsh is due if a new tooth grows. The correct view according to al-Tatimma is to wait for an adult until healing to determine the final outcome.

Key Terms
قلع سن (qal' sin): Extraction or pulling out of a tooth.
نبات سن (nabat sin): Growth of a new tooth in place of the extracted one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if an adult's tooth is pulled out and a new one grows identical to the original, what is the ruling?
A) Full arsh is due
B) No arsh is due
C) Half arsh is due
D) Hukumat adl is due

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on tooth regrowth shows that the effect of the injury is central: regrowth may nullify compensation.

Postponement of Qisas for Wounds: The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Dispute on timing of qisas for wounds and pain compensation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on postponement of qisas for wounds and explain the Hanafi evidence from hadith and ma'al (outcome consideration), distinguishing it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Qisas for a wound must wait until healing because it may turn fatal.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rule that qisas for a wound cannot be executed immediately; one must wait until the wound heals. The Shafi'i school disagrees, arguing for immediate execution. We will analyze the prophetic hadith cited by the Hanafis and the rational basis for the delay.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on qisas for wounds
Identify the basic ruling: qisas is not executed for a wound until the victim's wound heals. Note the rationale: the injury might spread to the soul, turning into murder.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and their dalil
State that al-Shafi'i holds immediate execution is valid because the cause of qisas is already realized, analogizing to qisas for life.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
Examine the hadith prohibition and the principle of ma'al (outcome consideration). Explain how the hadith supports delay and why analogy to life is flawed in the Hanafi view.
The hadith is narrated by Ahmad and al-Daraqutni.
4
Explore the intra-Hanafi dispute on pain compensation
Note that Abu Hanifa held no arsh for pain, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad held for hukumat adl or physician's fee. Understand the basis: benefits are only compensable by contract or its equivalent.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Conclude that in the Hanafi school, qisas is postponed and no pain compensation is due if the wound heals without trace; in the Shafi'i school, qisas is immediate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا أرش ولا قود بجرح حتى يبرأ، وكل عمد سقط قوده بشبهة كقتل الأب ابنه عمدا، فديته في مال القاتل وكذا ما وجب صلحا أو اعترافا أو لم يكن نصف العشر، يجب في مال القاتل من حيث الصلح بقتل الخطأ
فلا أرش أي على الذي شج أو ضرب وهذا قول أبي حنيفة بالله، وقال أبو يوسف له: عليه أرش الألم، وهو حكومة عدل؛ لأن الشين الموجب إن زال فالألم الحاصل لم يزل، وقال محمد الله: أجرة الطبيب؛ لأن ذلك أثر فعله، فكان له أخذ ذلك من ماله، وإعطاؤه الطبيب، وفي "شرح الطحاوي" فسر قول أبي يوسف: عليه أرش الألم بأجرة الطبيب والمداواة، فعلى هذا لا اختلاف بين أبي يوسف ومحمد، وبقولهما قال الشافعي وأحمد في رواية، ولأبي حنيفة له: أن الموجب هو الشين الذي يلحقه بفعله وزوال منفعته وقد زال ذلك بزوال أثره، والمنافع لا تتقوم إلا بالعقد كالإجارة الصحيحة أو ما يشبه العقد كالفاسد، ولم يوجد شيء من ذلك في حق الجاني، فلا يلزمه الغرامة، وكذلك مجرد الألم لا يوجب شيئا، ألا ترى أن من ضرب إنسانا ضربا مؤلما من غير جرح، لا يجب عليه شيء من الأرش تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٥١/٩]
ولا قود بجرح لا يقتص عندنا بجرح حتى يبرأ صاحبه وقال الشافعي الله : يقتص منه في الحال؛ لأن الموجب : قد تحقق، فلا يؤخر كما في القصاص في النفس، ولنا ما روي أنه عليها "نهى أن يقتص من جرح حتى يبرأ صاحبه"، رواه أحمد والدار قطني؛ ولأن الجراحات يعتبر فيها مآلها؛ لاحتمال أن تسري إلى النفس، فيظهر أنه قتل، فلا يعلم أنه جرح إلا بالبرء، فيستقر به تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٥١/٩] حتى يبرأ قال في "ملا مسكين": لكن العبارة لا تساعد. قال في "الفتح": أي لا تساعد المراد ؛ لأنه بعد البرء لا يقضي بشيء من قود وأرش، وعبارة المتن يوهم أن القود شرط بالبرء.
نصف العشر: أي يكون الدية في كل من هذه الصور في مال القاتل كما روي عن ابن عباس ما موقوفا ومرفوعا "لا تعقل العاقلة عمدا ولا عبدا ولا صلحا ولا اعترافا، ولأن العاقلة تتحمل تخفيفا عن القاتل، وذلك يليق بالمخطئ، والذي وجب بالصلح وجب بعقده، والعاقلة لا تتحمل إلا ما وجب بالقتل، وكذا ما لزمه بإقراره، وإنما لا تتحمل أقل من نصف عشر الدية؛ لأنه لا يؤدي إلى الإجحاف والاستئصال بالجاني. ثم الكل يجب مؤجلا إلى ثلاث سنين إلا ما وجب بالصلح، فإنه يجب حالا؛ لأنه واجب بالعقد، فيكون حالا بخلاف غيره، وما دون أرش الموضحة يجب في سنة؛ لأنه دون ثلث الدية والثلث وما دونه يجب في سنة وقال الشافعي محله ما وجب بقتل الأب ابنه يجب حالا؛ لأن القصاص سقط شرعا إلى بدل فيكون ذلك البدل حالا كسائر المتلفات ولنا أن المتلف ليس بمال وما ليس بمال لا يضمن بالمال أصلا، وإنما عرفنا تقومه بالمال بالشرع، والشرع إنما قومه بدية مؤجلة إلى ثلاث سنين وإيجاب المال حالا زيادة على ما أوجبه الشرع وصفا، فلا يجوز كما لا يجوز إيجاب الزيادة على ما أوجبه الشرع قدرا تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٥١/٩]
So no arsh and no qisas for a wound until its owner heals, and every intentional act whose qisas falls due to doubt, like a father killing his son intentionally, its diyah is in the wealth of the killer, and likewise what is due by compromise or admission or is less than half a tenth, it is due in the killer's wealth. So no arsh i.e., upon the one who wounded or struck, and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa, by Allah, and Abu Yusuf said: upon him is the arsh of pain, which is hukumat adl, because the defect that necessitates (compensation) if it is removed, the pain that occurred has not been removed, and Muhammad said: the wage of the physician, because that is an effect of his action, so he may take that from his wealth and give it to the physician. And in Sharh al-Tahawi, the saying of Abu Yusuf 'arsh of pain' is interpreted as the wage of the physician and medication, so on this there is no difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i and Ahmad in one narration say the same. And for Abu Hanifa: the cause is the defect that he inflicts upon him and loss of benefit, and that has been removed by the removal of its trace, and benefits are only valued by contract like a valid lease or what resembles a contract like a void one, and nothing of that exists concerning the offender, so he is not liable for guarantee, and similarly mere pain does not necessitate anything. Do you not see that if someone strikes another a painful strike without wounding, nothing of arsh is due upon him. (Takmila al-Bahr al-Raiq 9:151) And no qisas for a wound according to us: qisas is not executed for a wound until its owner heals, and al-Shafi'i said: qisas is executed immediately, because the cause is realized, so it should not be delayed like qisas for life. And for us it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) prohibited qisas for a wound until its owner heals, narrated by Ahmad and al-Daraqutni, and because wounds are considered based on their outcome due to the possibility of their spreading to the soul, so it appears that it is killing, so it is not known that it is a wound except by healing, so it is established by it. (Takmila al-Bahr al-Raiq 9:151) Until he heals: Mulla Miskeen said: but the expression does not help. In al-Fath: it does not help the intended meaning, because after healing nothing of qisas or arsh is decreed, and the wording of the text suggests that qisas is conditioned upon healing. Half a tenth: i.e., the diyah in each of these forms is in the wealth of the killer, as narrated from Ibn Abbas as a mawquf and marfu' hadith: 'The 'agila does not bear the diyah for intentional killing, nor for a slave, nor for a compromise, nor for an admission.' And because the 'agila bears it as a relief for the killer, and that suits the mistaken one, and what is due by compromise is due by his contract, and the 'agila only bears what is due by killing, and likewise what is due by his admission. And the less than half of a tenth is not borne because it does not lead to hardship and ruination of the offender. Then all is deferred to three years except what is due by compromise, for it is due immediately because it is due by contract, so it is immediate unlike others. And what is less than the arsh of a mawdihah is due in one year, because it is less than a third of the diyah. And al-Shafi'i said: his view is that what is due for killing a father by his son is due immediately, because qisas fell legally to a substitute, so that substitute is immediate like other damages. And for us: the damaged thing is not property, and what is not property is not guaranteed by property at all, and we only know its evaluation by law, and the law evaluated it with a diyah deferred to three years, and requiring the wealth immediately would be an increase beyond what the law required in description, so it is not permissible, just as it is not permissible to require an increase beyond what the law required in quantity. (Takmila al-Bahr al-Raiq 9:151)
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage covers two main issues. First, it discusses the postponement of qisas for wounds until healing. The Hanafi school holds that qisas for a wound cannot be carried out immediately; one must wait until the wound heals because it may turn fatal, turning the offense into murder. The Prophet (peace be upon him) is reported to have prohibited qisas for a wound until the owner heals. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that the cause of qisas is already present and should be executed immediately. Second, the passage addresses the liability for diyah in cases where qisas is dropped due to a doubt, such as a father killing his son. In such cases, the diyah is due from the killer's personal wealth, not from the 'agila (family treasury). The same applies to diyah agreed upon by compromise or admission. The diyah is deferred over three years, except for diyah by compromise which is immediate. Al-Shafi'i argues that diyah for a father killed by his son should be immediate, but the Hanafis respond that the original obligation was qisas, which is not considered property, and the substitute is financial compensation deferred as per law. The text also notes a sub-dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf/Muhammad regarding compensation for pain and suffering when the wound heals without trace.

Key Terms
برء (bur'): Healing of a wound; used to determine the final outcome of the injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why must qisas for a wound be postponed?
A) Because the offender needs time to prepare.
B) Because the wound may turn fatal, altering the legal classification.
C) Because the victim must first seek medical treatment.
D) Because the 'aqila must approve.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi law requires postponing qisas for wounds until healing due to uncertainty of outcome and a prophetic prohibition.

Diyat — Blood Money

Diyah Liability from the Killer's Wealth and Deferral Rules
Rules on source of diyah and deferral periods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when diyah is due from the killer's personal wealth rather than the 'aqila, and explain the deferral periods for diyah including exceptions for compromise.

Core Idea
Diyah from killer's wealth for intentional acts with doubt; deferred three years unless by compromise.

This lesson covers the rules of diyah liability when qisas falls due to a doubt (e.g., father killing son) and similar cases. The diyah is borne by the killer's personal wealth, not the 'aqila, and is generally deferred over three years. However, diyah by compromise is immediate. We also examine the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi justification for deferral.

Guided Path
1
Identify cases where diyah is from killer's wealth
List the four cases mentioned: (1) intentional act where qisas falls due to doubt (e.g., father killing son), (2) diyah by compromise (sulh), (3) diyah by admission, (4) diyah for injuries less than half a tenth.
2
Explain the rationale for excluding the 'aqila
The 'aqila only bears diyah as a relief for the killer in accidental cases. Intentional acts with doubt, compromise, and admission are not accidental, so the killer himself is liable.
Also note the hadith: 'لا تعقل العاقلة عمدا ولا عبدا ولا صلحا ولا اعترافا'
3
Understand the deferral periods
General rule: diyah is deferred over three years. Exception: diyah by compromise is due immediately because it is a contractual obligation. Also, arsh less than the arsh of a mawdihah (less than a third of diyah) is due in one year.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Al-Shafi'i argues that diyah for a father killing his son should be immediate because qisas is replaced by a substitute, which should be due immediately like other damages. Hanafis respond: the original right was qisas, not property; the substitute is a legal compensation deferred as per law.
5
Apply the rules to a hypothetical
Given a scenario, determine whether diyah is from killer's wealth, whether it is immediate or deferred, and whether the 'aqila shares any liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

فلا أرش أي على الذي شج أو ضرب وهذا قول أبي حنيفة بالله، وقال أبو يوسف له: عليه أرش الألم، وهو حكومة عدل؛ لأن الشين الموجب إن زال فالألم الحاصل لم يزل، وقال محمد الله: أجرة الطبيب؛ لأن ذلك أثر فعله، فكان له أخذ ذلك من ماله، وإعطاؤه الطبيب، وفي "شرح الطحاوي" فسر قول أبي يوسف: عليه أرش الألم بأجرة الطبيب والمداواة، فعلى هذا لا اختلاف بين أبي يوسف ومحمد، وبقولهما قال الشافعي وأحمد في رواية، ولأبي حنيفة له: أن الموجب هو الشين الذي يلحقه بفعله وزوال منفعته وقد زال ذلك بزوال أثره، والمنافع لا تتقوم إلا بالعقد كالإجارة الصحيحة أو ما يشبه العقد كالفاسد، ولم يوجد شيء من ذلك في حق الجاني، فلا يلزمه الغرامة، وكذلك مجرد الألم لا يوجب شيئا، ألا ترى أن من ضرب إنسانا ضربا مؤلما من غير جرح، لا يجب عليه شيء من الأرش تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٥١/٩]
ولا قود بجرح لا يقتص عندنا بجرح حتى يبرأ صاحبه وقال الشافعي الله : يقتص منه في الحال؛ لأن الموجب : قد تحقق، فلا يؤخر كما في القصاص في النفس، ولنا ما روي أنه عليها "نهى أن يقتص من جرح حتى يبرأ صاحبه"، رواه أحمد والدار قطني؛ ولأن الجراحات يعتبر فيها مآلها؛ لاحتمال أن تسري إلى النفس، فيظهر أنه قتل، فلا يعلم أنه جرح إلا بالبرء، فيستقر به تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٥١/٩] حتى يبرأ قال في "ملا مسكين": لكن العبارة لا تساعد. قال في "الفتح": أي لا تساعد المراد ؛ لأنه بعد البرء لا يقضي بشيء من قود وأرش، وعبارة المتن يوهم أن القود شرط بالبرء.
نصف العشر: أي يكون الدية في كل من هذه الصور في مال القاتل كما روي عن ابن عباس ما موقوفا ومرفوعا "لا تعقل العاقلة عمدا ولا عبدا ولا صلحا ولا اعترافا، ولأن العاقلة تتحمل تخفيفا عن القاتل، وذلك يليق بالمخطئ، والذي وجب بالصلح وجب بعقده، والعاقلة لا تتحمل إلا ما وجب بالقتل، وكذا ما لزمه بإقراره، وإنما لا تتحمل أقل من نصف عشر الدية؛ لأنه لا يؤدي إلى الإجحاف والاستئصال بالجاني. ثم الكل يجب مؤجلا إلى ثلاث سنين إلا ما وجب بالصلح، فإنه يجب حالا؛ لأنه واجب بالعقد، فيكون حالا بخلاف غيره، وما دون أرش الموضحة يجب في سنة؛ لأنه دون ثلث الدية والثلث وما دونه يجب في سنة وقال الشافعي محله ما وجب بقتل الأب ابنه يجب حالا؛ لأن القصاص سقط شرعا إلى بدل فيكون ذلك البدل حالا كسائر المتلفات ولنا أن المتلف ليس بمال وما ليس بمال لا يضمن بالمال أصلا، وإنما عرفنا تقومه بالمال بالشرع، والشرع إنما قومه بدية مؤجلة إلى ثلاث سنين وإيجاب المال حالا زيادة على ما أوجبه الشرع وصفا، فلا يجوز كما لا يجوز إيجاب الزيادة على ما أوجبه الشرع قدرا تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٥١/٩]
So no arsh and no qisas for a wound until its owner heals, and every intentional act whose qisas falls due to doubt, like a father killing his son intentionally, its diyah is in the wealth of the killer, and likewise what is due by compromise or admission or is less than half a tenth, it is due in the killer's wealth. So no arsh i.e., upon the one who wounded or struck, and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa, by Allah, and Abu Yusuf said: upon him is the arsh of pain, which is hukumat adl, because the defect that necessitates (compensation) if it is removed, the pain that occurred has not been removed, and Muhammad said: the wage of the physician, because that is an effect of his action, so he may take that from his wealth and give it to the physician. And in Sharh al-Tahawi, the saying of Abu Yusuf 'arsh of pain' is interpreted as the wage of the physician and medication, so on this there is no difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i and Ahmad in one narration say the same. And for Abu Hanifa: the cause is the defect that he inflicts upon him and loss of benefit, and that has been removed by the removal of its trace, and benefits are only valued by contract like a valid lease or what resembles a contract like a void one, and nothing of that exists concerning the offender, so he is not liable for guarantee, and similarly mere pain does not necessitate anything. Do you not see that if someone strikes another a painful strike without wounding, nothing of arsh is due upon him. (Takmila al-Bahr al-Raiq 9:151) And no qisas for a wound according to us: qisas is not executed for a wound until its owner heals, and al-Shafi'i said: qisas is executed immediately, because the cause is realized, so it should not be delayed like qisas for life. And for us it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) prohibited qisas for a wound until its owner heals, narrated by Ahmad and al-Daraqutni, and because wounds are considered based on their outcome due to the possibility of their spreading to the soul, so it appears that it is killing, so it is not known that it is a wound except by healing, so it is established by it. (Takmila al-Bahr al-Raiq 9:151) Until he heals: Mulla Miskeen said: but the expression does not help. In al-Fath: it does not help the intended meaning, because after healing nothing of qisas or arsh is decreed, and the wording of the text suggests that qisas is conditioned upon healing. Half a tenth: i.e., the diyah in each of these forms is in the wealth of the killer, as narrated from Ibn Abbas as a mawquf and marfu' hadith: 'The 'agila does not bear the diyah for intentional killing, nor for a slave, nor for a compromise, nor for an admission.' And because the 'agila bears it as a relief for the killer, and that suits the mistaken one, and what is due by compromise is due by his contract, and the 'agila only bears what is due by killing, and likewise what is due by his admission. And the less than half of a tenth is not borne because it does not lead to hardship and ruination of the offender. Then all is deferred to three years except what is due by compromise, for it is due immediately because it is due by contract, so it is immediate unlike others. And what is less than the arsh of a mawdihah is due in one year, because it is less than a third of the diyah. And al-Shafi'i said: his view is that what is due for killing a father by his son is due immediately, because qisas fell legally to a substitute, so that substitute is immediate like other damages. And for us: the damaged thing is not property, and what is not property is not guaranteed by property at all, and we only know its evaluation by law, and the law evaluated it with a diyah deferred to three years, and requiring the wealth immediately would be an increase beyond what the law required in description, so it is not permissible, just as it is not permissible to require an increase beyond what the law required in quantity. (Takmila al-Bahr al-Raiq 9:151)
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage covers two main issues. First, it discusses the postponement of qisas for wounds until healing. The Hanafi school holds that qisas for a wound cannot be carried out immediately; one must wait until the wound heals because it may turn fatal, turning the offense into murder. The Prophet (peace be upon him) is reported to have prohibited qisas for a wound until the owner heals. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that the cause of qisas is already present and should be executed immediately. Second, the passage addresses the liability for diyah in cases where qisas is dropped due to a doubt, such as a father killing his son. In such cases, the diyah is due from the killer's personal wealth, not from the 'agila (family treasury). The same applies to diyah agreed upon by compromise or admission. The diyah is deferred over three years, except for diyah by compromise which is immediate. Al-Shafi'i argues that diyah for a father killed by his son should be immediate, but the Hanafis respond that the original obligation was qisas, which is not considered property, and the substitute is financial compensation deferred as per law. The text also notes a sub-dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf/Muhammad regarding compensation for pain and suffering when the wound heals without trace.

Key Terms
عاقلة (aqila): The male relatives of the offender who traditionally share in paying diyah for accidental killing.
صلح (sulh): Compromise agreement between the parties regarding diyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is diyah for a father killing his son deferred over three years?
A) Because the father is entitled to a payment plan.
B) Because the original right (qisas) is not property, so the law set its substitute as deferred.
C) Because the 'aqila needs time to gather funds.
D) Because the victim's family must agree to the deferral.

Key Takeaway
Diyah for intentional killing with doubt, compromise, admission, or minor injuries is from the killer's wealth, deferred three years (immediate for compromise).

No Arsh or Qisas for Wounds Until Healing: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Expansion of ruling on wound injuries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying qisas for wounds until healing and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on immediate medical expenses.

Core Idea
Qisas and permanent arsh are suspended until healing; medical expenses are due immediately per the mufta bihi.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a critical rule: no retaliatory action (qisas) or permanent indemnity (arsh) can be taken for a wound until it heals. Within the Hanafi school there is a nuanced dispute about whether the aggressor must immediately cover pain and medical costs. We will unpack the proofs and how the final fatwa reconciles the views of Abu Hanifa and his two students.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The matn states: there is no arsh and no qisas for a wound until it heals. Understand this as a suspended liability—the final outcome determines the extent of compensation.
This applies to both permanent defect (shayn) and retribution.
2
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds no compensation at all until healing. Abu Yusuf argues for an indemnity for pain (hukumat 'adl), while Muhammad says the aggressor must pay the doctor's wage. Compare the bases and note the reconciliation in Sharh al-Tahawi.
The mufta bihi follows the two students: medical expenses are immediate.
3
Analyse the dalil for delaying qisas
The hadith 'نهى أن يقتص من جرح حتى يبرأ صاحبه' is the primary proof. Also the rationale that wounds may become fatal, so the final outcome is uncertain.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in practice.
4
Engage the inter-madhhab dispute
Al-Shafi'i argues for immediate qisas because the cause (the wound) is established. The Hanafi response uses the hadith and the uncertainty principle.
The thamarah al-khilaf: premature qisas could be invalid if the victim later dies.
5
Apply the ruling to the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view: medical expenses are wajib immediately; qisas and arsh for permanent defect are deferred until healing.
This balances the victim's need for treatment and the need for finality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا أرش ولا قود بجرح حتى يبرأ، وكل عمد سقط قوده بشبهة كقتل الأب ابنه عمدا، فديته في مال القاتل وكذا ما وجب صلحا أو اعترافا أو لم يكن نصف العشر، يجب في مال القاتل من حيث الصلح بقتل الخطأ
فلا أرش أي على الذي شج أو ضرب وهذا قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله: عليه أرش الألم، وهو حكومة عدل؛ لأن الشين الموجب إن زال فالألم الحاصل لم يزل، وقال محمد رحمه الله: أجرة الطبيب؛ لأن ذلك أثر فعله، فكان له أخذ ذلك من ماله، وإعطاؤه الطبيب، وفي "شرح الطحاوي" فسر قول أبي يوسف: عليه أرش الألم بأجرة الطبيب والمداواة، فعلى هذا لا اختلاف بين أبي يوسف ومحمد، وبقولهما قال الشافعي وأحمد في رواية، ولأبي حنيفة رحمه الله: أن الموجب هو الشين الذي يلحقه بفعله وزوال منفعته وقد زال ذلك بزوال أثره، والمنافع لا تتقوم إلا بالعقد كالإجارة الصحيحة أو ما يشبه العقد كالفاسد، ولم يوجد شيء من ذلك في حق الجاني، فلا يلزمه الغرامة، وكذلك مجرد الألم لا يوجب شيئا، ألا ترى أن من ضرب إنسانا ضربا مؤلما من غير جرح، لا يجب عليه شيء من الأرش. (تكملة البحر الرائق)
ولا قود بجرح لا يقتص عندنا بجرح حتى يبرأ صاحبه، وقال الشافعي رحمه الله: يقتص منه في الحال؛ لأن الموجب قد تحقق، فلا يؤخر كما في القصاص في النفس، ولنا ما روي أنه عليه السلام "نهى أن يقتص من جرح حتى يبرأ صاحبه" رواه أحمد والدارقطني؛ ولأن الجراحات يعتبر فيها مآلها؛ لاحتمال أن تسري إلى النفس، فيظهر أنه قتل، فلا يعلم أنه جرح إلا بالبرء، فيستقر به. (تكملة البحر الرائق) حتى يبرأ قال في "ملا مسكين": لكن العبارة لا تساعد. قال في "الفتح": أي لا تساعد المراد؛ لأنه بعد البرء لا يقضي بشيء من قود وأرش، وعبارة المتن يوهم أن القود شرط بالبرء.
نصف العشر: أي يكون الدية في كل من هذه الصور في مال القاتل كما روي عن ابن عباس موقوفا ومرفوعا "لا تعقل العاقلة عمدا ولا عبدا ولا صلحا ولا اعترافا" ولأن العاقلة تتحمل تخفيفا عن القاتل، وذلك يليق بالمخطئ، والذي وجب بالصلح وجب بعقده، والعاقلة لا تتحمل إلا ما وجب بالقتل، وكذا ما لزمه بإقراره، وإنما لا تتحمل أقل من نصف عشر الدية؛ لأنه لا يؤدي إلى الإجحاف والاستئصال بالجاني. ثم الكل يجب مؤجلا إلى ثلاث سنين إلا ما وجب بالصلح، فإنه يجب حالا؛ لأنه واجب بالعقد، فيكون حالا بخلاف غيره، وما دون أرش الموضحة يجب في سنة؛ لأنه دون ثلث الدية والثلث وما دونه يجب في سنة. وقال الشافعي رحمه الله: ما وجب بقتل الأب ابنه يجب حالا؛ لأن القصاص سقط شرعا إلى بدل فيكون ذلك البدل حالا كسائر المتلفات. ولنا أن المتلف ليس بمال وما ليس بمال لا يضمن بالمال أصلا، وإنما عرفنا تقومه بالمال بالشرع، والشرع إنما قومه بدية مؤجلة إلى ثلاث سنين وإيجاب المال حالا زيادة على ما أوجبه الشرع وصفا، فلا يجوز كما لا يجوز إيجاب الزيادة على ما أوجبه الشرع قدرا. (تكملة البحر الرائق)
There is no indemnity nor qisas for a wound until it heals. And every intentional act whose qisas drops due to a shubhah, like a father killing his son intentionally, its diyah is in the wealth of the killer. Likewise whatever is wajib by settlement or confession or is less than half of a tenth (of diyah), it is wajib in the wealth of the killer from the perspective of settlement for accidental killing. The explanation: 'No indemnity' means upon the one who inflicts a head wound or strikes. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: upon him is the indemnity for pain, which is a valuation of justice, because the defect that causes [liability] if it disappears, the pain that occurred has not disappeared. And Muhammad said: the wage of the doctor, because that is an effect of his action, so he may take that from his wealth and give it to the doctor. In Sharh al-Tahawi, the statement of Abu Yusuf 'indemnity for pain' is interpreted as the wage of the doctor and medical treatment, so on this there is no difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i and Ahmad in one narration follow them. And for Abu Hanifa: that which causes is the defect that he brings about by his action and the loss of benefit, and that has disappeared with the disappearance of its effect, and benefits are not compensable except through a contract like a valid lease or something resembling a contract like an invalid one, and nothing of that exists regarding the aggressor, so he is not liable for compensation. Also, mere pain does not obligate anything; do you not see that if someone strikes a person painfully without wounding, nothing of indemnity is required of him. (Completion from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) Also: no qisas for a wound; we do not execute qisas for a wound until its owner heals. Al-Shafi'i said: qisas is executed immediately because the cause has been realized, so it is not delayed as in qisas for life. And we have what is narrated that he (peace be upon him) forbade executing qisas from a wound until its owner heals, narrated by Ahmad and al-Daraqutni. Also because wounds are considered with regard to their outcome, due to the possibility that it may spread to the life, so it becomes apparent that it was killing, so it is not known that it is a wound until healing, so [the ruling] is established by it. (Completion from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) 'Until he heals': Mulla Miskin said: but the expression does not help. Al-Fath said: it does not help the intended meaning, because after healing nothing is judged regarding qisas or indemnity, and the wording of the matn gives the impression that qisas is conditional upon healing. (Regarding) less than half of a tenth: the diyah in each of these cases is in the wealth of the killer, as narrated from Ibn Abbas, both as a mawquf and marfu' tradition: 'The 'aqilah does not bear responsibility for intentional killing, nor for a slave, nor for a settlement, nor for a confession.' And because the 'aqilah bears [the diyah] as a relief for the killer, and that is appropriate for the mistaken person. And what is wajib by settlement is wajib by his contract, and the 'aqilah only bears what is wajib by killing. Likewise what is owed by his confession. And the 'aqilah does not bear less than half of a tenth of the diyah because it does not lead to oppression and total loss for the aggressor. Then all of this is deferred to three years except what is wajib by settlement, for it is immediate because it is wajib by contract, so it is immediate unlike others. And what is less than the indemnity of a scalp wound is wajib within one year because it is less than one-third of the diyah, and one-third and below is wajib within one year. Al-Shafi'i said: what is wajib by killing the father of his son is immediate because qisas is replaced by a substitute, so that substitute is immediate like other compensations. For us: the thing replaced is not wealth, and what is not wealth is not guaranteed by wealth at all. We only know its valuation by wealth through the Sharia, and the Sharia only valued it with a diyah deferred to three years. Imposing wealth immediately is an addition in description to what the Sharia imposed, so it is not permissible, just as it is not permissible to impose an addition in quantity to what the Sharia imposed. (Completion from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq)
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) of the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the chapter of diyat, specifically the rulings on wounds (shijaj). The commentator explains several key points. First, the ruling that no indemnity (arsh) or qisas is due for a wound until it heals completely. Within the Hanafi school, there is an intra-madhhab dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that no compensation at all is required during the healing period, because the defect that causes liability (the scar/disfigurement) disappears with healing, and benefits lost are not compensable without a contract. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the aggressor must pay for pain and medical expenses, though they differ on the basis: Abu Yusuf says it is a valuation for pain, while Muhammad says it is the doctor's wage. However, according to Sharh al-Tahawi, both positions amount to the same practical result (medical expenses). The commentator notes that al-Shafi'i and Ahmad in one narration agree with the two students. The passage then provides the Hanafi proof for delaying qisas until healing: a hadith from the Prophet forbidding qisas from a wound until the victim recovers, and the rationale that wounds may prove fatal, so their final outcome is unknown. This is followed by a response to al-Shafi'i, who argues for immediate qisas. Next, the passage covers cases where the diyah is solely on the killer's wealth (not on the 'aqilah): intentional killing where qisas drops due to shubhah (like a father killing his son), killing by settlement, confession, or where the diyah is less than half of a tenth (i.e., less than 5% of the full diyah). The proof is a hadith from Ibn Abbas that the 'aqilah does not bear responsibility for these cases, and the principle that the 'aqilah provides relief, which is appropriate only for accidental killing. Finally, the timing of payment is discussed: the full diyah is deferred over three years, except for that due by settlement which is immediate. For wounds less than a scalp wound (muwaddihah), the arsh is due within one year. The passage ends with a rebuttal to al-Shafi'i's view that the diyah for a father killing his son should be immediate, arguing that the Sharia only imposed a deferred diyah, and imposing immediate payment is an unauthorized addition.

Key Terms
أرش (arsh): Financial compensation for injury to a body part, measured by the extent of damage or pain.
قود (qawd): Retaliatory punishment (qisas) for wounding, equivalent to the injury inflicted.
شبهة (shubhah): A semblance of right that prevents qisas, such as a father's authority over a son.
نصف العشر (nisf al-'ushr): Half of a tenth of the full diyah, i.e., 1/20 of the diyah (approximately 5% of full diyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi position, what is the aggressor's immediate obligation for a wound?
A) Full arsh for the permanent defect
B) Qisas immediately
C) Medical expenses (ajr al-tabib)
D) Nothing until the wound heals

Key Takeaway
Qisas and permanent arsh are deferred until the wound heals, but medical expenses are due immediately per the mufta bihi.

Diyat — Blood Money

When the Killer Pays the Full Diyah: Cases and Payment Schedule
Expansion on diyah liability and timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the cases where diyah is wajib solely on the killer's wealth and state the payment timing for each.

Core Idea
Diyah is on the killer's wealth (not 'aqilah) for intentional acts with shubhah, settlement, confession, and amounts below half a tenth; timing varies.

This section of the passage specifies exceptions where the diyah (blood money) is not borne by the 'aqilah (tribal guarantors) but exclusively by the killer's own wealth. These include intentional killings where qisas drops due to a shubhah, killings resolved by settlement (sulh), cases of confession, and injuries requiring less than half a tenth of diyah. The passage also details the payment schedule: deferred over three years, immediate for settlement amounts, and one year for small sums.

Guided Path
1
List the cases where diyah is on the killer's wealth
The text enumerates: (1) intentional act with shubhah (e.g., father killing son), (2) killing by settlement (sulh), (3) killing by confession, (4) when the due amount is less than half a tenth of diyah.
These are exceptions to the rule that 'aqilah bears diyah for accidental killing.
2
Understand the rationale
The 'aqilah provides relief for the killer, which is appropriate only for the mistaken (accidental) killer. For intentional acts or contractual obligations (settlement, confession), the killer himself bears the full burden. Small amounts are excluded because they do not cause hardship.
The hadith from Ibn Abbas supports this: 'The 'aqilah does not bear responsibility for intentional killing, nor for a slave, nor for a settlement, nor for a confession.'
3
Analyse the payment timing rules
Full diyah (in these cases) is deferred over 3 years. Exception: diyah wajib by settlement (sulh) is immediate because it is contractual. For amounts less than arsh of muwaddihah (scalp wound), the payment is within one year.
The three-year deferment is a concession; immediate payment for settlement respects the contractual nature.
4
Engage the inter-madhhab dispute
Al-Shafi'i argues that diyah for a father killing his son should be immediate because qisas is replaced by a substitute. The Hanafi response: the substitute (diyah) is not wealth originally, and the Sharia only imposed it deferred; adding immediacy is an unauthorized addition.
The Hanafi position preserves the deferred structure set by revelation.
5
Apply the rules to a scenario
Given a case of intentional killing with shubhah, the killer pays the full diyah from his own wealth, deferred over 3 years. If the victim's family agrees to a settlement (sulh), the agreed amount is immediate.
The mufta bihi follows the deferred schedule except for settlement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا أرش ولا قود بجرح حتى يبرأ، وكل عمد سقط قوده بشبهة كقتل الأب ابنه عمدا، فديته في مال القاتل وكذا ما وجب صلحا أو اعترافا أو لم يكن نصف العشر، يجب في مال القاتل من حيث الصلح بقتل الخطأ
فلا أرش أي على الذي شج أو ضرب وهذا قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله: عليه أرش الألم، وهو حكومة عدل؛ لأن الشين الموجب إن زال فالألم الحاصل لم يزل، وقال محمد رحمه الله: أجرة الطبيب؛ لأن ذلك أثر فعله، فكان له أخذ ذلك من ماله، وإعطاؤه الطبيب، وفي "شرح الطحاوي" فسر قول أبي يوسف: عليه أرش الألم بأجرة الطبيب والمداواة، فعلى هذا لا اختلاف بين أبي يوسف ومحمد، وبقولهما قال الشافعي وأحمد في رواية، ولأبي حنيفة رحمه الله: أن الموجب هو الشين الذي يلحقه بفعله وزوال منفعته وقد زال ذلك بزوال أثره، والمنافع لا تتقوم إلا بالعقد كالإجارة الصحيحة أو ما يشبه العقد كالفاسد، ولم يوجد شيء من ذلك في حق الجاني، فلا يلزمه الغرامة، وكذلك مجرد الألم لا يوجب شيئا، ألا ترى أن من ضرب إنسانا ضربا مؤلما من غير جرح، لا يجب عليه شيء من الأرش.
