ولا قود بجرح لا يقتص عندنا بجرح حتى يبرأ صاحبه، وقال الشافعي رحمه الله: يقتص منه في الحال؛ لأن الموجب قد تحقق، فلا يؤخر كما في القصاص في النفس، ولنا ما روي أنه عليه السلام "نهى أن يقتص من جرح حتى يبرأ صاحبه" رواه أحمد والدارقطني؛ ولأن الجراحات يعتبر فيها مآلها؛ لاحتمال أن تسري إلى النفس، فيظهر أنه قتل، فلا يعلم أنه جرح إلا بالبرء، فيستقر به. (تكملة البحر الرائق) حتى يبرأ قال في "ملا مسكين": لكن العبارة لا تساعد. قال في "الفتح": أي لا تساعد المراد؛ لأنه بعد البرء لا يقضي بشيء من قود وأرش، وعبارة المتن يوهم أن القود شرط بالبرء.
نصف العشر: أي يكون الدية في كل من هذه الصور في مال القاتل كما روي عن ابن عباس موقوفا ومرفوعا "لا تعقل العاقلة عمدا ولا عبدا ولا صلحا ولا اعترافا" ولأن العاقلة تتحمل تخفيفا عن القاتل، وذلك يليق بالمخطئ، والذي وجب بالصلح وجب بعقده، والعاقلة لا تتحمل إلا ما وجب بالقتل، وكذا ما لزمه بإقراره، وإنما لا تتحمل أقل من نصف عشر الدية؛ لأنه لا يؤدي إلى الإجحاف والاستئصال بالجاني. ثم الكل يجب مؤجلا إلى ثلاث سنين إلا ما وجب بالصلح، فإنه يجب حالا؛ لأنه واجب بالعقد، فيكون حالا بخلاف غيره، وما دون أرش الموضحة يجب في سنة؛ لأنه دون ثلث الدية والثلث وما دونه يجب في سنة. وقال الشافعي رحمه الله: ما وجب بقتل الأب ابنه يجب حالا؛ لأن القصاص سقط شرعا إلى بدل فيكون ذلك البدل حالا كسائر المتلفات. ولنا أن المتلف ليس بمال وما ليس بمال لا يضمن بالمال أصلا، وإنما عرفنا تقومه بالمال بالشرع، والشرع إنما قومه بدية مؤجلة إلى ثلاث سنين وإيجاب المال حالا زيادة على ما أوجبه الشرع وصفا، فلا يجوز كما لا يجوز إيجاب الزيادة على ما أوجبه الشرع قدرا. (تكملة البحر الرائق)
There is no indemnity nor qisas for a wound until it heals. And every intentional act whose qisas drops due to a shubhah, like a father killing his son intentionally, its diyah is in the wealth of the killer. Likewise whatever is wajib by settlement or confession or is less than half of a tenth (of diyah), it is wajib in the wealth of the killer from the perspective of settlement for accidental killing. The explanation: 'No indemnity' means upon the one who inflicts a head wound or strikes. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: upon him is the indemnity for pain, which is a valuation of justice, because the defect that causes [liability] if it disappears, the pain that occurred has not disappeared. And Muhammad said: the wage of the doctor, because that is an effect of his action, so he may take that from his wealth and give it to the doctor. In Sharh al-Tahawi, the statement of Abu Yusuf 'indemnity for pain' is interpreted as the wage of the doctor and medical treatment, so on this there is no difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i and Ahmad in one narration follow them. And for Abu Hanifa: that which causes is the defect that he brings about by his action and the loss of benefit, and that has disappeared with the disappearance of its effect, and benefits are not compensable except through a contract like a valid lease or something resembling a contract like an invalid one, and nothing of that exists regarding the aggressor, so he is not liable for compensation. Also, mere pain does not obligate anything; do you not see that if someone strikes a person painfully without wounding, nothing of indemnity is required of him. (Completion from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) Also: no qisas for a wound; we do not execute qisas for a wound until its owner heals. Al-Shafi'i said: qisas is executed immediately because the cause has been realized, so it is not delayed as in qisas for life. And we have what is narrated that he (peace be upon him) forbade executing qisas from a wound until its owner heals, narrated by Ahmad and al-Daraqutni. Also because wounds are considered with regard to their outcome, due to the possibility that it may spread to the life, so it becomes apparent that it was killing, so it is not known that it is a wound until healing, so [the ruling] is established by it. (Completion from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) 'Until he heals': Mulla Miskin said: but the expression does not help. Al-Fath said: it does not help the intended meaning, because after healing nothing is judged regarding qisas or indemnity, and the wording of the matn gives the impression that qisas is conditional upon healing. (Regarding) less than half of a tenth: the diyah in each of these cases is in the wealth of the killer, as narrated from Ibn Abbas, both as a mawquf and marfu' tradition: 'The 'aqilah does not bear responsibility for intentional killing, nor for a slave, nor for a settlement, nor for a confession.' And because the 'aqilah bears [the diyah] as a relief for the killer, and that is appropriate for the mistaken person. And what is wajib by settlement is wajib by his contract, and the 'aqilah only bears what is wajib by killing. Likewise what is owed by his confession. And the 'aqilah does not bear less than half of a tenth of the diyah because it does not lead to oppression and total loss for the aggressor. Then all of this is deferred to three years except what is wajib by settlement, for it is immediate because it is wajib by contract, so it is immediate unlike others. And what is less than the indemnity of a scalp wound is wajib within one year because it is less than one-third of the diyah, and one-third and below is wajib within one year. Al-Shafi'i said: what is wajib by killing the father of his son is immediate because qisas is replaced by a substitute, so that substitute is immediate like other compensations. For us: the thing replaced is not wealth, and what is not wealth is not guaranteed by wealth at all. We only know its valuation by wealth through the Sharia, and the Sharia only valued it with a diyah deferred to three years. Imposing wealth immediately is an addition in description to what the Sharia imposed, so it is not permissible, just as it is not permissible to impose an addition in quantity to what the Sharia imposed. (Completion from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq)
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) of the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the chapter of diyat, specifically the rulings on wounds (shijaj). The commentator explains several key points. First, the ruling that no indemnity (arsh) or qisas is due for a wound until it heals completely. Within the Hanafi school, there is an intra-madhhab dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that no compensation at all is required during the healing period, because the defect that causes liability (the scar/disfigurement) disappears with healing, and benefits lost are not compensable without a contract. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the aggressor must pay for pain and medical expenses, though they differ on the basis: Abu Yusuf says it is a valuation for pain, while Muhammad says it is the doctor's wage. However, according to Sharh al-Tahawi, both positions amount to the same practical result (medical expenses). The commentator notes that al-Shafi'i and Ahmad in one narration agree with the two students. The passage then provides the Hanafi proof for delaying qisas until healing: a hadith from the Prophet forbidding qisas from a wound until the victim recovers, and the rationale that wounds may prove fatal, so their final outcome is unknown. This is followed by a response to al-Shafi'i, who argues for immediate qisas. Next, the passage covers cases where the diyah is solely on the killer's wealth (not on the 'aqilah): intentional killing where qisas drops due to shubhah (like a father killing his son), killing by settlement, confession, or where the diyah is less than half of a tenth (i.e., less than 5% of the full diyah). The proof is a hadith from Ibn Abbas that the 'aqilah does not bear responsibility for these cases, and the principle that the 'aqilah provides relief, which is appropriate only for accidental killing. Finally, the timing of payment is discussed: the full diyah is deferred over three years, except for that due by settlement which is immediate. For wounds less than a scalp wound (muwaddihah), the arsh is due within one year. The passage ends with a rebuttal to al-Shafi'i's view that the diyah for a father killing his son should be immediate, arguing that the Sharia only imposed a deferred diyah, and imposing immediate payment is an unauthorized addition.

Key Terms
أرش الموضحة (arsh al-muwaddihah): The indemnity for a scalp wound that exposes the bone; a fixed amount (1/20 of diyah).
صلح (sulh): Settlement agreement between the victim's family and the killer to waive qisas in exchange for diyah or other consideration.
عاقلة ('aqilah): The tribal guarantors who bear the diyah for accidental killing as a relief for the killer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in which of the following cases is diyah NOT borne by the 'aqilah?
A) Accidental killing by a minor
B) Intentional killing with shubhah
C) Accidental killing by a sane adult
D) Killing during sleep

Key Takeaway
Diyah is wajib on the killer's wealth for intentional acts with shubhah, settlement, confession, and small amounts; full diyah is deferred 3 years except settlement (immediate) and small amounts (1 year).

Intentional Killing by a Child or Insane Person Treated as Accidental
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intentional killing by a child or insane person, distinguish it from the Shafi'i position, and apply the rule to determine the consequences for diyah, kaffarah, and inheritance.

Core Idea
Intentional killing by a child or insane person is treated as accidental: diyah on 'aqilah, no kaffarah, no inheritance deprivation.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies a key principle in Hanafi diyat law: the legal capacity for intention. While the act appears intentional, the actor's lack of full reason changes its legal classification. We will explore the ruling, the proof from 'Ali (ra), and the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal classification
The passage states that the intentional killing by a child (sabi) or an insane person (majnoon) is legally treated as accidental (khat'). This means the act is not considered fully intentional for criminal liability.
The ruling covers both the child and the insane person; the same logic applies to the mentally deficient (ma'tuh).
2
Determine the three consequences
Because the killing is classified as accidental, three consequences follow: (1) diyah (blood money) is wajib on the 'aqilah (victim's clan), not on the killer's own wealth; (2) no kaffarah (expiation) is required; (3) the killer is not deprived of inheritance from the victim.
These consequences are distinct from intentional killing, where diyah would be from the killer's own wealth, kaffarah might apply, and inheritance could be barred.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school relies on a narration from 'Ali (ra) who placed the diyah of an insane person on his 'aqilah and said: 'His intentional and his accidental are the same.' Additionally, qiyas (analogy) is drawn: if a sane mistaken person is given mitigation (diyah on 'aqilah), then a child or insane person, being more excusable, deserves even greater mitigation.
The proof combines a dalil naqli (narration) and qiyas.
4
Examine the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i argues that the act is literally intentional (the killer intended to strike), so it should be treated as intentional. Since qisas is dropped only because of the killer's incapacity, the remaining effects of intentional killing (diyah in the killer's wealth, kaffarah, inheritance deprivation) should still apply.
This is a disagreement over how to classify the act when the actor lacks full legal responsibility.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that genuine intentionality requires knowledge and reason (aql). The child has deficient reason, the insane person none, so true intent cannot be formed. Their act is akin to that of a sleeping person. Without intent, the killing cannot be considered intentional, and the accidental regime applies.
This highlights the principle that legal capacity (ahliyyah) is crucial for classifying acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعمد الصبي والمجنون خطأ، وديته على عاقلته ولا تكفير فيه ولا حرمان، والمعتوه في حكم الخطأ دية عمد الصبي قتلهما عمدا عن الإرث كالصبي.. في الحكم المذكور
وعمد الصبي إلخ: أي إذا قتل صبي أو مجنون رجلا عمدا، فحكمه حكم الخطأ، فيجب ديته على عاقلته؛ لما روي عن علي رضي الله عنه أنه جعل عقل المجنون على عاقلته وقال: "عمده وخطأه سواء" ولأن الصبي مظنة العذر، والعاقل الخاطئ لما استحق التخفيف حتى وجبت الدية على العاقلة، فالصبي أحق بهذه التخفيف، وقال الشافعي: عمدهما عمد حتى تجب الدية في مالهما؛ إذ العمد هو القصد غير أنه تخلف عنه أحد حكميه، وهو القصاص، فينسحب عليه حكمه الآخر، وهو الوجوب في ماله، ولهذا تجب الكفارة، ويحرم عن الميراث على أصله؛ لأنهما يتعلقان بالقتل ولنا ما قدمنا ولا نسلم تحقق العمدية فإنها تترتب على العلم والعلم بالعقل، والمجنون عديم العقل، والصبي قاصر العقل، فأنى يتحقق منهما القصد، فصار كالنائم. (فتح) ولا تكفير فيه إلخ أي لا كفارة على الصبي والمجنون، ولا يحرمان عن الميراث بالقتل عندنا؛ لأن الكفارة كاسمها ستارة ولا ذنب تستره؛ لأنهما مرفوعا القلم، وحرمان الإرث عقوبة وهما ليس من أهلها، وأما حرمان الصبي المرتد من ميراث أبيه، فلاختلاف الدين لا جزاء للردة، وفيه خلاف الشافعي كما مر. (فتح وغيره بتصرف)
And the intentional killing by a child and an insane person is accidental (khat'), and its diyah is upon their 'aqilah, and there is no kaffarah (expiation) in it, and no deprivation (of inheritance). And the mentally deficient person is in the ruling of accidental. The diyah of intentional killing by a child... They killed both intentionally from inheritance like a child... in the aforementioned ruling. The explanation: 'And the intentional by a child etc.' meaning: if a child or an insane person intentionally kills a man, its ruling is the ruling of accidental killing, so its diyah is wajib upon their 'aqilah. This is based on what is narrated from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that he placed the aql (diyah) of an insane person upon his 'aqilah and said: 'His intentional and his accidental are the same.' And because a child is an occasion for excuse, and the mistaken sane person deserved mitigation so that the diyah is upon the 'aqilah, so the child is more deserving of this mitigation. Al-Shafi'i said: their intentional is truly intentional, so the diyah is wajib in their own wealth; because intentionality is the intent, except that one of its two effects, qisas, is dropped, so the other effect (obligation in his wealth) applies. For this reason, kaffarah is wajib and he is deprived of inheritance according to his principle, because both are connected to killing. And for us, we have what we presented and we do not concede the realization of intentionality, because it depends on knowledge and knowledge depends on reason. The insane person lacks reason, and the child has deficient reason, so how can intent be realized from them? Thus they are like the sleeping person. (Fath) 'And no kaffarah in it etc.' meaning there is no kaffarah upon the child and the insane person, and they are not deprived of inheritance due to killing according to us. Because kaffarah, as its name suggests, is a covering, and there is no sin to cover because the pen is lifted from them. And deprivation of inheritance is a punishment, and they are not eligible for punishment. As for the deprivation of an apostate child from inheriting his father, it is due to difference of religion, not as a penalty for apostasy, and there is disagreement with al-Shafi'i as mentioned. (Fath and others with modification)
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage expands on the matn ruling that the intentional killing by a child or an insane person is legally treated as accidental (khat'). The consequence is that the diyah is due on the 'aqilah (the victim's clan), not on the killer's own wealth, and there is no kaffarah (expiation) nor deprivation of inheritance for the killer. The commentator provides the Hanafi proof: a narration from 'Ali (ra) that he placed the diyah of an insane person on his 'aqilah and stated that his intentional and accidental are the same. Additionally, the child is even more deserving of this mitigation because he lacks full reason. The passage then records the Shafi'i opposition: al-Shafi'i considers their killing truly intentional, so the diyah should be from their own wealth, and they must perform kaffarah and be deprived of inheritance (on the principle that these follow from killing). The Hanafi response is that true intentionality requires knowledge and reason, which the child and insane person lack, so their act is akin to that of a sleeping person. The passage also clarifies that no kaffarah is required because their actions are not sinful (the pen is lifted), and deprivation of inheritance is a punishment they do not deserve. An exception is noted: an apostate child is deprived of inheriting from a non-Muslim father due to difference of religion, not as a penalty for apostasy, and this is a point of disagreement with al-Shafi'i.

Key Terms
الصبي (al-sabi): A minor male who has not reached puberty; his intentional acts are not legally considered intentional in the context of criminal liability.
المجنون (al-majnoon): An insane person who lacks reason entirely; his acts have no legal intent.
عاقلة (al-aqilah): The group of male relatives who are liable to pay diyah in cases of accidental killing.
تكفير (takfir): Expiation (kaffarah) required for accidental killing, such as freeing a slave or fasting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The child's 'aqilah pays the diyah, and the child is not deprived of inheritance.
B) The child pays the diyah from his own wealth and is deprived of inheritance.
C) The child is subject to qisas because the killing was intentional.
D) The child must perform kaffarah and is deprived of inheritance.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats intentional killing by a child or insane person as accidental due to lack of legal capacity, shifting diyah to the 'aqilah and exempting from kaffarah and inheritance deprivation.

The Ghurrah for a Miscarried Fetus: Definition and Ruling
Definition of janīn and ruling of ghurrah for a dead fetus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of janīn, identify the ruling of ghurrah for a miscarried fetus, and explain the Hanafi position regarding its amount, duration, and who pays it.

Core Idea
A miscarried fetus requires a ghurrah, not a full diyah, paid by the ʿāqila within one year.

This passage introduces the rulings on the fetus. It defines the term janīn and then presents the obligation of the ghurrah when a free pregnant woman miscarries a dead fetus due to a strike. We will examine the definition, the amount of the ghurrah, its payment by the ʿāqila, and the evidence from the hadith of the woman of Hudhayl. Understanding this ruling provides insight into how Hanafi fiqh values potential life and structures compensation.

Guided Path
1
Define the term 'janīn'
Extract the linguistic and legal definition of janīn from the passage. Note that it is the child in the womb before birth, named for concealment.
The word janīn is faʿīl in the passive sense (mafʿūl).
2
Identify the triggering scenario
The ghurrah becomes obligatory when a free pregnant woman is struck and miscarries a dead fetus. Confirm that the strike can be on any part of the body – the belly is just an example.
The mother must be a free woman; slave women have a separate ruling.
3
Determine the amount of ghurrah
The ghurrah is half a tenth of the diyah of a man (500 dirhams) regardless of the fetus's gender. For a male fetus, it is half a tenth of a man's diyah; for a female fetus, it is a tenth of a woman's diyah, both equalling 500 dirhams.
This is because a woman's diyah is half a man's, so half a tenth of a man's diyah equals a tenth of a woman's diyah.
4
Identify who pays and the time frame
According to the Hanafi school, the ghurrah is paid by the ʿāqila (paternal relatives) within one year. Contrast with other schools: Mālik says the offender pays personally; Shāfiʿī says it is due in three years.
The ʿāqila are the male paternal relatives including the offender.
5
Analyze the evidence and principle
The primary evidence is the hadith of the woman from Hudhayl, where the Prophet ﷺ ruled a ghurrah on the ʿāqila. The Hanafi school also uses istiḥsān to set the amount as 500 dirhams, departing from strict qiyās which would require certainty of the fetus's life.
The istiḥsān is based on the prophetic practice (athar) and the ijmāʿ of the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في الجنين [هو اسم الولد في بطن الأم قبل أن يولد فإذا ولد يسمى وليدا ثم رضيعا على ما عرف في موضعه] لما كان الجنين في حكم الجزء من الكل ذكر أحكامه عقيب أحكام الأجزاء الحقيقية، والجنين فعيل بمعنى مفعول من جنّه إذا ستره، وهو الولد ما دام في الرحم سمي به لاجتنانه أي استتاره في البطن. (من الفتح وغيره) ضرب بطن امرأة إلخ أي امرأة حرة حامل، وكذا لو ضرب ظهرها أو جنبها أو رأسها أو عضوا من أعضائها فالبطن مثال لا قيد وإنما قيد بالمرأة؛ ليخرج البهيمة، وقيدنا بالحرة؛ لتخرج الأمة، فإن حكمها سيجيء، وأطلق في المرأة فعم ما لو كانت المرأة كتابية أو مجوسية أو زوجته. (ملخص الكتب) غرة بضم الغين المعجمة وتشديد الراء وغرة الشيء في اللغة: خياره كالفرس النجيب والحمار الفاره، وغرة ء أوله كما . سمي أول الشهر غرة، وسمي وجه الإنسان غرة؛ لأنه أول شيء يظهر. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٦/٢] نصف : ، أراد نصف عشر دية الرجل إذا كان الجنين ذكرا، وعشر دية المرأة إذا كان أنثى، وكل منهما خمسمائة درهم؛ لأن دية المرأة نصف دية الرجل، والأصل فيه ما روي أن امرأة من هذيل ضربت بطن امرأة بحجر فقتلتها، وما في بطنها، فاختصموا إلى رسول الله ، فقضى أن دية جنينها غرة عبد أو وليدة، وقضى بدية المرأة على عاقلتها"، رواه البخاري ومسلم، وهي على العاقلة عندنا. وعند مالك في ماله؛ لأنه بدل الجزء، ولنا: أنه عليه قضى بالغرة على العاقلة ولأنه بدل النفس من وجه، وتجب في سنة عندنا، وعند الشافعي: في ثلاث سنين؛ لأنه بدل النفس، ألا ترى أنه يورث، ولنا: ما روي عن الحسن أنه قال: بلغنا أن رسول الله اول قضى بالغرة على العاقلة في سنة رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٦/٢] وهذا استحسان، والقياس أن لا يجب شيء؛ لأنه يتيقن بحياته، والظاهر لا يصلح حجة للاستحقاق، لكن تركناه بالأثر، وهو حجة على من قدرها بست مائة نحو مالك والشافعي.
Chapter on the Fetus [It is the name of the child in the mother's womb before birth; when born it is called a walīd, then a raḍīʿ as known in its place.] Since the fetus is in the ruling of a part of the whole, he mentioned its rulings after the rulings of the real parts. 'Janīn' is faʿīl in the meaning of mafʿūl from janna-hu when he covered it, and it is the child as long as it is in the womb, named for its concealment, i.e., its being hidden in the belly. (From al-Fatḥ and others) 'He struck the belly of a woman, etc.' i.e., any free pregnant woman; likewise if he struck her back, side, head, or any limb, the belly is an example not a restriction. He restricted with 'woman' to exclude an animal, and we restricted with 'free' to exclude a slave woman, for her ruling will come later. He made it absolute regarding the woman, so it includes whether the woman is a Kitābiyya, Majūsiyya, or his wife. (Mukhtaṣar al-Kutub) 'Ghurrah' with a ḍamma on the ghayn and tashdīd on the rā’. The ghurrah of something in language: its best, like a noble horse and a brisk donkey. The first of the month is called ghurrah, and the face of a human is called ghurrah because it is the first thing that appears. [Ramz al-Ḥaqāʾiq 2/446] 'Half': he meant half of a tenth of the diyah of a man if the fetus is male, and a tenth of the diyah of a woman if it is female; each of them is five hundred dirhams because the diyah of a woman is half the diyah of a man. The basis for this is what is narrated that a woman from Hudhayl struck the belly of another woman with a stone, killing her and what was in her belly. They brought the case to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, and he ruled that the diyah of her fetus is a ghurrah: a slave or a slave girl, and he ruled the diyah of the woman on her ʿāqila. Narrated by Bukhārī and Muslim. It is on the ʿāqila according to us. According to Mālik, it is from his own wealth because it is compensation for a part. Our proof: he ﷺ ruled the ghurrah on the ʿāqila, and because it is compensation for a life in a sense. It is due in one year according to us, while according to al-Shāfiʿī it is due in three years because it is compensation for a life; don’t you see that it is inherited? Our proof: what is narrated from al-Ḥasan that he said: It reached us that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ ruled the ghurrah on the ʿāqila in one year. [Ramz al-Ḥaqāʾiq 2/446] This is istiḥsān, and the qiyās is that nothing should be due because his life is certain, and the apparent (evidence) is not sufficient for entitlement, but we abandoned it for the athar, and it is a proof against those who estimated it as six hundred, like Mālik and al-Shāfiʿī.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqāʾiq is the opening of a new chapter on rulings pertaining to the fetus (janīn) after the rulings on actual bodily parts. The commentator begins by defining the term: janīn is the child in the womb before birth. The form faʿīl here is in the passive sense (mafʿūl), meaning 'covered' because the fetus is concealed in the womb. The main ruling is: if a person strikes the belly of a free pregnant woman and she miscarries a dead fetus, a ghurrah is obligatory. Ghurrah linguistically means the best of something—like a choice horse or the first of the month—and here it refers to a slave or slave girl of fixed value. Its amount is half a tenth of the full diyah; i.e., if the fetus is male, half a tenth of a man's diyah (500 dirhams), and if female, a tenth of a woman's diyah (500 dirhams as well, since a woman's diyah is half a man's). The proof is the well-known hadith of the woman from Hudhayl, where the Prophet ﷺ ruled a ghurrah for the fetus. The ghurrah is paid by the ʿāqila (the paternal relatives) according to the Hanafī school, not from the offender's own wealth as Mālik held. It is due in one year, contrary to al-Shāfiʿī who says three years. The commentator explains that the ruling is based on istiḥsān, as strict qiyās would require certainty of life before birth, but the ruling is established by the prophetic practice (athar). This also refutes those like Mālik and al-Shāfiʿī who set the amount at six hundred dirhams.

Key Terms
جنين (janīn): The child in the mother's womb before birth, named for its concealment (ijtinān).
غرة (ghurrah): A slave or slave girl of fixed value, specifically half a tenth of the diyah when required for a fetus.
عاقلة (ʿāqila): The paternal relatives (ʿaṣaba) who are responsible for paying diyah in cases of homicide or injury by negligence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafī school, how much is the ghurrah for a male fetus when the mother is a free woman?
A) One-tenth of the diyah of a man (1000 dirhams)
B) Half a tenth of the diyah of a man (500 dirhams)
C) Full diyah of a man (10,000 dirhams)
D) One-twentieth of the diyah of a woman (250 dirhams)

Key Takeaway
The ghurrah is a wajib compensation of half a tenth of the diyah (500 dirhams) for a miscarried dead fetus, paid by the ʿāqila within one year.

Diyah and Ghurrah for Fetal Deaths: Scenarios and Madhhab Differences
Rulings for fetal death scenarios in diyat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for diyah and ghurrah in the three scenarios of a struck pregnant woman and defend the Hanafi position against the Shafi'i objection.

Core Idea
A live-born child requires full diyah; a dead fetus requires ghurrah; but if the mother dies first, no ghurrah is due.

When a pregnant woman is struck, the compensation depends on the fetus's outcome and the order of deaths. This lesson unpacks three scenarios: live birth then death, both die, and mother dies first. We will also examine the inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school over the last scenario and the inheritance rules for the compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
List three distinct cases from the passage: (1) fetus born alive then dies, (2) woman aborts dead fetus and both die, (3) woman dies first and then aborts dead fetus. Note the ruling for each.
The passage also mentions multiple aborted fetuses and a scenario with one live and one dead.
2
Extract the Hanafi ruling for each scenario
From the text: (1) full diyah for the live child, (2) diyah for mother + ghurrah for fetus, (3) only diyah for mother. Understand the basis: the act multiplies with multiple effects, but when mother dies first, the fetus's death is attributed to her death, not the strike.
The principle 'al-fi'l yata'addadu bi ta'addudi atharihi' is key.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof (dalil)
The text cites a narration 'روينا' (we have narrated) as evidence for two separate offenses. Identify the dalil as a hadith that establishes ghurrah for a dead fetus. Consider its transmission (zanni al-thubut) and how it supports the obligation.
The exact hadith is not quoted but is a known proof in diyat.
4
Examine the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
The Shafi'i school argues that in the mother-death scenario, ghurrah is still due because the fetus died by the same strike. The Hanafi response: the mother's death is the apparent cause, not the strike, because the fetus's life depends on hers. Hence doubt prevents obligation.
This is a classic usul dispute over causation and doubt (shubha).
5
Apply the inheritance rule
The diyah and ghurrah are inherited by the heirs of the deceased, but the killer cannot inherit. In the case where the father strikes his own wife and kills his son, the ghurrah is on the father's 'aqila, but he does not inherit.
This prevents the killer from benefiting from his own crime.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن ألقته حيا إلخ: أي تحب دية كاملة؛ لأنه أتلف آدميا خطأ أو شبه عمد، فتجب فيه الدية تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٥٤/٩] محمد بن فدية وغرة لما ،روينا ولأنهما جنايتان، فيجب فيهما موجبهما، وهذا لما عرف أن الفعل يتعدد بتعدد أثره، فصار كما إذا رمى فأصاب شخصا ونفذت منه إلى آخر فقتله فإنه يجب عليه ديتان ولو ألقت ميتين أو أكثر، تعددت الغرة كما في "الذخيرة"، وفي "الدر" عن البزازية: ضرب بطن امرأة بالسيف فألقت جنينا حيا، وآخر ميتا، وبه جراحة السيف وماتت أيضا، يقتص لأجل المرأة وعلى عاقلته دية الولد الحي إذا مات، وتجب غرة الولد الميت؛ لأنه لما ضرب ولم يعلم بالولدين في بطنها كان الضرب خطأ. (تكملة، فتح)  كتاب الديات ٤٣٩ أحكام الجنين وإن ماتت فألقت ميتا فدية فقط، وما يجب فيه يورث عنه، ولا يرث الضارب، في الأم في الجنين من الغرة والدية عن الجنين فلو ضرب بطن امرأته فألقت ابنه ميتا فعلى عاقلة الأب ،غرة، ولا يرث منها، وفي أي ابن الرجل الضارب أي أبوه
'If she aborts it alive, etc.' i.e., a full diyah is obligatory, because he destroyed a human being by mistake or quasi-intentional, so the diyah is obligatory upon him. (Takmilat al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq 9/154) 'Fidyah and ghurrah' because, as we have narrated, they are two offenses, so their respective compensations are obligatory. This is because it is known that the act is multiplied by the multiplicity of its effect; it becomes like when one shoots and hits a person and it penetrates to another and kills him, then two diyahs are obligatory. If she aborts two or more dead fetuses, multiple ghurrahs are due, as in al-Dhakhīra. In al-Durr from al-Bazzāziyya: A man struck the belly of a woman with a sword and she aborted one live fetus and another dead one, and she also died from the sword wound. Retaliation is applicable for the woman, and on his ʿāqila is the diyah of the live child if it dies, and the ghurrah for the dead child is obligatory because when he struck he did not know there were two fetuses in her belly, so the strike was a mistake. (Takmila, Fatḥ) [PAGE_440] Book of Diyat: 'And if she dies and aborts a dead fetus, only the diyah is due, and what is obligatory (diyah and ghurrah) is inherited from the deceased, and the killer does not inherit. For the mother, from the fetus, from the ghurrah and diyah for the fetus. If he strikes the belly of his wife and she aborts his son dead, then the ʿāqila of the father must pay a ghurrah, and he does not inherit from it.' And concerning 'any son of the striking man' i.e., his father.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage continues from the previous lesson by providing further scenarios of strikes on a pregnant woman. The first scenario: if the woman aborts a live fetus and it subsequently dies, full diyah is obligatory because it is a living human being destroyed. The second scenario: if the woman aborts a dead fetus and the mother also dies, both diyah for the mother and ghurrah for the fetus are due since they are two separate offenses. The commentator illustrates this with an analogy: if an arrow kills two persons, two diyahs are due. The principle is that the act is multiplied by the multiplicity of effects. A third scenario, where the mother dies first and then aborts a dead fetus, only the diyah for the mother is due; no ghurrah is required. The Hanafīs argue that her death is the apparent cause of the fetus's death, as its life depends on hers, so compensation is not established by doubt. The passage also discusses inheritance: the diyah and ghurrah are inherited by the heirs of the deceased, but the killer does not inherit. A specific case is given: a man strikes his own wife and she aborts his son dead; the ghurrah is on the ʿāqila of the father (the killer), but he does not inherit from that ghurrah because he is the killer directly.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money paid for wrongful death or injury; full diyah is 10,000 dirhams for a free man in Hanafī school.
غرة (ghurrah): Compensation for a dead fetus, set at one-twentieth of full diyah (500 dirhams) or the value of a male or female slave.
جناية (jināyah): An offense against life or limb; in this context, each homicide or fetal death is a separate jināyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, which of the following scenarios requires payment of both diyah and ghurrah?
A) A pregnant woman is struck and dies, then the fetus is aborted dead.
B) A pregnant woman is struck, aborts a dead fetus, and she survives.
C) A pregnant woman is struck, aborts a live child that later dies, and she survives.
D) A pregnant woman is struck and dies, then the fetus is aborted alive and dies.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes fetal death scenarios based on the timing of the mother's death: if she dies first, her death is the cause, and no separate ghurrah is obligated.

Compensation for a Slave Fetus: Hanafi Position and Disputes
Determines compensation for a miscarried slave fetus and disputes with Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a miscarried slave fetus, distinguish it from the Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf positions, and apply the valuation method correctly.

Core Idea
A slave fetus is compensated by its own market value, not the mother's value — it is a substitute for itself.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the compensation (diyah) for a miscarried fetus of a slave woman (amah). Unlike the fixed ghurrah for a free fetus, here the compensation is based on the fetus's market value. The Hanafi school's reasoning involves a key dispute with al-Shafi'i and an internal disagreement with Abu Yusuf. Understanding this ruling sharpens your ability to distinguish between different types of compensation in Islamic criminal law and appreciate how the Hanafi school reasons about property and substitution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is causing the miscarriage of a slave fetus. The ruling is that wajib compensation is paid by the striker from his own wealth to the slave's master immediately, because the 'aqila do not bear responsibility for slaves.
2
Locate the Hanafi position
The fetus is valued as if alive on the day of separation. If male, half a tenth (1/20) of that value is due; if female, one tenth (1/10). If sex is unknown, nothing is due.
This is based on the principle that a slave's diyah is his market value.
3
Examine the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the fetus is a part of the mother, so compensation should be one tenth of the mother's value regardless of sex, by analogy with compensation for parts.
This is the opposing school's dalil.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: compensation for a limb is only due when deficiency appears, which does not apply to the fetus. The fetus is a substitute for itself (badal nafsihi), so it is valued independently.
This rebuttal is based on the lack of apparent deficiency for the fetus.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi variant
Abu Yusuf holds that only the deficiency in the mother's value due to the miscarriage should be paid, analogizing to animals. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) reject this, and the mufta bihi is the value-based position.
The text sides with the majority; Abu Yusuf's view is not adopted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي جنين الأمة إلخ وما يجب من المال في جنين الأمة فهو من مال الضارب يأخذه مولاها من الضارب من ساعته وإنما كان في مال الضارب؛ لأن العاقلة لا تعقل العبيد والإماء، وقيد بالأمة؛ لأن جنين أم الولد يجب فيه ما يجب في جنين الحرة. نصف عشر قيمته إلخ: بيان هذا أنه يقوم الجنين بعد انفصاله ميتا على لونه وهيئته لو كان حيا، فينظر كم قيمته بهذا المكان، فبعد هذا إن كان ذكرا يجب نصف عشر قيمته وإن كان أنثى يجب عشر قيمته؛ لما تقرر أن دية الرقيق قيمته، ولا يلزم زيادة الأنثى لزيادة قيمة الذكر غالبا، وفيه إشارة إلى أنه إذا لم يمكن الوقوف على كونه ذكرا أو أنثى، فلا شيء عليه، وقال الشافعي تجب عشر قيمة الأم ذكرا كان أو أنثى؛ لأنه جزء من وجه، وضمان الأجزاء يؤخذ مقدارها من الأصل، ولنا أنه بدل نفسه؛ لأن ضمان الطرف لا يجب إلا عند ظهور النقصان وهو غير معتبر في ضمان الجنين فكان بدل نفسه، فيقدر بها، وعن أبي يوسف أنه يجب ضمان نقصان الأم إن انتقصت بذلك اعتبارا بجنين البهائم؛ فإن في جنين البهيمة يجب ما نقصت الأم، وإن لم تنقص لا يجب فيه شيء بالاتفاق، وهذا المذكور في جنين الأمة إذا لم يكن حملها من مولاها ولا من المغرور؛ لأن الحمل من حر، فتجب الغرة ذكرا كان أو أنثى. (فتح، ملا مسكين وغيرهما) ففيه قيمته حيا أي قيمة الجنين حال كونه حيا، ولا تجب الدية، وإن مات بعد العتق؛ لأنه قتله بالضرب السابق، وقد كان في حالة الرق، قال العلامة نوح آفندي وبالجملة هاهنا حالتان حالة الضرب وحالة التحرير، فبالنظر إلى حالة الضرب تجب قيمة الجنين على الضارب وتكون للمولى قطعا؛ لأنه كان رقيقا في تلك الحالة،
Concerning 'the fetus of a female slave, etc.': What is due of wealth for the fetus of a female slave is from the wealth of the striker; her master takes it from the striker immediately. It is from the wealth of the striker because the ʿāqila do not take responsibility for slaves. It is restricted to a female slave because the fetus of an umm walad incurs what is incurred for a free woman's fetus. 'Half a tenth of its value, etc.': Explanation: The fetus is valued after separation dead according to its color and form as if it were alive, then consider what its value is in that place. After that, if it is male, half a tenth of its value is due; if female, a tenth of its value is due, as established that the diyah of a slave is his value. There is no necessary increase for a female due to the usually higher value of a male. It is indicated that if it is impossible to determine whether it is male or female, nothing is due. Al-Shāfiʿī said: one tenth of the mother's value is due, male or female, because it is a part in a way, and compensation for parts is taken from the original. Our proof: it is a substitute for itself, because compensation for a limb is not due except upon appearance of deficiency, and that is not considered in compensation for the fetus, so it is a substitute for itself, and thus it is valued. From Abū Yūsuf: compensation for the deficiency in the mother is due if she is thereby reduced, by analogy with the fetus of animals. For the fetus of an animal, what the mother has decreased is due; if she does not decrease, nothing is due by agreement. This mentioned ruling for the fetus of a slave woman applies if her pregnancy is not from her master nor from a deceived person (maghrūr), because if the pregnancy is from a free man, then the ghurrah is due, male or female. (Fatḥ, Mullā Miskīn and others) 'Fihi qīmatuhu ḥayyan' i.e., its value as if alive, and diyah is not due even if it dies after emancipation, because he killed it by the previous strike and it was in a state of slavery. Shaykh Nūḥ Afandī said: In summary, here are two states: the state of striking and the state of emancipation. With respect to the state of striking, the value of the fetus is due from the striker and goes to the master definitively because it was a slave at that time.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage addresses the compensation for a miscarried fetus of a slave woman (amah). Unlike a free woman's fetus where a fixed ghurrah is due, for a slave fetus the compensation is based on its market value. The amount is half a tenth of that value if the fetus is male, and one tenth if female. This is because the diyah of a slave is his value. If the sex cannot be determined, nothing is due. Al-Shāfiʿī argued that the compensation should be one tenth of the mother's value, analogizing to compensation for parts. The Hanafī response is that the fetus is a substitute for itself, not a part of the mother, so its own value is used. Abū Yūsuf held an alternative view: only the deficiency in the mother's value due to the miscarriage should be paid, akin to a pregnant animal; if no deficiency occurs, nothing is due. The passage adds that if the fetus is from a free man (not the master or a maghrūr), the ghurrah of a free fetus applies. Additionally, if the slave owner frees the fetus after the strike but before death, and then the fetus dies from the earlier injury, the compensation remains its value as a slave at the time of the strike; full diyah does not apply because it was a slave at injury.

Key Terms
أمة (amah): A female slave. In diyat, her fetus is compensated based on the fetus's value, not a fixed ghurrah.
قيمة (qīmah): Market value of the slave at the time of death as an assessment for compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafī school, what is the compensation for a male slave fetus?
A) Half a tenth of the mother's value
B) Half a tenth of the fetus's own value
C) One tenth of the mother's value
D) A fixed ghurrah of 500 dirhams

Key Takeaway
A slave fetus is compensated by its own market value — half a tenth for a male, one tenth for a female — not by the mother's value.

Ghurra and Diyat for the Fetus: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on ghurra when mother dies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that only one diya is due when a pregnant woman dies from a blow and the fetus is found dead, and distinguish this from the Shafi'i position requiring ghurra in addition.

Core Idea
When mother dies, fetus's death is doubtful; only diya for mother is wajib.

The compensation for fetal death (ghurra) is a well-established ruling, but its application depends on the circumstances. This lesson addresses a key dispute: when the mother dies from the same blow and the fetus is found dead, do we pay one or two compensations? The Hanafi school insists on doubt and limits payment to one diya, while Imam al-Shafi'i argues for two. By examining the underlying reasoning, you will learn how Hanafi usul principles of certainty (yaqin) and doubt (shakk) shape fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and parties
Note the scenario: a man strikes his pregnant wife, causing her death and the death of the fetus. Identify who is liable (the striker's 'aqila) and for what (diyat).
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that only diya for the mother is due, and no ghurra for the fetus. Why? Because the mother's death is the apparent cause of the fetal death, creating uncertainty. The fetus's life depends on hers, so it is not clearly the blow that killed it.
The key principle: 'No obligation by doubt' (لا يجب بالشك).
3
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that both ghurra and diya are due. He analogizes to the case where the mother survives and the fetus is found dead – there, ghurra is due without dispute. Since the blow is the common cause, he argues the same applies here.
Shafi'i uses qiyas based on the apparent causation.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafi scholars rebut by distinguishing the two scenarios. When the mother survives, the blow is the direct cause. When she dies, her death intervenes, making the causation indirect. The hadith text (about ghurra) applies to the case where the mother lives, not where she dies.
The phrase 'ليس في معنى ما ورد به النص' indicates that the case is not analogous to the revealed text.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Shafi'i, the heirs receive two payments (diya for mother + ghurra for fetus); under Hanafi, they receive only one (diya for mother). This affects the total compensation.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position due to the principle that obligations are not imposed based on doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

أي ابن الرجل الضارب أي أبوه جنين الأمة لو ذكرا نصف عشر قيمته لو كان حيا، وعشر قيمته لو أنثى، فإن الرقيق أي لو كان الجنين ذكراً الجنين الجنين حرره سیده بعد ضربه فألقته فمات، ففيه قيمته حيا .. الجنين ضرب رجل بطن أمته الجنين كان فدية فقط وقال الشافعي تجب الغرة مع الدية؛ لأن الجنين مات بضربته ظاهرا كما إذا ألقته ميتا وهي بالحياة، ولنا: أن موت الأم سبب لموته ظاهرا؛ لأن حياته بحياتها، وتنفسه بتنفسها، فيتحقق بموتها، فلا يكون في معنى ما ورد به النص؛ إذ الاحتمال فيه أقل، فلا يجب شيء بالشك، وإن ألقته حيا بعد ما ماتت ثم مات، تجب ديتان: دية الأم، ودية الولد؛ لأنه كما إذا ألقته حيا وماتت تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٥٤/٩] يورث عنه إلخ : وإنما يورث؛ لأنه نفس من وجه والغرة بدله فيرثها ،وارثه ولا يرث الوارث من الغرة شيئا؛ لأنه قاتل مباشرة ،ظلما، ولا ميراث للقاتل بهذه الصفة تكملة البحر الرائق فلو ضرب: تفريع على قوله: "ولا يرث". منها: أي من غرة هذا الجنين. وفي جنين الأمة إلخ وما يجب من المال في جنين الأمة فهو من مال الضارب يأخذه مولاها من الضارب من ساعته وإنما كان في مال الضارب؛ لأن العاقلة لا تعقل العبيد والإماء، وقيد بالأمة؛ لأن جنين أم الولد يجب فيه ما يجب في جنين الحرة. نصف عشر قيمته إلخ: بيان هذا أنه يقوم الجنين بعد انفصاله ميتا على لونه وهيئته لو كان حيا، فينظر كم قيمته بهذا المكان، فبعد هذا إن كان ذكرا يجب نصف عشر قيمته وإن كان أنثى يجب عشر قيمته؛ لما تقرر أن دية الرقيق قيمته، ولا يلزم زيادة الأنثى لزيادة قيمة الذكر غالبا، وفيه إشارة إلى أنه إذا لم يمكن الوقوف على كونه ذكرا أو أنثى، فلا شيء عليه، وقال الشافعي تجب عشر قيمة الأم ذكرا كان أو أنثى؛ لأنه جزء من وجه، وضمان الأجزاء يؤخذ مقدارها من الأصل، ولنا أنه بدل نفسه؛ لأن ضمان الطرف لا يجب إلا عند ظهور النقصان وهو غير معتبر في ضمان الجنين فكان بدل نفسه، فيقدر بها، وعن أبي يوسف أنه يجب ضمان نقصان الأم إن انتقصت بذلك اعتبارا بجنين البهائم؛ فإن في جنين البهيمة يجب ما نقصت الأم، وإن لم تنقص لا يجب فيه شيء بالاتفاق، وهذا المذكور في جنين الأمة إذا لم يكن حملها من مولاها ولا من المغرور؛ لأن الحمل من حر، فتجب الغرة ذكرا كان أو أنثى.
Rulings on the fetus: If she dies and then miscarries a dead fetus, only diya (for the mother) is due, and what is obligatory upon him (the fetus) is inherited from him, and the striker does not inherit. Regarding the mother, concerning the fetus: ghurra and diya from the fetus. So if a man strikes his wife's belly and she miscarries his son dead, the father's 'aqila must pay a ghurra, and he does not inherit from it. And regarding the son of the striker, i.e., his father, the fetus of a slave woman: if male, half a tenth of his value if he were alive; if female, a tenth of her value. For the slave, i.e., if the fetus is male. The fetus, the fetus: if her master frees it after striking it and she miscarries it dead, then its value when alive is due. The fetus, a man struck the belly of his slave woman, the fetus, it was only diya. Al-Shafi'i said: The ghurra is obligatory along with the diya because the fetus clearly died from his strike, just as if she miscarried it dead while she was alive. Our proof: The mother's death is an apparent cause of its death because its life is through her life and its breathing through her breathing, so it occurs by her death. Therefore, it is not analogous to what the text (of hadith) covered, since the possibility (of other causes) is less, so nothing is obligatory due to doubt. And if she miscarried it alive after she died and then it died, two diyas are obligatory: diya of the mother and diya of the child, because it is as if she miscarried it alive and she died. (From completion of al-Bahr al-Raiq: 9/154) "Yurathu 'anhu" etc.: It is inherited because it is a soul in some sense, and the ghurra is its substitute, so its heir inherits it. The heir does not inherit anything from the ghurra because he is a direct killer unlawfully, and there is no inheritance for a killer with this description. (From completion of al-Bahr al-Raiq) "Falaw daraba": a branch on his saying "and he does not inherit." "Minha": i.e., from the ghurra of this fetus. "Wa fi janin al-amah" etc.: What is obligatory of wealth for the fetus of a slave woman is from the wealth of the striker, taken by her owner from him immediately. It is from the striker's wealth because the 'aqila does not take responsibility for slaves and slave women. It is restricted to the slave woman because for the fetus of an umm walad, what is obligatory for the fetus of a free woman is obligatory. "Nisf 'ushr qimatihi" etc.: Explanation: The fetus is valued after separation dead according to its color and form if it were alive, and it is seen how much its value is in this place. Then, if it is male, half a tenth of its value is obligatory; if female, a tenth of its value is obligatory, because it is established that the diya of a slave is his value, and the female is not necessarily more due to the male's value usually being higher. It indicates that if it cannot be determined whether it is male or female, nothing is obligatory. Al-Shafi'i said: A tenth of the mother's value is obligatory whether male or female because it is a part in a sense, and compensation for parts is taken from the original. Our proof: It is a substitute for itself because compensation for a limb is only obligatory when loss appears, and that is not considered in compensation for the fetus, so it is a substitute for itself, and thus estimated by it. From Abu Yusuf: The compensation for the mother's loss is obligatory if she is diminished by that, by analogy with the fetus of animals; for the fetus of an animal, what the mother lost is obligatory, and if she is not diminished, nothing is obligatory by consensus. This mentioned (ruling) for the fetus of a slave woman when her pregnancy is not from her master nor from one deceived (mexican marriage), because the pregnancy is from a free man, so the ghurra is obligatory whether male or female.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage begins with rulings on the fetus (janin) in diyat. It first addresses the case where a pregnant woman dies and then miscarries a dead fetus: only the diya for the mother is due, and the fetus's blood money (ghurra) is inherited from it, but the striker does not inherit. The text then gives the classic example: a man strikes his wife's belly, she miscarries a dead son—the father's 'aqila (tribal guarantors) must pay a ghurra (100 camels or equivalent), and the father does not inherit from it because he is the killer. For the fetus of a slave woman, the ruling differs: if male, half a tenth of its value if alive; if female, a tenth. This is because the diya of a slave is his market value. The text includes a detailed dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i. He argues that when the mother dies and the fetus is found dead, both ghurra and diya are due because the death appears caused by the blow. The Hanafis respond that the mother's death is the apparent cause of the fetus's death, as its life depends on hers, so it is not clearly analogous to the hadith text where the mother survives. Therefore, due to doubt, nothing additional is owed. If the fetus is born alive after the mother's death and then dies, two full diyas are due—one for the mother and one for the child. The passage then explains valuation methodology for the slave fetus, including Abu Yusuf's opinion that compensation should be based on the loss to the mother, by analogy with animals. However, the relied-upon Hanafi position is that the fetus's own value is the basis, with gender distinctions. Finally, the text notes that this ruling for the slave woman's fetus applies only when the pregnancy is not from the master or a deceived person; if from a free man, the ghurra (like a free woman) is due.

Key Terms
غرة (ghurrah): A fixed compensation of five camels (or equivalent) for causing a miscarriage, paid by the 'aqila.
عاقلة ('aqilah): The tribal group or guarantors who pay diyat on behalf of a killer.
جنين (janin): An unborn child, a fetus, considered a human in some rulings once limbs are formed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man strikes his pregnant wife, she miscarries a dead fetus, and then she also dies from the injuries. What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) Both diya for the wife and ghurra for the fetus are due.
B) Only diya for the wife is due; no ghurra for the fetus.
C) Only ghurra for the fetus is due; no diya for the wife.
D) Neither diya nor ghurra is due.

Key Takeaway
When a pregnant woman dies from a blow and the fetus is found dead, the Hanafi school imposes only one diya (for the mother) based on the principle that doubt prevents additional obligation.

Valuing the Fetus: When the Blow Precedes Manumission
Ruling on fetus after striking then freeing the mother

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi Hanafi ruling for the compensation of a fetus when the mother is freed after being struck, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute and cross-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
The act of striking determines the status – a blow on a slave fetus yields its value, not diya.

A man strikes his pregnant slave woman; later he frees her, and she miscarries a dead fetus from the blow. What compensation is due? The answer turns on whether we look at the status at the time of the blow or at the time of death. Hanafis apply the principle 'consider the state of the launching, not the arrival.' This lesson unpacks the ruling and the internal debate within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two states
The passage distinguishes two temporal states: the moment of striking (when the fetus was a slave) and the moment of freeing (when the mother became free). The fetus dies after the freeing but from the earlier blow. The legal question: does the compensation follow the slave or free status?
2
Apply the Hanafi principle al-ramy la al-wusul
The author states that the controlling factor is the state of the 'launching' (the harmful act) not the 'arrival' (the death). Since the blow occurred while the fetus was a slave, its slavery status governs liability.
This principle prevents the status after the act from retroactively altering the original tort.
3
Derive the mufta bihi ruling
The majority view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) imposes the value of the fetus as a slave at the time it was alive – its market value, not a fixed diya. No diya is due because the killing effectively happened in slavery.
The value is assessed as if the fetus were alive at the moment of the blow.
4
Contrast Imam Muhammad's view
Imam Muhammad argues that manumission cuts off the progression (sirayah) of the injury. Therefore only the difference in the fetus's value before and after the blow is due – the depreciation caused by the injury, not the full value.
This is a minority view within the school; the mufta bihi follows the majority.
5
Note cross-madhhab disagreement
The passage mentions that according to the other three schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali), a full diya is due after manumission because the fetus died free. Some Hanafi narrations also convey this, but the relied upon position is the majority Hanafi view.
This highlights the practical difference: the same fact pattern leads to different amounts of compensation across schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ففيه قيمته حيا أي قيمة الجنين حال كونه حيا، ولا تجب الدية، وإن مات بعد العتق؛ لأنه قتله بالضرب السابق، وقد كان في حالة الرق، قال العلامة نوح آفندي وبالجملة هاهنا حالتان حالة الضرب وحالة التحرير، فبالنظر إلى حالة الضرب تجب قيمة الجنين على الضارب وتكون للمولى قطعا؛ لأنه كان رقيقا في تلك الحالة، وبالنظر إلى حالة التحرير تجب الدية على عاقلة الضارب وتكون لورثته؛ لأنه كان حرا في تلك الحالة، فاعتبرنا حالة الضرب لما مر من أن المعتبر حالة الرمي لا الوصول فقلنا: تجب القيمة وتكون للمولى كذا في "الفتح"، وقال في "رد المحتار" في توجيه المسألة لأنه قتله بالضرب السابق، وقد كان في حالة الرق، فلهذا تجب القيمة دون الدية، وتحب قيمته حيا؛ لأنه صار قاتلا إياه وهو حي، فنظرنا إلى حالتي السبب والتلف، يعني أو جبنا القيمة دون الدية اعتبارا لحالة الضرب وأوجبنا قيمته حيا لا مشكوكا في حياته باعتبار حالة التلف؛ إذ لو اعتبر حالة الضرب فقط، جاز أن لا يكون حيا، فلا تجب القيمة بل تجب الغرة انتهى قال العيني: قيل: هذا عندهما، وعند محمد: تحب قيمته ما بين كونه مضروبا إلى كونه غير مضروب؛ لأن الإعتاق قاطع للسراية، ولا تجب الدية، وإن مات بعد العتق عندنا، وعند الثلاثة تجب دية، وهو رواية عنا
In it is its value when alive, meaning the value of the fetus at the time it was alive, and the diya is not obligatory, even if it dies after manumission, because he killed it by the prior striking, and it was in a state of slavery. Al-Allamah Nuh Afandi said: In summary, here are two states: the state of striking and the state of freeing. With respect to the state of striking, the value of the fetus is obligatory upon the striker and goes to the owner (master) definitively, because it was a slave in that state. With respect to the state of freeing, the diya is obligatory upon the striker's 'aqila and goes to his heirs, because he was free in that state. We considered the state of striking based on what passed: the consideration is the state of the launching, not the arriving. So we said: the value is obligatory and goes to the master. This is in al-Fath. And in Radd al-Muhtar, in explanation of the issue: because he killed it by the prior striking, and it was in a state of slavery, so the value is obligatory without diya. And its value when alive is obligatory because he became its killer while it was alive. We looked at both states of cause and destruction: we imposed value without diya considering the state of striking, and we imposed its value when alive, not doubted in its life, considering the state of destruction; if we only considered the state of striking, it might not have been alive, so value would not be obligatory but rather the ghurra. End. Al-Ayni said: It is said that this is according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Muhammad, its value is imposed as the difference between its value when struck and when not struck, because manumission cuts off the progression. And diya is not obligatory even if it dies after manumission according to us. According to the three (other imams), diya is obligatory, and it is a narration from us (Hanafis).
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific scenario: a man strikes his slave woman's belly, then frees her, and she miscarries a dead fetus. The key issue is whether the compensation is the value of the fetus (as a slave) or diya (as a free person). The Hanafi ruling, as stated by Imam Nuh Afandi, distinguishes between two states: the time of striking (the fetus was a slave) and the time of freeing (the fetus was free but already dead). The principle applied is 'consideration is given to the state of the launching (al-ramy), not the arriving (al-wusul)'—meaning the time of the act (striking) determines the status. Thus, the value of the fetus as a slave is due, paid by the striker to the master. However, since the fetus died after being freed (even though from the blow), its value is assessed as if alive at the time of the blow. The text then reports a dispute within the Hanafi school: According to Imam Muhammad, the compensation should be the difference in value between the fetus before and after the blow (since manumission severs the progression of the injury). Others, including Abu Yusuf, agree with the first opinion. The text also notes that according to the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad? Actually 'the three' here likely refers to the three caliphs or other schools), diya would be obligatory, but the Hanafi view is that diya is not due because the killing effectively occurred while the fetus was still a slave.

Key Terms
تحرير (tahrir): Manumission, freeing a slave.
سراية (sirayah): The progression or extension of an injury causing death.
قيمة (qimah): Market value, used here as compensation for a slave property.
دية (diyah): Blood money, a fixed compensation for homicide or injury to a free person.
غرة (ghurrah): A fixed payment of one-twentieth of diya, due for miscarriage when the fetus is not known to be alive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi view, when a pregnant slave woman is struck, then freed, and the fetus dies from the blow, the striker must pay:
A) Diya of a free fetus, because the mother was free at death.
B) The value of the fetus as a slave at the time of the blow.
C) The difference in the fetus's value before and after the blow.
D) Ghurra (1/20 diya) because the fetus was property.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi tort law, the status of the victim at the time of the harmful act, not at death, determines the type of compensation – value for a slave, diya for a free person.

Kaffarah and Ghurra for Fetal Death: The Hanafi Position
Ruling on kaffarah for fetal death and woman's abortion liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kaffarah and ghurra for fetal death, and explain the distinction based on consent and certainty of life.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, kaffarah is not obligatory for fetal death due to uncertainty; instead, ghurra is due from the 'aqila if the woman acts without permission.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses two related questions: whether expiation (kaffarah) is due when a fetus dies due to someone's action, and whether a woman who aborts herself incurs liability. The Hanafi school distinguishes between these penalties based on the certainty of life and the presence of permission. Understanding this ruling is essential for correctly applying the law of diyat in cases of fetal death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage first states that there is no kaffarah for causing fetal death. Then it discusses a woman who self-aborts: kaffarah is not obligatory (wajib) but recommended (nadb), and ghurra is wajib on her 'aqila if she acts without permission.
Note the distinction: kaffarah = expiation, ghurra = financial compensation.
2
Locate the evidence
The passage cites 'the generality of what we narrated' (referring to a hadith or general principle) and an analogy (qiyas): a formed fetus (limbs apparent) is treated like a complete child in rulings of motherhood, 'iddah, and nifas, so likewise for ghurra and kaffarah.
The analogy is based on the fetus being considered a child (walad) in other legal contexts.
3
Distinguish the two penalties
Kaffarah is a religious expiation for killing a human life; it is not wajib because the life of the fetus is uncertain. Ghurra is a financial penalty for the loss of a potential life; it is wajib to compensate the father or heirs.
The Hanafi school holds that certainty of life is required for kaffarah, which is not present for a fetus.
4
Note the condition of consent
If the woman acts with her husband's permission, she is not considered a transgressor, so no ghurra is due. Without permission, she is liable, and her 'aqila must pay.
Consent indicates that the act is not a wrongful aggression.
5
Apply the general rule for formed fetus
A fetus whose limbs have become apparent (i.e., a formed fetus) is treated like a complete child for all these rulings, meaning the same rules for ghurra and kaffarah apply regardless of age.
Early-stage fetuses (before formation) may have different rules, not covered in this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا كفارة في الجنين، وإن شربت دواء لتطرحه، أو عالجت فرجها حتى أسقطته عندنا وجوبا بل ندبا المرأة ضمن عاقلتها الغرة إن فعلت بلا إذن. أي عاقلة المرأة فعلها المذكور الزوج فلو بإذنه فلا شيء عمدا المرأة الولد والجنين الذي استبان بعض خلقه بمنزلة التام في جميع هذه الأحكام؛ لإطلاق ما روينا، ولأنه ولد في حق أمومية الولد وانقضاء العدة والنفاس فكذا في حق هذا الحكم.
And there is no kaffarah (expiation) for the fetus. And if she (the woman) drinks a medicine to abort it, or treats her private part until she miscarries it, according to us (the Hanafis) it is not obligatory (wajib) but rather recommended (nadb). The woman's 'aqila guarantees the ghurra if she acts without permission. Meaning the 'aqila of the woman (if her husband is the one who did the mentioned act? Actually text unclear: 'ay 'aqilat al-mar'ah fi'laha al-madhkur al-zawj, fa-law bi-idhnihi fala shay' 'amdan al-mar'ah al-walad) The woman (is liable) for the child. And the fetus whose some of its limbs have become apparent is like the complete (fetus) in all these rulings due to the generality of what we have narrated, and because it is a child regarding motherhood of the child, completion of 'iddah, and postnatal bleeding, so likewise regarding this ruling.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This final passage covers two topics: (1) expiation (kaffarah) for causing fetal death, and (2) a woman's liability if she aborts herself. The Hanafi position is that kaffarah is not wajib (obligatory) for a miscarried dead fetus; it is only recommended (nadb). This is in contrast to Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds kaffarah wajib because it is killing (as noted in the text earlier). The Hanafi reasoning is that the killing is not certain (since the fetus may not have been alive). If the woman intentionally induces abortion by medicine or treatment without her husband's permission, her 'aqila must pay the ghurra (compensation for the fetus). However, if she acts with her husband's permission, she is not liable because she is not transgressing. The passage then states a general rule: a fetus whose limbs have become apparent (i.e., a formed fetus) is treated like a complete child in all these rulings (ghurra, kaffarah, etc.) because it is considered a child for rulings of motherhood, 'iddah, and nifas.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation, a penalty for certain sins, here specifically for killing a human.
ندب (nadb): Recommended, meaning the act is rewarded but not sinful to omit.
غرة (ghurra): Financial compensation for the loss of a fetus, typically half the diyah of the mother or a fixed amount.
عاقلة ('aqila): The group of male agnates (or a responsible party) who pay blood money on behalf of the offender.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman drinks a potion to abort her pregnancy without her husband's permission and succeeds. According to the Hanafi school, what is due?
A) Her 'aqila must pay a ghurra.
B) She alone must pay a ghurra.
C) Neither ghurra nor kaffarah is due.
D) Kaffarah is wajib on her.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, kaffarah is not required for fetal death due to uncertainty; instead, a financial penalty (ghurra) is imposed on the 'aqila if the woman acts without permission.

Rulings on the Fetus: No Kaffara, Only Ghurra
Explains Hanafi rulings on diya and kaffara for fetus and accidental killing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kaffara and ghurra for causing fetal death and distinguish when kaffara becomes wajib.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, causing a stillbirth does not require expiation (kaffara); only compensation (ghurra) is due.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a critical area of Hanafi tort law: the legal consequences of causing the death of a fetus. The text establishes a fundamental distinction between the fetus and a born child, limiting expiation to cases where the child is born alive. It also clarifies the liability for compensation (ghurra) and the role of the 'aqila, while contrasting the Hanafi position with that of other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Locate the statement 'ولا كفارة في الجنين' (no kaffara for the fetus). What is the act being ruled upon? It is causing the death of a fetus (through abortion or injury).
The ruling here concerns a fetus that is stillborn.
2
Determine the Hukm Level of Kaffara
The text says 'عندنا وجوبا بل ندبا' - meaning according to us (Hanafis) it is not obligatory (wajib) but rather recommended (mandub). Identify the precise hukm level.
Kaffara is not wajib; it is only mandub (recommended) for stillbirth.
3
Identify the Condition that Triggers Kaffara
The text states: 'وإن وقع حيا ثم مات، ففيه الكفارة'. Find this condition. When does kaffara become wajib?
Only if the fetus is born alive and then dies.
4
Analyze Liability for Ghurra
The woman's 'aqila must pay ghurra if she acted without permission. Note the conditions: (a) the act was without husband's permission, (b) the fetus was stillborn. If with permission, no ghurra.
Ghurra is like compensation for destroying a potential life.
5
Note the Inter-Madhhab Dispute
The text mentions that Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali hold kaffara obligatory even for stillbirth. Note their evidence and the Hanafi response.
Dispute hinges on whether a fetus is considered a full human life before birth.

ولا كفارة في الجنين، وإن شربت دواء لتطرحه، أو عالجت فرجها حتى أسقطته عندنا وجوبا بل ندبا المرأة ضمن عاقلتها الغرة إن فعلت بلا إذن. = أي عاقلة المرأة فعلها المذكور الزوج فلو بإذنه فلا شيء عمدا المرأة الولد وبالنظر إلى حالة التحرير تجب الدية على عاقلة الضارب وتكون لورثته؛ لأنه كان حرا في تلك الحالة، فاعتبرنا حالة الضرب لما مر من أن المعتبر حالة الرمي لا الوصول فقلنا: تجب القيمة وتكون للمولى كذا في "الفتح"، وقال في "رد المحتار" في توجيه المسألة لأنه قتله بالضرب السابق، وقد كان في حالة الرق، فلهذا تجب القيمة دون الدية، وتجب قيمته حيا؛ لأنه صار قاتلا إياه وهو حي، فنظرنا إلى حالتي السبب والتلف، يعني أوجبنا القيمة دون الدية اعتبارا لحالة الضرب وأوجبنا قيمته حيا لا مشكوكا في حياته باعتبار حالة التلف؛ إذ لو اعتبر حالة الضرب فقط، جاز أن لا يكون حيا، فلا تجب القيمة بل تجب الغرة انتهى قال العيني: قيل: هذا عندهما، وعند محمد: تجب قيمته ما بين كونه مضروبا إلى كونه غير مضروب؛ لأن الإعتاق قاطع للسراية، ولا تجب الدية، وإن مات بعد العتق عندنا، وعند الثلاثة تجب دية، وهو رواية عنا رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٧/٢] ولا كفارة إلخ: أي وجوبا عندنا بل ندبا، وقال الشافعي: تجب عليه الكفارة؛ لأنه قاتل، وبه قال مالك وأحمد، ولنا أن القتل غير متحقق؛ الجواز أن لا حياة فيه هذا إذا وقع الجنين ميتا، وإن وقع حيا ثم مات، ففيه الكفارة. (عيني، طائي) ضمن عاقلتها إلخ لأنها أتلفته متعدية، فيجب عليها ضمانه وتتحمل عنها العاقلة، ولا ترث هي من الغرة شيئا؛ لأنها قاتلة بغير حق، بخلاف ما إذا فعلت ذلك بإذن الزوج حيث لا تجب الغرة؛ لعدم التعدي، وعند الثلاثة: ضمن عاقلتها الغرة مطلقا، وتجب الكفارة أيضا رمز الحقائق : ٤٤٧/٢] وقال في "الفتح": ضمن عاقلتها الغرة في سنة واحدة، وهذا إن ألقته ميتا وإن ألقته حيا ثم مات فعلى عاقلتها الدية في ثلث سنين إن كان لها عاقلة، وإلا ففي مالها، وعليها الكفارة والجنين الذي استبان بعض خلقه بمنزلة التام في جميع هذه الأحكام؛ لإطلاق ما روينا، ولأنه ولد في حق أمومية الولد وانقضاء العدة ،والنفاس فكذا في حق هذا الحكم.
There is no expiation (kaffara) for the fetus. And if a woman drinks medicine to abort it, or treats her vagina until she miscarries, according to us (Hanafis) it is not obligatory but rather recommended that the woman's 'aqila guarantee the ghurra if she did so without permission. That is, the 'aqila of the woman for her action mentioned, [if done by] the husband, then if with his permission there is nothing. 'Amdan al-mar'at al-walad? And with regard to the state of freedom, the diya is obligatory on the 'aqila of the striker and is for his heirs; because he was free in that state, so we considered the state of striking as per what has passed that the considered state is the state of throwing, not reaching. So we say: the value is obligatory and is for the master. Thus in al-Fath. And he said in Radd al-Muhtar in directing the issue: because he killed him by the prior striking, and he was in a state of slavery, therefore the value is obligatory without diya, and his value as living is obligatory because he became his killer while he was alive. So we looked at both states: cause and destruction; meaning we obligated the value without diya considering the state of striking, and we obligated his value as living, not doubted in his life, considering the state of destruction; for if we considered only the state of striking, it would be possible that he was not alive, so value would not be obligatory but rather ghurra. End. Al-'Ayni said: it is said this is according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Muhammad: his value is obligatory as between being struck and not being struck, because emancipation cuts off the progression, and diya is not obligatory if he dies after emancipation according to us, and according to the three (other schools) diya is obligatory, and it is a narration from us. The symbol of al-Haqa'iq: 2/447. 'And no kaffara' etc.: i.e., not obligatory according to us, but rather recommended. Al-Shafi'i said: kaffara is obligatory on him because he is a killer, and Malik and Ahmad also said. Our evidence: killing is not confirmed because it is possible there was no life. This is if the fetus falls dead; if it falls alive then dies, then there is kaffara. (al-'Ayni, al-Ta'i) 'The 'aqila guarantees the ghurra' etc. because she destroyed it transgressively, so guarantee is obligatory on her and the 'aqila bears it for her, and she does not inherit any of the ghurra because she is a killer without right. Unlike if she did so with the husband's permission, where ghurra is not obligatory due to lack of transgression. And according to the three (other schools): her 'aqila guarantees the ghurra absolutely, and kaffara is also obligatory. Symbol of al-Haqa'iq: 2/447. And said in al-Fath: her 'aqila guarantees the ghurra in one year. This if she aborts it dead; if she aborts it alive then it dies, then upon her 'aqila is the diya in three years if she has an 'aqila, otherwise from her wealth, and upon her is kaffara. And the fetus whose some limbs are manifest is like a complete one in all these rulings, due to the general import of what we narrated, and because it is a child with regard to motherhood, completion of 'idda, and postpartum period, so likewise with regard to this ruling.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq is a commentary that expands on the rulings concerning the fetus (janin). It begins by stating a key Hanafi principle: no expiation (kaffara) is due for causing the death of a fetus. The author then discusses the case of a woman who takes medicine or treats herself to abort. According to the Hanafi school, it is not obligatory but recommended that the woman's 'aqila (paternal relatives who pay blood money) pay a ghurra (compensation) if she acted without her husband's permission. If the husband authorized it, nothing is due. The text then shifts to a case of striking a slave who is later freed; the diya (full blood money) is on the striker's 'aqila and goes to the victim's heirs because at the time of the strike he was free (status of freedom is considered at the time of the act). The discussion includes an intra-madhhab difference: according to Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, the value is based on the difference between the slave's value before and after the strike, because emancipation cuts off the progression (saraya). The author then returns to the fetus, reiterating that kaffara is not obligatory in the Hanafi view, contrasting with Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali who hold it obligatory. The text explains the reasoning: the killing is not verified because there may have been no life. However, if the fetus is born alive and then dies, kaffara becomes wajib. The passage also details the liability for ghurra or diya depending on whether the fetus was born dead or alive, and the time periods for payment. Finally, it states that a fetus whose limbs have become discernible is treated as a complete human in these rulings, based on the general import of hadith and its recognized status for motherhood, 'idda, and postpartum period.

Key Terms
الجنين (al-janin): An unborn offspring in the womb; a fetus.
الغرة (al-ghurra): A fixed compensation (value of a male or female slave) paid for causing miscarriage or death of a fetus.
العاقلة (al-'aqila): The paternal male relatives who are liable to pay blood money (diya or ghurra) on behalf of the offender.
الكفارة (al-kaffara): An expiation required for certain sins, such as involuntary killing (freeing a slave, fasting, or feeding the poor).
الدية (al-diya): Full blood money payable for homicide or bodily harm.
المتعدي (al-muta'addi): One who acts without legal right, transgressing boundaries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on kaffara (expiation) for causing a stillbirth?
A) Kaffara is wajib (obligatory).
B) Kaffara is mandub (recommended) but not wajib.
C) Kaffara is haram.
D) Kaffara is wajib only if the mother aborted intentionally.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, causing a stillbirth does not require expiation; only the ghurra compensation is due, and the matter differs among schools.
